COMMITTEE AMENDMENT ·I~" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 11. Parent barred from inheriting though child. A parent is barred from inheriting 
2 through intestate succession from or through a child of the parent if: 
3 A. The parent's parental rights were terminated and the parent-child relationship was 
4 not judicially reestablished; or 
5 B. The child died before reaching 18 years of age and there is clear and convincing 
6 evidence that immediately before the child's death the parental rights of the parent 
7 could have been tenninated under the laws of this State other than Articles 1 to 8 on 
8 the basis of nonsupport, abandonment, abuse. neglect or other actions or inactions of 
9 the parent toward the child.1 
10 Amend the bill in Part A in section 2 in Article 2 by striking out all of subpart 2 and 
11 inserting the following: 
12 'SUBPART 2 
13 PARENT-CHILD RELATIONSIDP 
14 §2-115. Determination of parentage for purposes of intestate succession 
15 Unless otherwise provided in this subpart. 11parent11 for purposes of intestate 
16 succession means a person who has established a parent-child relationship with the child 
17 under Alticle 9 or Title 19-A, chapter 61 and whose parental rights have not been 
18 terminated. 
19 §2-116. Effect of a pending petition 
20 If a petition to establish parentage under Title 19-A, chapter 61 or a petition for 
21 adoption under Alticle 9 is pending and has not been finally adjudicated at the time of the 
22 petitioner1s death, the subject of the petition is considered a child of the petitioner for 
23 intestate succession purposes and may inherit from and through the petitioner. If the 
24 subject of the petition dies before a final adjudication of parentage is issued, the petitioner 
25 may inherit from or through the subject of the petition only if there is a final adjudication 
26 of parentage. 
27 §2-117. Effect of an order granting adoption on adoptee and adoptee's former 
28 parents 
29 An order granting an adoption divests the adoptee1s fom1er parents of all legal rights, 
30 powers, privileges, immunities, duties and obligations concerning the adoptee. including 
31 the right to inherit from or through the adoptee. An adoptee, however, may inherit from 
32 the adoptee1s former parents if so provided in the adoption decree. 
33 §2-118. Child born after death of parent 
34 An individual is a parent of a child who is born after the individual1s death. if the 
35 child is: 
36 1. In utero. In utero not later than 36 months after the individual1s death; or 
37 2. Born. Born not later than 45 months after the individual's death.1

3 '2. Valuation. The value of property is determined as follows. 
4 A. The value of property included in the augmented estate under section 2-205,

21 Amend the bill in Part A in section 2 by striking out all of §2-403 (page 49, lines 27 
22 to 39 and page 50, lines 1 to 3 in L.D.) and inserting the following: 
23 '§2-403. Exempt property 
24 In addition to the homestead allowance, the decedent's surviving spouse is entitled 
25 from the estate to a value. not exceeding $15,000 in excess of any security interests in the 
26 estate of tangible personal property, including, but not limited to, in household furniture, 
27 automobiles, furnishings, appliances and personal effects. If there is no surviving spouse, 
28 children of the decedent are entitled jointly to the same value; however, the decedent, by 
29 will, may exclude one or more adult children from the receipt of exempt property. If 
30 encumbered chattels are selected and the value in excess of security interests, plus that of 
31 other exempt property, is less than $15,000, or if there is not $15,000 w01th of exempt 
32 property in the estate, the spouse or children are entitled to other assets of the estate, if 
33 any, to the extent necessary to make up the $15,000 value. Rights to exempt property and 
34 assets needed to make up a deficiency of exempt property have priority over all claims 
35 against the estate, except that the right to any assets to make up a deficiency of exempt 
36 property abates as necessary to permit earlier payment of homestead allowance and 
37 family allowance. These rights are in addition to any benefit or share passing to the 
38 surviving spouse or children by the decedent's will unless otherwise provided by intestate 
39 succession or by way of elective share.'

1 Amend the bill in Part A in section 2 by striking out all of §2-705 (page 71, lines 1 to 
2 3 8 and page 72, lines 1 to 18 in L.D.) and inserting the following: 
3 '§2-705. Class gifts construed to accord with intestate succession; exceptions 
4 1. Definitions. As used in this section, unless the context othe1wise indicates, the 
5 following terms have the following meanings. 
6 A. "Distribution date" means the date when an immediate or postponed class gift 
7 takes effect in possession or enjoyment. 
8 B. "Relative" means a grandparent or the descendant of a grandparent. 
9 2. Terms of relationship. A class gift that uses a term ofrelationship to identify the 
10 class members includes in the class a child of parents regardless of their martial status, 
11 and their respective descendants if appropriate to the class, in accordance with the rules 
12 for intestate succession regarding parent-child relationships. 
13 3. Relatives by marriage. Terms of relationship in a governing instrument that do 
14 not differentiate relationships by parentage, including relatives of parents, from those by 
15 marriage, such as uncles, aunts, nieces or nephews, are construed to exclude relatives by 
16 marriage, unless: 
17 A. When the governing instrument was executed, the class was then and foreseeably 
18 . would be empty; or 
19 B. The language or circumstances otherwise establish that relatives by marriage were 
20 intended to be included. 
21 4. Relatives of shared parentage. Terms of relationship in a governing instrument 
22 that do not differentiate relationships by whether all parents are shared, such as brothers, 
23 sisters, nieces or nephews, are construed to include all types of relationships regardless of 
24 whether relatives share all parents. 
25 5. Transferor not parent. In construing a dispositive provision of a transferor who 
26 is not the parent, the transferor or a relative of the transferor must have established a 
27 parent-child relationship with the child before the child reached 18 years of age. 
28 6. Class-closing rules. The following provisions apply for purposes of the class-
29 closing rules. 
30 A. A child in utero at a particular time is treated as living at that time if the child 
31 lives 120 hours after birth. 
32 B. If the distribution date is the date of the deceased parent's death, a child in utero 
33 not later than 36 months after the deceased parent's death or born not later than 45 
34 months after the deceased parent's death is treated as living at that time if the child 
35 lives 120 hours after birth. 
36 C. An individual who is in the process of being adopted when the class closes is 
3 7 treated as a child of the parent when the class closes if the adoption is subsequently 
38 granted.'

7 '§3-604. Bond amount; security; procedure; reduction 
8 If bond is required and the provisions of the will or order do not specify the amount, 
9 unless stated in the application or petition, the person qualifying shall file a statement 
1 O under oath with the register indicating that person's best estimate of the value of the 
11 personal estate of the decedent and of the income expected from the personal and real 
12 estate during the next year, and that person shall execute and file a bond with the register, 
13 or give other suitable security, in an amount not less than the estimate. The register shall 
14 determine that the bond is duly executed by a corporate surety, or one or more individual 
15 sureties whose performance is secured by pledge of personal property, mortgage on real 
16 property or other adequate security. The register may permit the amount of the bond to 
17 be reduced by the value of assets of the estate deposited with a domestic financial 
18 institution, as defmed in section 6-201, subsection 4, in a manner that prevents their 
19 unauthorized disposition. On petition of the personal representative or another interested 
20 person the court may excuse a requirement of bond, increase or reduce the amount of the 
21 bond, release sureties or permit the substitution of another bond with the same or 
22 different sureties.'

1 '§3-711. Powers of personal representatives; in general 
2 Until termination of the personal representative's appointment, a personal 
3 representative has the same power over the title to property of the estate that an absolute 
4 owner would have, in trust however, for the benefit of the creditors and others interested 
5 in the estate. This power may be exercised without notice, hearing or order of court, 
6 except as limited by this section. The personal representative may not sell or transfer any 
7 interest in real property of the estate without giving notice at least 10 days prior to that 
8 sale or transfer to any person succeeding to an interest in that property, unless the 
9 personal representative is authorized under the will to sell or transfer real estate without 
10 this notice.'

19 Amend the bill in Part A in section 2 by striking out all of Article 5 and inserting the 
20 following: 
21 'ARTICLE 5 
22 UNIFORM GUARDIANSHIP AND PROTECTIVE PROCEEDINGS 
23 PART 1 
24 GENERAL PROVISIONS 
25 §5-101. Short title 
26 Parts 1, 2, 3, 4 and 5 of this Article may be known and cited as "the Uniform 
27 Guardianship and Protective Proceedings Act." 
28 §5-102. Definitions 
29 As used in this Article, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following terms 
30 have the following meanings. 
31 1. Adult. "Adult" means an individual at least 18 years of age or an emancipated 
32 individual under 18 years of age. 
33 2. Adult subject to conservatorship. "Adult subject to conservatorship" means an 
34 adult for whom a conservator has been appointed under this Act. 
35 3. Adult subject to guardianship. "Adult subject to guardianship" means an adult 
36 for whom a guardian has been appointed under this Act. 
Page 7 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 4. Best interest of the minor. "Best interest of the minor" means the standard of the 
2 best interest of the child according to the factors set forth in Title 19-A, section 1653, 
3 subsection 3. 
4 5. Claim. "Claim" includes a claim against an individual or conservatorship estate, 
5 whether arising in contract, tort or otherwise. 
6 6. Conse1·vator. "Conservator" means a person appointed by a court to make 
7 decisions with respect to the property or financial affairs of an individual subiect to 
8 conservatorship. "Conservator" includes a coconservator. 
9 7. Conservatorship estate. "Conservatorship estate" means the property subject to 
10 conservatorship under this Act. 
11 8. Full conse1·vatorship. "Full conservatorship" means a conservatorship that grants 
12 the conservator all powers available under this Act. 
13 9. Full guardianship. "Full guardianship" means a guardianship that grants the 
14 guardian all powers available under this Act. 
15 10. Guardian. "Guardian" means a person appointed by a court to make decisions 
16 with respect to the personal affairs of an individual. "Guardian" includes a coguardian 
17 but does not include a guardian ad litem. 
18 11. Guardian ad litem. "Guardian ad litem" means a person appointed to inform 
19 the court about, and to represent, the needs and best interest of an individual. 
20 12. Individual subject to conservatorship. "Individual subject to conservatorship" 
21 means an adult or minor for whom a conservator has been appointed. 
22 13. Individual subject to guardianship. "Individual subject to guardianship" 
23 means an adult or minor for whom a guardian has been appointed. 
24 14. Less restrictive alternative. "Less restrictive alternative" means an approach to 
25 meeting an individual's needs that restricts fewer rights than would the appointment of a 
26 guardian or conservator. "Less restrictive alternative" includes supported decision 
27 maldng, appropriate technological assistance, appointment of an agent by the individual, 
28 including appointment under a power of attorney for health care or power of attorney for 
29 finances, or appointment of a representative payee. 
30 15. Letters of office. "Letters of office'' means judicial certification of guardianship 
31 or conservatorship. 
32 16. Limited conservatorship. "Limited conservatorship" means a conservatorship 
33 that grants the conservator less than all powers available under this Act, grants powers 
34 over only certain property or otherwise restricts the powers of the conservator. 
35 17. Limited guardianship. "Limited guardianship" means a guardianship that 
36 grants the guardian less than all powers available under this Act or otherwise restricts the 
37 powers of the guardian. 
38 18. Minor. "Minor" means an unemancipated individual who is under 18 years of 
39 age.

19. Minor subject to conservatorship. "Minor subject to conservatorship11 means a 
minor for whom a conservator has been appointed under this Act. 
20. Minor subject to guardianship. "Minor subject to guardianship" means a 
minor for whom a guardian has been appointed under this Act. 
21. Parent. 11Parent11 means a person who has established a parent-child relationship 
with the child under Title 19-A, chapter 61 and whose parental rights have not been 
terminated. 
22. Person. 11Person11 means an individual, estate, business or nonprofit entity, 
public corporation, government or governmental subdivision, agency or instrumentality 
or other legal entity. 
23. Property. 11Property11 means anything that may be the subject of ownership and 
includes both real and personal property, tangible and intangible, or any interest therein. 
24. Protective arrangement instead of conservatorship. "Protective arrangement 
instead of conservatorship11 means a court order entered under section 5-503.

instead of guardianship" means a court order entered under section 5-502. 
26. Protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship. 
"Protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship" means a court order 
entered under Part 5, including an order authorizing a single transaction or more than one 
related transaction. 
27. Record. "Record," used as a noun, means information that is inscribed on a 
tangible medium or that is stored in an electronic or other medium and is retrievable in 
perceivable form. 
28. Respondent. 11Respondent11 means an individual for whom appointment of a 
guardian or conservator or a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or 
conservatorship is sought. 
29. Sign. "Sign" means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record: 
A. To execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or 
B. To attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic symbol, sound or 
process. 
30. State. "State" means a state of the United States, the District of Columbia. the 
Commonwealth of Puerto Rico, the United States Virgin Islands or any territory or 
insular possession subject to the jurisdiction of the United States. 11State11 includes an 
Indian tribe or band recognized by federal law or formally acknowledged by a state. 
31. Suitable. "Suitable," with respect to a guardian for a minor, means that the 
guardian can provide a safe and appropriate residence for the minor, understands and is 
prepared to follow the terms of the appointment and understands and can address the 
minor's needs and protect the minor from harm. 
32. Supported decision maldng. "Supported decision making" means assistance 
from one or more persons of an individual's choosing:

A. In understanding the nature and consequences of potential personal and financial

§5-103. Facility of transfer 
1. Transfer of money or personal property to minor. Unless a person required to 
transfer money or personal property to a minor knows that a conservator has been 
appointed or that a proceeding for appointment of a conservator of the estate of the minor 
is pending, the person may do so, as to an amount or value not exceeding $10,000 a year, 
by transferring it to: 
A. A person who has the care and custody of the minor and with whom the minor 
resides; 
B. A guardian of the minor; 
C. A custodian under the Maine Uniform Transfers to Minors Act; 
D. A financial institution as a deposit in an interest-bearing account or certificate in 
the sole name of the minor and giving notice of the deposit to the minor; or 
E. The minor, if married or emancipated. 
2. Responsibility for proper application. A person who transfers money or 
property in compliance with this section is not responsible for its proper application. 
3. For benefit of minor; no personal financial benefit. A guardian or other person 
who receives money or property for a minor under subsection 1, paragraph A or B may 
apply it only to the support, care, education, health and welfare of the minor and may not 
derive a personal financial benefit, but may be reimbursed for necessary expenses for the 
benefit of the minor. Any excess must be preserved for the future support, care, 
education, health and welfare of the minor, and any balance must be transferred to the 
minor when the minor becomes an adult or is othe1wise emancipated. 
§5-104. Subject matter jurisdiction 
1. Jurisdiction; minors. Except to the extent that jurisdiction is precluded by the 
Unifo1m Child Custody Jurisdiction and Enforcement Act and Title 4, section 152, 
subsection 5-A, the comt has jurisdiction over a guardianship for a minor domiciled or 
present in this State. The court has jurisdiction over a conservatorship or protective 
arrangement instead of conservatorship for a minor domiciled in or having property 
located in this State. 
2. Jurisdiction; adults. The court has jurisdiction over a guardianship, a 
conservatorship and an order for a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or 
conservatorship for an adult as provided in the Uniform Adult Guardianship and 
Protective Proceedings Jurisdiction Act, Part 6. 
3. Exclusive or concurrent jurisdiction. After service of notice in a proceeding 
seeldng a guardianship, conservatorship or protective arrangement instead of 
Page 10 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEEAMENDMENT"A"toH.P. 91,L.D.123 
C>1 , guardianship or conservatorship and until termination of the proceeding, the court in 
2 which the petition is filed has: 
3 A. Exclusive jurisdiction to determine the need for a guardianship, conservatorship 
4 or protective arrangement; 
5 B. Exclusive jurisdiction to dete1mine how property of the respondent that is subject 
6 to the law of this State must be managed, expended or distributed to or for the use of 
7 the respondent, an individual who is dependent in fact on the respondent or other 
8 claimant; 
9 C. Concurrent jurisdiction to determine the validity of a claim against the respondent 
10 or property of the respondent or a question of title concerning the property; and 
11 D. If a guardian or conservator is appointed, exclusive jurisdiction over issues related 
12 to administration of the guardianship or conservatorship. 
13 4. Exclusive and continuing jurisdiction. A court that appoints a guardian or 
14 conservator, or authorizes a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or 
15 conservatorship, has exclusive and continuing jurisdiction over the proceeding until the 
16 court terminates the proceeding or the appointment or protective arrangement expires by 
17 its terms. 
18 §5-105. Transfer of proceeding 
19 1. Guardianship or conservatorship subject to transfer provisions. This section 
20 does not apply to a guardianship or conservatorship for an adult that is subject to the 
21 transfer provisions of Part 6, subpart 3. 
22 2. Tran sf er if serves best interest of individual. After the appointment of a 
23 guardian or conservator, the court that made the appointment may transfer the proceeding 
24 to a court in another county in this State or to another state if transfer will serve the best 
25 interest of the individual subject to the guardianship or conservatorship. 
26 3. Proceeding pending in another state or foreign country. If a proceeding for a 
27 guardianship or conservatorship is pending in another state or a foreign country and a 
28 petition for guardianship or conservatorship is filed in a court in this State, the court shall 
29 · notify the court in the other state or foreign country and, after consultation with that 
30 court, assume or decline jurisdiction, whichever is in the best interest of the respondent. 
31 4. Petition for appointment in this State. A guardian or conservator appointed in 
32 another state or country may petition the court for appointment as a guardian or 
33 conservator in this State if jurisdiction in this State is or will be established. The 
34 appointment may be made on proof of appointment in the other state or foreign country 
35 and presentation of a certified copy of the part of the court record in the other state or 
36 country specified by the court in this State. 
37 5. Notice; appointment unless not in best interest of respondent. Notice of 
38 hearing on a petition under subsection 4, together with a copy of the petition, must be 
39 given to the respondent, if the respondent is 14 years of age or older at the time of the 
40 hearing, and to the persons that would be entitled to notice if the procedures for 
41 mmointment of a guardian or conservator under this Act were applicable. The court shall 
Page 11 -128LR0452(02)-1

2 in the best interest of the respondent. 
3 6. Copy of order of appointment. Not later than 14 days after appointment under 
4 subsection 5, the guardian or conservator shall give a copy of the order of appointment to 
5 the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship, if the individual is 14 years of 
6 age or older, and to all persons given notice of the hearing on the petition. 
7 §5-106. Venue 
8 1. Guardianship proceeding for minor. Venue for a guardianship proceeding for a 
9 minor is in: 
10 A. The county or division of this State in which the minor, the petitioner or a parent 
11 or guardian of the child resides or is present at the time the proceeding commences; 
12 or 
13 B. The county or division of this State where another proceeding concerning the 
14 custody and parental rights of the minor is pending. 
15 2. Guardianship proceeding or protective arrangement for adult. Venue for a 
16 guardianship proceeding or protective arrangement instead of guardianship for an adult is 
17 in: 
18 A. The county of this State in which the respondent resides; 
19 B. If the respondent has been admitted to an institution by order of a comt of 
20 competent jurisdiction, the county in which the court is located; or 
21 C. In a proceeding for appointment of an emergency guardian of an adult, the county 
22 in which the respondent is present. 
23 3. Conservatorship proceeding 01· protective arrangement. Venue for a 
24 conservatorship proceeding or protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is in: 
25 A. The county of this State in which the respondent resides, whether or not a 
26 guardian has been appointed in another county or another jurisdiction: or 
27 B. If the respondent does not reside in this State, any county of this State in which 
28 property of the respondent is located. 
29 4. Proceedings in more than one county. If proceedings under this Act are brought 
30 in more than one county in this State, the comt of the county in which the first proceeding 
31 is brought has the exclusive right to proceed unless the comt determines venue is properly 
32 in another court or the interest of justice otherwise requires transfer of the proceeding. 
33 §5-107. Practice in court 
34 1. Rules. Except as otherwise provided in this Act, the Maine Rules of Probate 
35 Procedure, the Maine Rules of Civil Procedure and the Maine Rules of Evidence, 
36 including rules concerning appellate review, govern a proceeding under this Act. 
37 2. Consolidation. If proceedings under this Act for the same individual are 
3 8 commenced or pending in the same court, the proceedings may be consolidated.

§5-108. Letters of office 
2 1. Guardian; letters of office. On a guardian's filing of an acceptance of 
3 appointment, the court shall issue appropriate letters of office. 
4 2. Conservator; letters of office. On a conservator's filing of an acceptance of 
5 appointment and filing of any required bond or compliance with any other asset-
6 protection arrangement required by the court, the court shall issue appropriate letters of 
7 office. 
8 3. Limitations stated. Limitations on the powers of the guardian or conservator or 
9 on the property subject to conservatorship must be stated in the letters of office. 
10 4. Limitations at any time; new letters of office; notice. Upon request or sua 
11 sponte, the court at any time may limit the powers conferred on the guardian or 
12 conservator. The court shall issue new letters of office to reflect the limitation. The court 
13 shall give notice of the limitation to the guardian or conservator, the individual subject to 
14 guardianship or conservatorship, each parent of a minor subject to guardianship or 
15 conservatorship and any other person as the court determines. 
16 §5-109. Effect of acceptance of appointment 
17 A guardian or conservator that accepts appointment submits personally to the 
18 jurisdiction of the court in any proceeding relating to the guardianship or conservatorship. 
19 §5-110. Coguardian; coconservator 
20 1. Appointment at any time. The court at any time may appoint a coguardian or 
21 coconservator to serve immediately or when a designated future event occurs. 
22 2. Acceptance of appointment. A coguardian or coconservator appointed to serve 
23 immediately may act when the coguardian or coconservator files an acceptance of 
24 appointment. 
25 3. Service upon designated future event. A coguardian or coconservator appointed 
26 to serve when a designated future event occurs may act when: 
27 A. The designated event occurs: and 
28 B. The coguardian or coconservator files an acceptance of appointment. 
29 4. Joint decisions. Unless an order of appointment under subsection 1 or subsequent 
30 order states otherwise, coguardians or coconservators shall make decisions jointly. 
31 §5-111. Judicial appointment of successor guardian or successor conservator 
32 1. Appointment of successor by court. The court at any time may appoint a 
33 successor guardian or successor conservator to serve immediately or when a designated 
34 future event occurs. 
35 2. Petition to appoint successor. A person entitled under section 5-202 or 5-302 to 
36 petition the court to appoint a guardian may petition the court to appoint a successor 
3 7 guardian. A person entitled under section 5-402 to petition the court to appoint a 
38 conservator may petition the court to appoint a successor conservator. 
Page 13 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 3. Service upon designated future event. A successor guardian or successor 
2 conservator appointed to serve when a designated future event occurs may act as guardian 
3 or conservator if: 
4 A. The designated event occurs; and 
5 B. The successor guardian or successor conservator files an acceptance of 
6 appointment. 
7 4. Succeeds to powers. A successor guardian or successor conservator succeeds to 
8 the predecessor's powers unless otherwise provided by the court. 
9 §5-112. Effect of death, removal 01· resignation of guardian or conservator 
10 1. Termination. Appointment of a guardian or conservator terminates on the death 
11 or removal of the guardian or conservator or when the court approves a resignation of the 
12 guardian or conservator under subsection 2. 
13 2. Petition to resign; approval. A guardian or conservator must petition the court 
14 to resign. The petition may include a request that the court appoint a successor. 
15 Resignation of a guardian or conservator is effective on the date the resignation is 
16 approved by the court. 
17 3. Liability. Death, removal or resignation of a guardian or conservator does not 
18 affect liability for a previous act or the obligation to account for an action taken on behalf 
19 of the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship or to account for the 
20 individual's money or other property. 
21 §5-113. Notice of hearing 
22 1. Notice by movant. If notice of a hearing under this Act is required, the movant 
23 shall give notice of the date, time and place of the hearing to the person to be notified 
24 unless otherwise ordered by the court for good cause. Except as otherwise provided in 
25 this Act, notice must be given in compliance with the Maine Rules of Probate Procedure, 
26 Rule 4 or the Maine Rules of Civil Procedure, Rule 4 at least 14 days before the hearing. 
27 2. Proof of notice. Proof of notice of a hearing under this Act must be made before 
28 or at the hearing and filed in the proceeding. 
29 3. Type size; plain language. Notice of a hearing under this Act must be in at least 
30 16-point type, in plain language and, to the extent feasible, in a language in which the 
31 recipient is proficient. 
32 §5-114. Waiver of notice 
33 1. Waiver bv person. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, a person may 
34 waive notice under this Act in a record signed by the person or the person's attorney and 
3 5 filed in the proceeding. 
36 2. Waiver prohibited. A respondent, an individual subject to guardianship, an 
37 individual subject to conservatorship, an individual subject to a protective arrangement 
38 instead of guardianship or conservatorship, an appointed guardian or an appointed 
39 conservator may not waive notice under this Act.

§5-115. Guardian ad litem 
At any stage of a proceeding under this Act, the court may appoint a guardian ad 
litem for an individual to identify and represent the individual's best interest or perform 
other duties if the court determines the individual's interest otherwise would not be 
adequately represented. If a conflict of interest or potential conflict of interest does not 
exist, a guardian ad litem may be appointed to represent multiple individuals or interests. 
The guardian ad litem may not be the same individual as the attorney representing the 
respondent. The court shall state on the record the duties of the guardian ad litem and the 
reasons for the appointment, as well as responsibility for payment of the guardian ad 
litem fees. 
§5-116. Request for notice 
A person that is interested in the welfare of a respondent, individual subject to 
guardianship or conservatorship or individual subject to a protective arrangement instead 
of guardianship or conservatorship and that is not otherwise entitled to notice under this 
Act may file a request with the court for notice. The court shall send or deliver a copy of 
the request to the guardian, to the custodian if one has been appointed and to the 
individual who is subject to the guardianship, conservatorship or protective arrangement. 
The recipient of the notice may file an objection within 60 days. If an objection is filed, 
the comt shall hold a hearing on the request. If the court approves the request, the court 
shall give notice of the approval to the guardian or conservator if one has been appointed 
or to the respondent if no guardian or conservator has been appointed. The request must 
include a statement showing the interest of the person making it and the address of the 
person or an attorney for the person to whom notice is to be given. 
§5-117. Disclosure of bankruptcy or criminal history 
1. Disclosure; petition. As part of the petition to be appointed a guardian or 
conservator. a person shall disclose to the court whether the person: 
A. Is or has been a debtor in a bankruptcy, insolvency or receivership proceeding; or 
B. Has been convicted of: 
(1) A felony; 
(2) A crime involving dishonesty, neglect, violence or use of physical force; or 
(3) Any other crime relevant to the functions the individual would assume as 
guardian or conservator. 
2. Agent; convictions; approval. A guardian or conservator may not engage an 
agent the guardian or conservator knows has been convicted of a felony. a crime 
involving dishonesty, neglect. violence or use of physical force or any other crime 
relevant to the functions the agent is being engaged to perform promptly without prior 
approval of the court. 
3. Finances manager agent; debtor; disclosure. If a conservator engages or 
anticipates engaging an agent to manage finances of the individual subject to 
conservatorship and knows the agent is or has been a debtor in a bankrnptcy, insolvency 
Page 15 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 or receivership proceeding, the conservator promptly shall disclose that knowledge to the 
2 court. 
3 §5-118. Multiple appointments or nominations 
4 If a respondent or other person makes more than one appointment or nomination of a 
5 guardian or a conservator, the latest in time governs. 
6 §5-119. Compensation and expenses; in general 
7 1. Attorney for respondent. Unless otherwise compensated for services rendered, 
8 an attorney for a respondent in a proceeding under this Act is entitled to reasonable 
9 compensation and reimbursement of reasonable expenses from the property of the 
10 respondent. 
11 2. Attorney 01· other person. Unless otherwise compensated for services rendered, 
12 an attorney or other person whose services resulted in an order beneficial to an individual 
13 subject to guardianship or conservatorship or beneficial to an individual for whom a 
14 protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship was ordered is entitled 
15 to reasonable compensation and reimbursement of reasonable expenses from the property 
16 of the individual. 
17 3. Court review. After notice to all interested persons, on petition of an interested 
18 person, the propriety of employment of any person by a conservator or guardian, 
19 including any attorney, accountant, investment advisor or other specialized agent or 
20 assistant, and the reasonableness of the compensation of any person so employed may be 
21 reviewed by the court. Any person who has received excessive compensation or 
22 reimbursement of inappropriate expenses for services rendered may be ordered to make 
23 appropriate refunds. The factors set forth in section 3-721, subsection 2 must be 
24 considered as guides in determining the reasonableness of compensation under this 
25 section. 
26 4. Costs assessed against petitioner. If the court dismisses a petition under this Act 
27 and determines the petition was filed in bad faith, the court may assess the cost of any 
28 court-ordered professional evaluation or visitor against the petitioner. 
29 §5-120. Liability of guardian or conservator for act of individual subject to 
30 guardianship or conservatorship 
31 A guardian or conservator is not personally liable to a 3rd person for the act of an 
32 individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship solely by reason of the guardianship 
33 or conservatorship. 
34 §5-121. Petition after appointment for instructions or ratification 
35 1. Petition. A guardian or conservator may petition the court for instruction 
36 conceming fiduciary responsibility or ratification of a paiiicular act. 
37 2. Instruction or order. On notice and hearing on a petition under subsection 1, the 
38 court may give an appropriate instruction and enter any appropriate order.

1 §5-122. Third-party acceptance of authority of guardian or conservator 
2 1. Refusal to recognize authority required. A person must refuse to recognize the 
3 authority of a guardian or conservator to act on behalf of an individual subject to 
4 guardianship or conservatorship if: 
5 A. The person has actual knowledge or a reasonable belief that the guardian's or 
6 conservator's letters of office are invalid or that the guardian or conservator is 
7 exceeding or improperly exercising authority granted by the court; or 
8 B. The person has actual knowledge that the individual subject to guardianship or 
9 conservatorship is subject to physical or financial abuse, neglect, exploitation or 
10 abandonment by· the guardian or conservator or a person acting for or with the 
11 guardian or conservator. 
12 2. Refusal to recognize authority discretionary. A person may refuse to recognize 
13 the authority of a guardian or conservator to act on behalf of an individual subject to 
14 guardianship or conservatorship if: 
15 A. The guardian's or conservator's proposed action would be inconsistent with this 
16 Act; or 
17 B. The person makes, or has actual knowledge that another person has made, a report 
18 to adult protective services or child protective services stating a good faith belief that 
19 the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship is subject to physical or 
20 financial abuse, neglect, exploitation or abandonment by the guardian or conservator 
21 or a person acting for or with the guardian or conservator. 
22 3. Report refusal to court. A person that refuses to accept the authority of a 
23 guardian or conservator in accordance with subsection 2 shall report the refusal and the 
24 reason for refusal to the court. The court on receiving a report shall consider whether 
25 removal of the guardian or conservator or other action is appropriate. 
26 4. Petition to require acceptance. A guardian or conservator may petition the court 
27 to require a 3rd party to accept a decision made by the guardian or conservator on behalf .. 
28 of the individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship. 
29 §5-123. Use of agent by guardian or conservator 
30 1. Delegation consistent with plan and fiduciary duty. Except as otherwise 
31 provided in subsection 3, a guardian or conservator may delegate a power to an agent that 
32 a prudent guardian or conservator of comparable skills could prudently delegate under the 
33 circumstances if the delegation is consistent with the guardian's or conservator's plan and 
34 fiduciary duty. · 
35 2. Delegating a power. In delegating a power under subsection 1, the guardian or 
36 conservator shall exercise reasonable care, skill and caution in: 
3 7 A. Selecting the agent; 
38 B. Establishing the scope and terms of the agent's work in accordance with the 
39 guardian's or conservator's plan; 
40 C. Monitoring the agent's performance and compliance with the delegation; and 
Page 17 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 D. Redressing action or inaction of the agent that would constitute a breach of the 
2 guardian's or conservator's duties if performed by the guardian or conservator. 
3 3. Delegation limitation. A guardian or conservator may not delegate all powers to 
4 an agent. 
5 4. Agent performing a delegated power. In performing a power delegated under 
6 this section, an agent shall: 
7 A. Exercise reasonable care to comply with the terms of the delegation and use 
8 reasonable care in the performance of the delegated power; and 
9 B. If the agent has been delegated the power to make a decision on behalf of the 
10 individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship, in making the decision use the 
11 same decision-making standard the guardian or conservator would be required to use 
12 in making the decision. 
13 5. Jurisdiction of court. By accepting a delegation of a power from a guardian or 
14 conservator under this section, an agent submits to the jurisdiction of the courts of this 
15 State in an action involving the agent's performance as agent. 
16 6. Liability. A guardian or conservator that delegates and monitors a power in 
17 compliance with this section is not liable for the decisions or actions of the agent. 
18 §5-124. Temporary substitute guardian or conservator 
19 1. Temporary substitute gua1·dian. The court may appoint a temporary substitute 
20 guardian for a period not longer than 6 months for an individual subject to guardianship 
21 if: 
22 A. A proceeding to remove an existing guardian is pending; or 
23 B. The comt finds an existing guardian is not effectively performing the guardian's 
24 duties and the welfare of the individual requires immediate action. 
25 2. Temporary substitute conservat01·. The court may appoint a temporary 
26 substitute conservator for a period not longer than 6 months for an individual subject to 
27 conservatorship if: 
28 A. A proceeding to remove an existing conservator is pending; or 
29 B. The court finds that an existing conservator is not effectively performing the 
30 conservator's duties and the welfare of the individual or the conservatorship estate 
31 requires immediate action. 
32 3. Powers. Except as otherwise ordered by the court, a temporary substitute 
33 guardian or temporary substitute conservator appointed under this section has the powers 
34 stated in the order of appointment of the guardian or conservator. The authority of an 
3 5 existing guardian or conservator is suspended for as long as the temporary substitute 
36 guardian or conservator has authority. 
37 4. Notice. The court shall give notice of appointment of a temporary substitute 
3 8 guardian or temporaiy substitute conservator under this section not later than 5 days after 
39 the appointment to: 
40 A. The individual subject to guardianship or conservatorship; 
Page 18 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
B. The affected guardian or conservator; and 
2 C. In the case of a minor, each parent of the minor and any person currently having 
3 custody or care of the minor. 
4 5. Removal. The court may remove a temporary substitute guardian or temporary 
5 substitute conservator appointed under this section at any time. The temporary substitute 
6 guardian or temporary substitute conservator shall make any report the court requires. 
7 6. Application. Except as otherwise provided in this section, the provisions of this 
8 Act: 
9 A. Concerning a guardian for a minor apply to a temporary substitute guardian for a 
10 minor; 
11 B. Concerning a guardian for an adult apply to a temporary substitute guardian for an 
12 adult; and 
13 C. Concerning a conservator apply to a temporary substitute conservator. 
14 §5-125. Registration of order; effect 
15 1. Registration of guardianship order. If a guardian has been appointed for an 
16 individual in another state and a petition for guardianship of the individual is not pending 
17 in this State, the guardian appointed in the other state, after giving notice to the 
18 appointing court, may register the guardianship order in this State by filing as a foreign 
19 judgment, in a court of an appropriate county of this State, certified copies of the order 
20 and letters of office. 
21 2. Registration of conservatorship order. If a conservator is appointed in another 
22 state and a petition for conservatorship is not pending in this State, the conservator 
23 appointed in the other state, after giving notice to the appointing court. may register the 
24 conservatorship in this State by filing as a foreign judgment, in a court of a county in 
25 which property belonging to the individual subject to conservatorship is located, certified 
26 copies of the order of conservatorship. letters of office and any bond or other asset-
27 protection arrangement required by the court. 
28 3. Exercise of powers. On registration of a guardianship or conservatorship order 
29 from another state, the guardian or conservator may exercise in this State all powers 
30 authorized in the order except as prohibited by the law of this State other than this Act. 
31 If the guardian or conservator is not a resident of this State, the guardian or conservator 
32 may maintain an action or proceeding in this State subject to any condition imposed by 
33 this State on a nonresident party. 
34 4. Enforcement of registered order. The court may grant any relief available under 
35 this Act and law of this State other than this Act to enforce a registered order. 
36 §5-126. Grievance against guardian or conservator 
37 1. File a grievance with the court. An individual who is subject to guardianship or 
38 conservatorship, or a person interested in the welfare of an individual subject to 
39 guardianship or conservatorship, who reasonably believes a guardian or conservator is 
40 breaching the guardian's or conservator's :fiduciary duty or otherwise acting in a manner 
Page 19 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 inconsistent with this Act may file a grievance with the court. The grievance must be in 
2 writing or another record. 
3 2. Procedure upon receiving grievance. Subject to subsection 3, after receiving a 
4 grievance under subsection 1, the court: 
5 A. Shall review the grievance and, if necessary to determine the appropriate response 
6 to the grievance, court records related to the guardianship or conservatorship; 
7 B. Shall schedule a hearing if the individual subject to guardianship or 
8 conservatorship is an adult and the grievance supports a reasonable belief that: 
9 (1) Removal of the guardian and appointment of a successor may be appropriate 
10 in accordance with section 5-318; 
11 (2) Termination or modification of the guardianship may be appropriate under 
12 section5-319; 
13 (3) Removal of the conservator and appointment of a successor may be 
14 appropriate under section 5-430; 
15 (4) Termination or modification of the conservatorship may be appropriate under 
16 section 5-431; and 
17 
18 
19 C. May take any action supported by the grievance and record, including: 
(1) Ordering the guardian or conservator to provide to the court a report, 
accounting, inventory, updated plan or other information; 
20 (2) Appointing a guardian ad litem; 
21 (3) Appointing an attorney for the individual subject to guardianship or 
22 conservatorship; or 
23 (4) Scheduling a hearing. 
24 3. Similar grievance filed within 6 months. The court may decline to proceed 
25 under subsection 2 if a similar grievance was made within the preceding 6 months and the 
26 comt followed the procedures of subsection 2 in considering the grievance. 
27 §5-127. Delegation by parent or guardian 
28 1. Delegation; power of attorney. A parent or a guardian of a minor or individual

32 adoption or termination of parental rights to the minor. A delegation of powers by a 
33 court-appointed guardian becomes effective only when the power of attorney is filed with 
34 the court. A delegation of powers under this section does not deprive the parent or 
3 5 guardian of any parental or legal authority regarding the care and custody of the minor or 
36 individual subject to guardianship. A delegation of powers under this section is subject to 
3 7 the same court supervision that applies to temporary substitute guardians as described in 
38 section 5-124, subsection 5. Any delegation lmder this section may be revoked or

2. National Guard or Reserves; extension. Notwithstanding subsection 1, unless 
otherwise stated in the power of attorney, if the parent or guardian is a member of the 
National Guard or Reserves of the United States Armed Forces under an order to active 
duty for a period of more than 30 days. a power of attorney that would otherwise expire is 
automatically extended until 30 days after the parent or guardian is no longer under that 
active duty order or until an order of the court so provides. 
This subsection applies only if the parent's or guardian's service is in support of: 
A. An operational mission for which members of the reserve components have been 
ordered to active duty without their consent; or 
B. Forces activated during a period of war declared by the United States Congress or 
a period of national emergency declared by the President of the United States or the 
United States Congress. 
3. Temporary care of minor. This subsection applies when a parent or guardian 
executes a power of attorney under subsection 1 for the purpose of providing for the 
temporary care of a minor. 
A. The execution of a power of attorney under subsection 1, without other evidence, 
does not constitute abandonment, abuse or neglect. A parent or guardian of a minor 
may not execute a power of attorney with the intention of permanently avoiding or 
divesting the parent or guardian of parental and legal responsibility for the care of the 
minor. Upon the expiration or termination of the power of attorney, the minor must 
be returned to the custody of the parent or guardian as soon as reasonably possible 
unless otherwise ordered by the court. 
B. Unless the power of attorney is terminated, the agent named in the power of 
attorney shall exercise parental or legal authority on a continuous basis without 
compensation from the State for the duration of the power of attorney authorized by 
subsection 1. Nothing in this subsection disqualifies the agent from applying for and 
receiving benefits from any state or federal program of assistance for the minor or the 
agent. Nothing in this subsection prevents individuals or religious, community or 
other charitable organizations from voluntarily providing the agent with support 
related to the care of the minor while the minor is in the temporary care of the agent. 
C. A minor may not be considered placed in foster care or in any way a ward of the 
State by virtue of the parent's or guardian's execution of a power of attorney 
authorized by subsection 1. The agent named in the power of attorney may not be 
considered a family foster home by virtue of the parent's or guardian's execution of a 
power of attorney authorized by subsection 1 and is not subject to any laws regarding 
the licensure or regulation of family foster homes unless licensed as a family foster 
home. Nothing in this subsection disqualifies the agent from being or becoming a 
family foster home licensed by the State or prevents the placement of the minor in the 
agent's care if the minor enters state custody. 
4. Background check. An organization, other than an organization whose primary 
purpose is to provide free legal services or to provide hospital services, that is exempt 
Page 21 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D, 123 
1 from federal income taxation under Section 501(a) of the United States Internal Revenue 
2 Code of 1986 as an organization described by Section 501(c)(3) and that assists parents or 
3 guardians with the process of executing a power of attorney for the temporary care of a 
4 minor shall ensure that a background check is conducted for the agent and any adult 
5 members of the agent's household, whether by completing the background check directly 
6 or by verifying that a current background check has already been conducted. The 
7 background check must include the following sources, and the results must be shared 
8 with the parent or guardian and the proposed agent: 
9 A A screening for child and adult abuse, neglect or exploitation cases in the records 
10 of the Department of Health and Human Services; and 
11 B. A criminal hist01y record check that includes information obtained from the 
12 Federal Bureau of Investigation. 
13 The organization shall maintain records on the training and background checks of agents, 
14 including the content and dates of training and full transcripts of background checks, for a 
15 period of not less than 5 years after the minor attains 18 years of age. The organization 
16 shall make the records available to a parent or guardian executing a power of attorney 
17 under this section and to the ombudsman under Title 22, section 4087-A and any local, 
18 state or federal authority conducting an investigation involving the agent, the parent or 
19 guardian o:i; the minor. 
20 Without regard to whether an organization is included or excluded by the terms of this 
21 subsection, nothing in this section changes the restrictions on the unauthorized practice of 
22 law as provided in Title 4, section 807 with regard to the preparation of powers of 
23 attorney. 
24 5. Disqualification of agent. An employee or volunteer for an organization 
25 described in subsection 4 may not further assist with a process that results in the 
26 completion of a power of attorney for the temporary care of a minor if the background 
27 checks conducted pursuant to subsection 4, paragraphs A and B disclose any 
28 substantiated allegations of child abuse, neglect or exploitation or any crimes that would 
29 disqualify the agent from becoming a licensed family foster home in the State. 
3 0 6. Penalties. The following penalties apply to violations of this section. 
31 A An organization that knowingly fails to perfo1m or verify the background checks 
32 or fails to share the background check information as required by subsection 4 is 
33 subject to a civil penalty not to exceed $5,000, payable to the State and recoverable in 
34 a civil action. 
35 B. An organization or an employee or volunteer of an organization that continues to 
36 assist a parent, guardian or agent in completing a power of attorney under subsection 
3 7 4 if the background checks conducted pursuant to subsection 4 disclose any 
38 substantiated allegations of child abuse, neglect or exploitation or any crimes that 
39 would disqualify the agent from becoming a licensed family foster home is subject to 
40 a civil penalty not to exceed $5,000, payable to the State and recoverable in a civil 
41 action. 
42 C. An organization or an employee or volunteer of an organization that knowingly 
43 fails to maintain records or to disclose information as required by subsection 4 is

3 PART 2 
4 GUARDIANSHIP OF MINOR 
5 §5-201. Appointment and status of guardian 
6 A person becomes a guardian of a minor by parental appointment or upon 
7 appointment by the court. The guardianship status continues until terminated. without 
8 regard to the location of the guardian or the minor. This section does not apply to 
9 permanency guardians appointed in District Court child protective proceedings under 
10 Title 22. section 4038-C. If a minor has a permanency guardian, the court may not 
11 appoint another guardian without leave of the District Court in which the child protective 
12 proceeding is pending. 
13 §5-202. Parental appointment of guardian 
14 1. Appointment by parent. A guardian may be appointed by will or other signed 
15 writing by a parent for any minor child the parent has or may have in the future. The 
16 appointment may specify the desired limitations on the powers to be given to the 
17 guardian. The appointing parent may revoke or amend the appointment before 
18 confirmation by the court. 
19 2. Petition to confirm selection, terminate right to object. Upon petition of an 
20 appointing parent and a finding that the appointing parent will likely become unable to 
21 care for the child within 2 years. and after notice as provided in section 5-205, subsection 
22 1, the court. before the appointment becomes effective, may confirm the parent's selection 
23 of a guardian and terminate the rights of others to object. 
24 3. Appointment effective. Subject to section 5-203, the appointment of a guardian 
25 becomes effective upon the appointing parent's death. an adjudication that the parent is an 
26 incapacitated person or a written determination by a physician who has examined the 
27 parent that the parent is no longer able to care for the child. whichever frrst occurs. 
28 4. Acceptance of appointment. The guardian becomes eligible to act upon the· 
29 filing of an acceptance of appointment, which must be filed within 30 days after the 
30 guardian's appointment becomes effective. The guardian shall: 
31 A. File the acceptance of appointment and a copy of the will with the court of the 
32 county in which the will was or could be probated or. in the case of another 
33 appointing instrument, file the acceptance of appointment and the appointing 
34 instrument with the court of the county in which the minor resides or is present; and 
35 B. Give written notice of the acceptance of appointment to every parent, if living, the 
36 minor. if the minor has attained 14 years of age, and a person other than the parent 
37 having care and custody of the minor. 
38 5. Notice of right to object. Unless the appointment was previously confirmed by 
39 the court, the notice given under subsection 4, paragraph B must include a statement of 
40 the right of those notified to terminate the appointment by filing a written objection in the 
41 court as provided in section 5-203. 
Page 23 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. [}, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 6. Petition to confirm appointment. Unless the appointment was previously 
2 confirmed by the court, within 30 days after filing the notice and the appointing 
3 instrument, a guardian shall petition the court for confirmation of the appointment, giving 
4 notice in the manner provided in section 5-205, subsection 1. 
5 7. Parental rights not superseded; priority. The appointment of a guardian by a 
6 parent does not supersede the parental rights of any parent. If all parents are dead or have 
7 been adjudged incapacitated persons, an appointment by the last parent who died or was 
8 adjudged incapacitated has priority. An appointment by a parent that is effected by filing 
9 the guardian's acceptance under a will probated in the state of the testator's domicile is 
10 effective in this State. 
11 8. Relation back of powers. The powers of a guardian who timely complies with 
12 the requirements of subsections 4 and 6 relate back to give acts by the guardian that are of 
13 benefit to the minor and occurred on or after the date the appointment became effective 
14 the same effect as those that occurred after the filing of the acceptance of the 
15 appointment. 
16 9. Termination of authority. The authority of a guardian appointed under this 
17 section terminates upon the first to occur of the appointment of a guardian by the court or 
18 the giving of written notice to the guardian of the filing of an objection pursuant to 
19 section 5-203. 
20 §5-203. Objection by minor or others to parental appointment 
21 Until the court has confirmed an appointee under section 5-202, a minor who is the 
22 subject of an appointment by a parent and who has attained 14 years of age, the other 
23 parent or a person other than a parent or guardian having care or custody of the minor 
24 may prevent or terminate the appointment at any time by filing a written objection in the 
25 court in which the appointing instrument is filed and giving notice of the objection to the 
26 guardian and any other persons entitled to notice of the acceptance of the appointment. 
27 An objection may be withdrawn and if withdrawn is of no effect. The objection does not 
28 preclude judicial appointment of the person selected by the parent if all other 
29 requirements for appointment, including appointment over the objection of a parent, are 
30 met. The court may treat the filing of an objection as a petition for the appointment of an 
31 emergency or interim guardian under section 5-204 and proceed accordingly. 
32 §5-204. Judicial appointment of guardian; conditions for appointment 
33 1. Petition. A minor or a person interested in the welfare of a minor may petition for 
34 appointment of a guardian. 
35 2. Appointment. The comt may appoint a guardian for a minor if the court finds the 
36 appointment is in the best interest of the minor, finds the proposed guardian is suitable 
3 7 and finds: 
38 A. That the parents consent; 
39 B. That all parental rights have been terminated; or 
40 C. By clear and convincing evidence that the parents are unwilling or unable to 
41 exercise their parental rights, including but not limited to: 
Page 24 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEEAMENDMENT"~"toH.P. 91,L.D.123 
1 (1) The parent is currently unwilling or unable to meet the minor's needs and that 
2 will have a substantial adverse effect on the minor's well-being if the minor lives 
3 with the parent; or 
4 (2) The parent has failed, without good cause, to maintain a parental relationship 
5 with the minor, including but not limited to failing to maintain regular contact 
6 with the minor for a length of time that evidences an intent to abandon the minor. 
7 3. Priority for appointment. If a guardian is appointed by a parent pursuant to 
8 section 5-202 and the appointment has not been prevented or terminated under section 
9 5-203, that appointee has priority for appointment. However, the court may proceed with 
10 another appointment upon a finding that the appointee under section 5-202 has failed to 
11 accept the appointment within 30 days after notice of the guardianship proceeding. 
12 4. Appointment of a guardian on an emergency basis. If the court finds that 
13 following the procedures of this Patt will likely result in substantial harm to a minor's 
14 health or safety and that no other person appears to have authority to act in the 
15 circumstances, the court, on appropriate petition, may appoint an emergency guardian for 
16 the minor. The duration of the guardian's authority may not exceed 90 days, and the 
17 guardian may exercise only the powers specified in the order. Reasonable notice of the 
18 time and place of the hearing on the petition for appointment of an emergency guardian 
19 must be given to the minor, if the minor has attained 14 years of age, to each living parent 
20 of the minor and a person having care or custody of the minor, if other than a parent. The 
21 court may dispense with the notice if it finds from affidavit or testimony that the minor 
22 will be substantially harmed before a hearing can be held on the petition. If the guardian 
23 is appointed without notice, notice of the appointment must be given within 48 hours 
24 after the appointment. The court shall schedule a hearing on the appointment of the 
25 guardian within 14 days but not less than 7 days after issuance of the order appointing the 
26 guardian, except that a parent may request that the hearing take place sooner. The 
27 petitioner bears the burden of proof on the appropriateness of the appointment pursuant to 
28 this section. 
29 5. Child support. When appointing a guardian, including on an emergency or 
30 interim basis, the court's order must indicate whether there are any support orders 
31 involving the child presently in effect through judicial or administrative proceedings and 
32 the effect of the guardianship appointment on the orders. The court shall consider 
33 whether to order a parent to pay child support to the guardian in accordance with Title 
34 19-A, Part 3. A guardian must be treated as a caretaker relative for computation of a 
35 parental support obligation pursuant to Title 19-A, section 2006, subsection 4. The comt 
36 may reserve the question of support or decline to issue an order if it determines that an 
3 7 order for support is not warranted at the time of the appointment. When the Department 
38 of Health and Human Services provides child support enforcement services, the 
39 Commissioner of Health and Human Services may designate employees of the 
40 depatiment who are not attorneys to represent the depatiment in court if a hearing is held. 
41 The commissioner shall ensure that appropriate training is provided to all employees who 
42 are designated to represent the department under this subsection.

1 §5-205. Judicial appointment of guardian; procedure 
2 1. Petition; notice of hearing. After a petition for appointment of a guardian is 
3 filed, the court shall schedule a he'aring, and the petitioner shall give notice of the time 
4 and place of the hearing, together with a copy of the petition, to: 
5 A. The minor, if the minor has attained 14 years of age and is not the petitioner; 
6 B. Any person alleged to have had the primary care and custody of the minor during 
7 the 60 days before the filing of the petition; 
8 C. Each living parent of the minor or, if there is none, the adult nearest in ldnship 
9 who can be found; 
10 D. Any person nominated as guardian by the minor if the minor has attained 14 years 
11 of age; 
12 E. Any appointee of a parent whose appointment has not been prevented or 
13 terminated under section 5-203; and 
14 F. Any guardian or conservator currently acting for the minor in this State or 
15 elsewhere. 
16 If the court finds that receiving information from the Department of Health and Human 
17 Services may be necessary for the determination of any issue before the court, it may 
18 order a Department of Health and Human Services employee to attend the hearing and to 
19 provide information relevant to the proceeding. When receiving infonnation by oral 
20 testimony that is confidential pursuant to Title 22, section 4008, the court shall close the 
21 proceeding and ensure that it is recorded. When receiving information contained in 
22 written or media records that is confidential pursuant to Title 22, section 4008, the court 
23 shall review those records in camera, weighing the confidentiality of such records against 
24 the necessity for counsel and the parties to have access to them, and enter an appropriate 
25 order regarding the scope and manner of access. The court, in its discretion, may take 
26 other measures necessary to preserve the confidentiality of the information received. 
27 2. Appointment; other disposition. The court, after the hearing scheduled pursuant 
28 to subsection 1, shall make the appointment of a guardian if the court finds that venue is 
29 proper, the required notices have been given, the conditions of section 5-204, subsection 
30 2 have been met and the best interest of the minor will be served by the appointment. In 
31 other cases, the court may dismiss the proceeding or make any other disposition of the 
32 matter that will serve the best interest of the minor. 
33 3. Priority of minor's nominee. The court shall appoint a person or persons 
34 nominated by the minor, if the minor has attained 14 years of age, in accordance with the 
35 requirements of section 5-204. 
36 4. Appointment of counsel. A nonconsenting parent whose parental rights have not 
37 been terminated is entitled to court-appointed legal counsel if indigent. In a contested 
3 8 action, the court may also appoint counsel for any indigent guardian or petitioner when a 
39 parent or legal custodian has counsel. 
40 5. Attorney for a minor; notice to minor. If the court dete1mines at any stage of 
41 the proceeding, before or after appointment, that the interests of the minor are or may be 
42 inadequately represented, the court may appoint an attorney to represent the minor, giving

the minor to be present for some or all of a hearing or other proceeding. A minor 14

6. Informed consent of parent. If the petition for guardianship is filed by or with 
the consent of a parent, the petition must include a consent signed by the parent verifying 
that the parent understands the nature of the guardianship and knowingly and voluntarily 
consents to the guardianship. If a parent infornis the court after the petition has been filed 
that the parent wishes to consent to the guardianship, the court shall require the parent to 
sign the consent fo1m at that time. The consent required by this section must be on a 
court form or substantially similar document. 
7. Term or duration of order. The court may specify the term of the appointment 
based on the parties' agreement or the court's findings. The term may be extended or 
otherwise modified by agreement of the parties or after a hearing. If no term is specified. 
the appointment remains in place until modified or the occurrence of an event resulting in 
termination set forth in section 5-210. 
If one of the parents of a minor is a member of the National Guard or the Reserves of the 
United States Armed Forces under an order to active duty for a period of more than 30 
days, a guardianship that would otherwise expire is automatically extended until 30 days 
after the parent is no longer under those active duty orders or until an order of the court so 
provides as long as the parent's service is in support of: 
A. An operational mission for which members of the reserve components have been 
ordered to active duty without their consent; or 
B. Forces activated during a period of war declared by the United States Congress or 
a period of national emergency declared by the President of the United States or the 
United States Congress. 
8. Interim order. Upon motion by a party or the court's initiative, and pursuant to 
an agreement of the parties or findings made after a hearing, the court may enter an· 
interim order appointing a guardian for a period of time up to 6 months or pending the 
court's order after the scheduled final hearing on a petition for appointment, if such an 
order is necessary to provide for the minor's housing, health, education, medical or other. 
essential needs prior to the hearing. Any interim order must meet the requirements of 
section 5-204 and this section, including notice, and may be extended or modified 
pursuant to an agreement of the parties or findings made after a hearing. 
9. Mediation. The court may refer the parties to mediation at any time after a 
petition or motion is filed, if meditation services are available at a reasonable fee or no 
cost, and may require that the parties have made a good faith effort to mediate the issue 
before holding a hearing. If the court finds that any party failed to make a good faith 
effort to mediate, the court may order the parties to submit to mediation, dismiss the 
action or any part of the action, render a decision or judgment by default, assess attorney's 
fees and costs or impose any other sanction that is appropriate in the circumstances. The 
court may also impose an appropriate sanction upon a party's failure without good cause

10. Identifying information sealed. If a party alleges in an affidavit or a pleading 
under oath that the health, safety or liberty of a party or the minor would be jeopardized 
by disclosure of identifying information, including but not limited to the address of a 
party or the minor, the information must be sealed by the register or clerk and not 
disclosed to any other party or to the public unless the court orders the disclosure to be 
made after a hearing in which the court takes into consideration the health, safety or 
liberty of the party or minor and determines that the disclosure is in the interest of justice. 
§5-206. Terms of order appointing guardian 
1. Terms of order. An order appointing a guardian of a minor must include the 
following: 
A The reasons for the appointment of the guardian, including whether there was any 
agreement by the parties or :findings after a hearing; 
B. The powers and duties granted to the guardian, including those set forth in section 
5-207; 
C. The rights and responsibilities retained by the parent, as described in subsection 3; 
D. The anticipated duration of the appointment, including whether it remains in place 
until a petition to modify or terminate and whether the parties agree to termination 
after a patticular event, such as return from deployment: 
E. A description of the process and standards for modification and termination; and 
F. Notice of the court's authority to hold a hearing and find that a party has violated a 
part of the order and is in contempt and to order relief to the other party for the 
violations or contempt. 
2. Other orders concerning minor. If any orders regarding custody or other 
parental rights with respect to a minor are in effect at the time of the appointment of a 
guardian of the minor, the order must refer to the orders and indicate the effect of the 
appointment on the rights and responsibilities set forth in the orders. 
3. Rights and responsibilities retained by parent. An order appointing a guardian 
of a minor must specify whether the minor's parent retains any of the following rights and 
responsibilities after the appointment and, if any such rights or responsibilities are not 
retained, the reasons they are not retained: 
A A schedule of parent-child contact or a determination by the court that denial of 
parent-child contact is necessary to protect the physical safety or emotional well­
being of the minor. The court may dete1mine the reasonable frequency and dlu-ation 
of parent-child contact and may set conditions for parent-child contact that are in the 
best interest of the minor. Any schedule of contact must reflect any existing parent­
child contact order in effect to the extent reasonably practicable and consistent with 
the court's findings or the agreement of the parties. The court may set forth specific 
conditions that must be satisfied by the parent prior to the start of some or all aspects 
of the contact schedule; 
Page 28 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
Cf' COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. (1,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 B. Access to records and information regarding the minor as provided under Title 
2 19-A, section 1653, subsection 2, paragraph D, subparagraph (4); 
3 C. Parental rights and responsibilities as described under Title 19-A, section 1501, 
4 subsection 5; and 
5 D. Child support as defined in Title 19-A, section 1501, subsection 2. 
6 4. Parent.as coguardian. A parent may copetition and be appointed as a coguardian 
7 of the parent's minor child if the court determines a joint appointment with a nonparent is 
8 in the best interest of the minor and is made with the parent's consent. 
9 §5-207. Duties of guardian 
10 1. Guardian has duties and responsibilities of a parent. Except as otherwise 
11 limited by the court, a guardian of a minor has the duties and responsibilities of a parent 
12 regarding the minor's support, care, education, health and welfare. A guardian shall act at 
13 all times in the best interest of the minor and exercise reasonable care, diligence and 
14 prudence. 
15 2. Specific duties and responsibilities. A guardian shall: 
16 A. Become or remain personally acquainted with the minor and maintain sufficient 
17 contact with the minor to know of the minor's capacities, limitations, needs, 
18 opportunities and physical and mental health; 
19 B. Take reasonable care of the minor's personal effects and bring a protective 
20 proceeding if necessary to protect other property of the minor; 
21 C. Expend money of the minor that has been received by the guardian for the minor's 
22 current needs for support, care, education, health and welfare; 
23 D. Conserve any excess money of the minor for the minor's future needs, but if a 
24 conservator has been appointed for the estate of the minor, the guardian shall pay the 
25 money at least quarterly to the conservator to be conserved for the minor's future 
26 needs; 
27 E. Report the condition of the minor and account for money and other assets in the 
28 guardian's possession or subject to the guardian's control, as ordered by the court on, 
29 application of any person interested in the minor's welfare or as required by court 
30 rule; and 
31 F. Inform the court of any change in the minor's custodial dwelling or address. 
32 3. Reporting on the status of the minor. The court may require the guardian of a 
33 minor to submit regular status reports about the minor, to be submitted under oath or 
34 affirmation to the court and served on the parent and guardian ad litem, if still active, on 
35 an annual basis or under other conditions set by the court. 
36 A. The corut may require the status report to include specific information, including 
37 but not limited to the following to the extent applicable to the guardianship: 
38 (1) The current address of the minor and each parent; 
39 (2) The minor's health care and health needs, including any medical and mental 
40 health services the child received;
