(3) The minor's educational needs and progress, including the name of the 
minor's school, day care or other early education program, the minor's grade level 
and the minor's educational achievements: 
(4) Contact between the minor and the minor's parents, including the frequency 
and duration of the contact and whether it was supervised: 
(5) How the parents have been involved in decision making for the minor: 
( 6) Whether the parents have provided any financial support for the minor: 
(7) How the guardian has carried out the guardian's responsibilities and duties 
under the order of appointment: 
(8) An accounting of any funds received on the minor's behalf: 
(9) The minor's strengths, challenges and any other areas of concern; and 
(10) Recommendations with supporting reasons as to whether the guardianship 
order should be continued, modified or terminated. 
B. Before deciding whether to require status reports, the court shall consider whether 
reporting would create a substantial likelihood of harm to the health, safety or liberty 
of the minor. 
C. The contents of status reports are confidential and may not be released to any 
nonparty except by court order. 
D. A parent may petition the court to seek a status report from the guardian if one is 
not othetwise required. A person who is not a parent but is interested in the minor's 
welfare may petition the court to seek a status report based upon specific concerns 
about the minor's care. 
E. Nothing in this subsection limits a court's authority to otherwise supervise the 
guardianship, including scheduling a status conference to address matters raised in a 
status report or to be held at a specified time after the entry of the order or appointing 
a guardian ad litem or visitor to conduct an investigation. The court shall accept any 
information submitted by a minor 14 years of age or older regarding the 
guardianship. 
§5-208. Powers of guardian 
1. Guardian has powers of a parent. Except as otherwise limited by the court, a 
guardian of a minor has the powers of a parent regarding the minor's support, care, 
education, health and welfare. 
2. Specific powers. A guardian may: 
A. Apply for and receive money for the support of the minor otherwise payable to 
the minor's parent, guardian or custodian under the terms of any statutory system of 
benefits or insurance or any private contract, devise, trust, conservatorship or 
custodianship; 
Page 30 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 B. If otherwise consistent with the terms of any order by a court of competent 
2 jurisdiction relating to custody of the minor. talce custody of the minor and establish 
3 the minor's place of custodial dwelling, but may establish or move the minor's 
4 custodial dwelling outside the State only upon express authorization of the court: 
5 C. If a conservator for the estate of a minor has not been appointed with existing 
6 authority, commence a proceeding, including an administrative proceeding, or take 
7 other appropriate action to compel a person to support the minor or to pay money for 
8 the benefit of the minor: 
9 D. Except as limited by section 5-807, consent to medical or other care, treatment or 
10 service for the minor: 
11 E. Consent to the marriage of the minor; and 
12 F. If reasonable under all of the circumstances. delegate to the minor certain 
13 responsibilities for decisions affecting the minor's well-being. 
14 3. Consent to adoption. The court may specifically authorize the gyardian to 
15 consent to the adoption of the minor. 
16 4. Powers of coguardians. If coguardians are appointed, the powers of the 
17 guardians are joint and several, unless limited by the appointing document. 
18 §5;.209. Rights and immunities of guardian 
19 1. Reasonable compensation and reimbursement. A guardian is entitled to 
20 reasonable compensation for services as guardian and to reimbursement for room, board 
21 and clothing grovided by the guardian to the minor, but only as approved by the court. If 
22 a conservator, other than the guardian or a person who is affiliated with the guardian, has 
23 been apgointed for the estate of the minor, reasonable compensation and reimbursement 
24 to the guardian may be agproved and paid by the conservator without order of the court. 
25 2. Personal liability. A guardian need not use the guardian's personal funds for the 
26 minor's expenses. A guardian is not liable to a 3rd person for acts of the minor solely by 
27 reason of the guardianship. A guardian is not liable for injury to the minor resulting from 
28 the negligence or act of a 3rd person providing medical or other care. treatment or service 
29 for the minor except to the extent that a parent would be liable under the circumstances. 
30 §5-210. Modification or termination of guardianship; other proceedings after 
31 appointment 
32 1. Modification of guardianship order. A guardian of a minor, a parent of a minor, 
3 3 a person interested in the welfare of a minor or the minor. if 14 years of age or older, may 
34 file a motion asking the court to modify the terms of an order appointing a guardian or to 
35 take other action in the best interest of the minor as circumstances require. The motion 
36 must be filed with the court and served on all parties entitled to notice. Unless the motion 
3 7 specifies that is it filed with the consent of all parties entitled to notice, the matter must be 
38 set for hearing to determine whether there has been a substantial change in circumstances 
39 necessitating modification of the order and how the court should modify the order in 
40 furtherance of the best interest of the minor and the parent's rights. The court may 
41 identify certain requirements that must be met before specific provisions of the order are 
Page 31 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 modified. A court may modify a term of a guardianship order as needed to grant relief to 
2 a party to address contempt or other failure to follow the order. 
3 2. Termination of guardianship. A guardianship of a minor terminates upon the 
4 minor's death, adoption, emancipation, marriage or attainment of majority or as ordered 
5 by the court pursuant to this section. 
6 3. Termination of appointment. The appointment of a guardian or conservator 
7 terminates upon the death, resignation or removal of the guardian or conservator ol' upon 
8 termination of the guardianship or conservatorship. A resignation of a guardian or 
9 conservator is effective when approved by the court. A parental or spousal appointment 
10 as guardian under an informally probated will terminates if the will is later denied probate 
11 in a formal proceeding. Te1mination of the appointment of a guardian or conservator 
12 does not affect the liability of either for previous acts or the obligation to account for 
13 money and other assets of the minor or protected person. 
14 4. Petition for removal or permission to resign. A minor, if 14 years of age or 
15 older, a parent of the minor or a person interested in the welfare of the minor may petition 
16 for removal of a guardian on the ground that removal would be in the best interest of the 
17 minor or for other good cause. A guardian may petition for permission to resign. A 
18 petition for removal or permission to resign may include a request for appointment of a 
19 successor guardian. 
20 5. Appointment of additional or successor guardian. The court may appoint an 
21 additional guardian at any time, to serve immediately or upon some other designated 
22 event, and may appoint a successor guardian in the event of a vacancy or make the 
23 appointment in contemplation of a vacancy, to serve if a vacancy occurs. An additional 
24 or successor guardian may file an acceptance of appointment at any time after the 
25 appointment, but not later than 30 days after the occurrence of the vacancy or other 
26 designated event. The additional or successor guardian becomes eligible to act on the 
27 occunence of the vacancy or designated event or the filing of the acceptance of 
28 appointment, whichever last occurs. A successor guardian succeeds to the predecessor's 
29 powers. 
30 6. Termination without consent; best interest; subsequent petitions. The court 
31 may not terminate the guardianship of a minor in the absence of the guardian's consent 
32 unless the comi finds by a preponderance of the evidence that the termination is in the 
33 best interest of the minor. The petitioner has the burden of showing by a preponderance 
34 of the evidence that te1mination of the guardianship is in the best interest of the minor. If 
3 5 the court does not terminate the guardianship, the court may dismiss subsequent petitions 
36 for termination of the guardianship unless there has been a substantial change of 
3 7 circumstances. 
38 7. Parent's petition to terminate guardianship; burden of proof. A parent may 
39 bring a petition to terminate the guardianship of a minor. A parent's notification to the 
40 comi of the revocation of prior consent for a guardianship must be considered a petition 
41 to te1minate the guardianship. Before the cou1i may apply the termination requirements 
42 in subsection 6, a party opposing a parent's petition to terminate a guardianship bears the 
43 burden of proving by a preponderance of the evidence that the parent seeking to terminate 
44 the guardianship is currently unfit to regain custody of the minor, in accordance with the 
45 standard set fotih in section 5-204, subsection 2, paragraph C. If the party opposing 
Page 32 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
-c5/\0MMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 termination of the guardianship fails to meet its burden of proof on the question of the 
2 parent's fitness to regain custody. the court shall terminate the guardianship and make any 
3 further order that may be appropriate. In a contested action. the court may appoint 
4 counsel for the minor or for any indigent guardian or parent. In ruling on a petition to 
5 terminate a guardianship, the court may modify the terms of the guardianship or order 
6 transitional arrangements pursuant to section 5-211. 
7 §5-211. Transitional arrangement for minors 
8 In issuing, modifying or terminating an order of guardianship for a minor, the court 
9 may enter an order providing for transitional arrangements for the minor if the corut 
10 determines that such arrangements will assist the minor with a transition of custody and 
11 are in the best interest of the minor. Orders providing for transitional arrangements may 
12 include, but are not limited to, rights of contact. housing, counseling or rehabilitation. In 
13 determining the best interest of the minor, a court may consider the minor's relationship 
14 with the guardian and need for stability. 
15 §5-212. Appointment of guardian ad litem for minor 
16 In any proceeding under this Part, including for issuing, modifying or terminating an 
17 order of guardianship for a minor, the court may appoint a guardian ad litem for the 
18 minor. The appointment may be made at any time, but the court shall make every effort 
19 to make the appointment as soon as possible after the commencement of the proceeding. 
20 The court shall follow the requirements of section 1-111 and other applicable law or court 
21 rules in making the appointment. 
22 PART3 
23 GUARDIANSHIP OF ADULT 
24 §5-301. Basis for appointment of guardian for adult 
25 1. Appointment. On petition and after notice and hearing. the court may: 
26 A. Appoint a guardian for a respondent who is an adult if it finds by clear and 
27 convincing evidence that the respondent lacks the ability to meet essential 
28 requirements for physical health, safety or self-care because: 
29 (1) The respondent is unable to receive and evaluate information or make or 
30 communicate decisions, even with appropriate supportive services. technological 
31 assistance or supported decision making: 
32 (2) The respondent's identified needs cannot be met by a protective arrangement 
33 instead of guardianship or other less restrictive alternatives; and 
34 (3) The appointment is necessary or desirable as a means of enabling the 
35 respondent to meet essential requirements for physical health. safety or self-care: 
36 or 
37 B. With appropriate findings, treat the petition as orte for a conservatorship under 
3 8 Part 4 or a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or conservatorship under 
39 Part 5, enter any other appropriate order or dismiss the proceeding. 
Page 33 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"µ,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 2. Powers. The court shall grant to a guardian appointed under subsection 1 only 
2 those powers necessitated by the limitations and demonstrated needs of the respondent 
3 and enter orders that will encourage the development of the respondent's maximum self-
4 determination and independence. The court may not establish a full guardianship if a 
5 limited guardianship, protective arrangement instead of guardianship or other less 
6 restrictive alternatives would meet the needs of the respondent. 
7 §5-302. Petition for appointment of guardian for adult 
8 1. Petition for appointment. A person interested in an adult's welfare, including the 
9 adult for whom the order is sought, may petition for the appointment of a guardian for the 
10 adult. 
11 2. Contents of petition. A petition under subsection 1 must set forth the petitioner's 
12 name, principal residence, current street address, if different, relationship to the 
13 respondent and interest in the appointment and state or contain the following to the extent 
14 known: 
15 A. The respondent's name, age, principal residence, current street address, if 
16 different, and, if different, address of the dwelling in which it is proposed that the 
17 respondent will reside if the petition is granted; 
18 B. The name and address of the respondent's: 
19 (1) Spouse or domestic partner or, if the respondent has none, any adult with 
20 whom the respondent has shared household responsibilities for more than 6 
21 months in the 12-month period before the filing of the petition; 
22 (2) Adult children or, if the respondent has none, each parent and adult sibling of 
23 the respondent or, if the respondent has none, at least one adult nearest in ldnship 
24 to the respondent who can be found with reasonable diligence; and 
25 (3) Adult stepchildren whom the respondent actively parented during the 
26 stepchildren's minor years and with whom the respondent had an ongoing 
27 relationship within 2 years before the filing of the petition; 
28 C. The name and current address of each of the following, if applicable: 
29 (1) A person responsible for care of the respondent; 
30 (2) Any attorney currently representing the respondent; 
31 (3) The representative payee appointed by the United States Social Security 
32 Administration for the respondent; 
33 (4) A guardian or conservator acting for the respondent in this State or in another 
34 jurisdiction; 
35 (5) A trustee or custodian of a trust or custodianship of which the respondent is a 
36 beneficiary; 
37 (6) The United States Department of Veterans Affairs fiduciary for the 
38 respondent;

4 respondent is identified as the principal; 
5 (9) A person nominated as guardian by the respondent;

1 §5-303. Notice and hearing 
2 1. Date, time and place for hearing. On receipt of a petition under section 5-302 
3 for appointment of a guardian for a respondent who is an adult, the court shall set a date, 
4 time and place for hearing the petition. 
5 2. Notice to respondent. A copy of a petition under section 5-302 and notice of a 
6 hearing on the petition must be served personally on the respondent. The notice must 
7 inform the respondent of the respondent's rights at the hearing, including the right to an 
8 attomey and to attend the hearing. The notice must also include a description of the 
9 nature, purpose and conseguences of granting the petition. Failure to serve the 
10 respondent with notice substantially complying with this subsection precludes the court 
11 from granting the petition. 
12 3. Notice to other persons. In a proceeding on a petition under section 5-302, 
13 notice of the hearing also must be given to any person required to be listed in the petition 
14 under section 5-302, subsection 2, paragraphs A to C and any other person the court 
15 determines is entitled to notice. Failure to give notice under this subsection does not 
16 preclude the court from appointing a guardian. 
17 4. Notice of petition after appointment. Notice of a hearing on a petition that is 
18 filed after the appointment of a guardian and that seeks an order under this Part, together 
19 with a copy of the petition, must be given to the adult subject to guardianship, the 
20 guardian and any other person as the court determines. 
21 §5-304. Appointment of visitor 
22 1. Appointment of visitor. On receipt of a petition for appointment of a guardian 
23 for a respondent who is an adult under section 5-302, the comt shall appoint a visitor. 
24 The visitor must be an individual having training or experience in the type of abilities, 
25 limitations and needs alleged in the petition. 
26 2. Interview with respondent. A visitor appointed under subsection 1 shall 
27 interview the respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to 
28 understand: 
29 A. Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature, purpose and 
30 effect of the proceeding, the respondent's rights at the hearing and the general powers 
31 and duties of a guardian; 
32 B. Determine the respondent's views about the appointment, including views about a 
33 proposed guardian, the guardian's proposed powers and duties and the scope and 
34 duration of the proposed guardianship; 
35 C. Inform the respondent of the respondent's right to employ and consult with an 
36 attorney at the respondent's expense and the right to request a court-appointed 
37 attorney; and 
38 D. Inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the proceeding, including the 
39 respondent's attorney's fees, may be paid from the respondent's assets. 
40 3. Additional duties. In addition to the duties imposed by subsection 2, the visitor 
41 shall:

1 A. Interview the petitioner and nroposed guardian, if any; 
2 B. Visit the respondent's present dwelling and any dwelling in which it is reasonably 
3 believed the respondent will live if the appointment is made; 
4 C. Obtain information from any physician or other person known to have treated, 
5 advised or assessed the respondent's relevant physical or mental condition; and 
6 D. Investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter relating to the 
7 petition as the court directs. 
8 4. Report of visitor. A visitor under this section shall file a report in a record with 
9 the court at least 10 days before any hearing on the petition. The report must include: 
10 A. Whether or not the respondent wishes to contest any aspect of the proceedings or 
11 to seek any limitation on the proposed guardian's powers; 
12 B. A recommendation whether an attorney should be appointed to represent the 
13 respondent; 
14 C. A summary of self-care and independent living tasks the respondent can manage 
15 without assistance or with existing supports, could manage with the assistance of 
16 appropriate supportive services, technological assistance or supported decision 
17 making and cannot manage; 
18 D. Recommendations regarding the appropriateness of guardianship, including 
19 whether a protective arrangement instead of guardianship or other less restrictive 
20 alternatives for meeting the respondent's needs are available and, if a guardianship is 
21 recommended, whether it should be full or limited and, if a limited guardianship, the 
22 powers to be granted to the guardian; 
23 E. A statement of the qualifications of the proposed guardian and whether the 
24 respondent approves or disapproves of the proposed guardian; 
25 F. A statement whether the proposed dwelling meets the respondent's needs and 
26 whether the respondent has expressed a preference as to residence; 
27 G. A recommendation whether a further professional evaluation under section 5-306 
28 is necessary;

30 court proceedings typically are conducted; 
31 I. A statement whether the respondent is able to participate in a hearing and that 
32 identifies any technology· or other form of support that would enhance the 
33 respondent's ability to participate; and 
34 J. Any other matter as the court directs.

3 8 A. Requested by the respondent; 
39 B. Recommended by the visitor;

1 C. The court determines that the respondent needs representation; or 
2 D. It comes to the court's attention that the respondent wishes to contest any aspect

4 2. Duties of attorney. An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding on a 
5 petition under section 5-302 shall: 
6 A. Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes; 
7 B. Advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably ascertainable; and 
8 C. If the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable, advocate for the result 
9 that is the least restrictive option in type, duration and scope, consistent with the 
10 respondent's interests. 
11 §5-306. Professional evaluation 
12 1. Evaluation; report. In every adult gµardianship matter, the respondent must be 
13 examined by a licensed physician or psychologist who is acceptable to the comt and who 
14 is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and functional abilities. The 
15 individual conducting the evaluation shall file a report in a record with the court at least 
16 10 days before any hearing on the petition. Unless otherwise directed by the court, the 
17 report must contain: 
18 A. A description of the nature, type and extent of the respondent's cognitive and 
19 functional abilities and limitations; 
20 B. An evaluation of the respondent's mental and physical condition and, if 
21 appropriate, educational potential, adaptive behavior and social skills; 
22 C. A prognosis for improvement and recommendation for the appropriate treatment, 
23 support or habilitation plan; and 
24 D. The date of the examination on which the report is based. 
25 2. Right to decline. The respondent has the right to decline to participate in an 
26 evaluation ordered under subsection 1. 
27 §5-307. Attendance and rights at hearing 
28 1. Attendance by respondent. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 2, a 
29 hearing under section 5-303 may proceed only if the respondent attends the hearing. If it 
30 is not reasonably feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the location comt 
31 proceedings typically are conducted, the court shall make reasonable efforts to hold the 
32 hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow the respondent to 
33 attend the hearing using real-time audiovisual technology. 
34 2. Hearing without respondent in attendance. A hearing under section 5-303 may 
35 proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court finds by clear and convincing 
36 evidence that: 
37 A. The respondent consistently and repeatedly has refused to attend the hearing after 
3 8 having been fully informed of the right to attend the hearing and the potential 
39 consequences of failing to do so; or 
Page 38 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. (1 "to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 B. There is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and participate in the 
2 hearing even with appropriate supportive services and technological assistance. 
3 3. Assistance to respondent. The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under 
4 section 5-303 by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing, assistive technology or 
5 an interpreter or translator, or a combination of these supports. If assistance would 
6 facilitate the respondent's participation in the hearing but is not otherwise available to the 
7 respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it. 
8 4. Attorney for respondent. The respondent has a right to choose an attorney to 
9 represent the respondent at a hearing under section 5-303. 
10 5. Rights of respondent at hearing. For or at a hearing under section 5-303, the 
11 respondent may: 
12 A. Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents; 
13 B. Examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and the visitor: and 
14 C. Otherwise participate in the hearing. 
15 6. Attendance bv urouosed guardian required. Unless excused by the court for 
16 good cause, the proposed guardian shall attend a hearing under section 5-303. 
17 7. Closed upon request; good cause. A hearing under section 5-303 must be closed 
18 on request of the respondent and a showing of good cause. 
19 8. Participation; best interest of respondent. Anv person may request to 
20 participate in a hearing under section 5-303. The court may grant the request, with or 
21 without hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent will be served. 
22 The court may attach appropriate conditions to the person's participation. 
23 §5-308. Confidentiality of records 
24 1. Matter of public record; exception. The existence of a proceeding for or the 
25 existence of a guardianship for an adult is a matter of public record unless the court seals 
26 the records after: · 
27 A. The respondent or individual subject to guardianship requests the records be 
28 sealed; and 
29 B. Either: 
30 (1) The petition for guardianship is dismissed: or 
31 (2) The guardianship is terminated. 
32 2. Access to court records. An adult subject of a proceeding for a guardianship, 
33 whether or not a guardian is appointed, any attorney designated by the adult and a person 
34 entitled to notice under section 5-310, subsection 5 are entitled to access court records of 
35 the proceeding and resulting guardianship, including a guardian's report or plan. In 
36 addition, a person for good cause may petition the court for access to court records of the 
3 7 guardianship, including an annual report or guardian's plan. The court shall grant access 
38 if access is in the best interest of the respondent or adult subject to guardianship or 
Page 39 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "R" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 furthers the public interest and does not endanger the welfare or financial interest of the 
2 adult. 
3 3. Reports confidential; availability. A report under section 5-304 of a visitor or a 
4 professional evaluation under section 5-306 is confidential and must be sealed on filing 
5 but is available to: 
6 A. The court; 
7 B. The individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation, without limitation as 
8 to use; 
9 C. The petitioner, visitor and petitioner's and respondent's attorneys, for purposes of 
10 the proceeding; 
11 D. An agent appointed under a power of attorney for health care or advance health 
12 care directive, or power of attorney for finances in which the respondent is identified 
13 as the principal, unless the court orders otherwise; and 
14 E. Other persons when it is in the public interest or for a purpose the court orders for 
15 good cause. 
16 §5-309. Who may be guardian of adult; priorities 
17 1. Priority for appointment. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, the 
18 court in appointing a guardian for an adult shall consider persons otherwise qualified in 
19 the following order of priority: 
20 A. A guardian, other than a temporary or emergency guardian, currently acting for 
21 the respondent in another jurisdiction; 
22 B. A person nominated as guardian by the respondent, including the respondent's 
23 most recent nomination made in a power of attorney; 
24 C. An agent appointed by the respondent under a power of attorney for health care or 
25 an advance health care directive; 
26 D. A spouse or domestic partner of the respondent; and 
27 E. A family member or other individual who has exhibited special care and concem 
28 for the respondent. 
29 2. Equal priority. With respect to persons having equal priority under subsection 1, 
30 the court shall select as guardian the person the court considers best qualified. In 
31 determining the best qualified person, the court shall consider the potential guardian's 
32 relationship with the respondent, the potential guardian's sldlls, the expressed wishes of 
33 the respondent, the extent to which the potential guardian and the respondent have similar 
34 values and preferences and the likelihood the potential guardian will be able to satisfy the 
3 5 duties of a guardian successfully. 
36 3. Appointment based on best interest of respondent. The court, acting in the best 
37 interest of the respondent, may decline to appoint as guardian a person having priority 
38 under subsection 1 and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority. 
39 4. Appointment prohibited; exceptions. A person that provides paid services to 
40 the respondent, or an individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services

§5-310. Order of appointment 
1. Order contents. A court order appointing a guardian for an adult must clearly: 
A. Include a finding that clear and convincing evide~ce has established that the 
identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a protective arrangement instead 
of guardianship or other less restrictive alternatives, including use of appropriate 
supportive services, technological assistance or supported decision making: 
B. Include a finding that clear and convincing evidence established that the 
respondent was given proper notice of the hearing on the petition: 
C. State whether the adult subject to guardianship retains the right to vote and, if the 
adult does not retain the right to vote, include findings that support removing that 
right, which must include a finding that the adult cannot communicate, with or 
without support, a specific desire to participate in the voting process: and 
D. State whether the adult subject to guardianship retains the right to marry and, if 
the adult's right to marry is subject to conditions or if the adult does not retain the 
right to marry, include findings that support the conditions on that right or the 
removal of that right. 
2. Rights retained. An adult subject to guardianship retains the right to vote unless 
the order under subsection 1 includes the findings required by subsection 1, paragraph C. 
An adult subject to guardianship retains the right to marry unless the order under 
subsection 1 includes the findings required by subsection l, paragraph D. 
3. Basis for full guardianship. A court order establishing a full guardianship for an 
adult clearly must state the basis for granting a full guardianship and include specific 
findings that support the conclusion that a limited guardianship would not meet the 
functional needs of the adult subject to guardianship. 
4. Limited guardianship; powers granted to guardian. A court order establishing 
a limited guardianship for an adult must state clearly the powers granted to the guardian. 
5. Notice; access to reports and plans. The court shall, as part of any order 
establishing a guardianship for an adult, identify any person that subsequently is entitled 
to: 
A. Notice of the rights of the adult subject to guardianship; 
Page 41 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"~" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 B. Notice of a change in the primary dwelling of the adult subject to gµardianship; 
2 C. Notice that the gµardian has delegated: 
3 (1) The power to manage the care of the adult subject to gµardianship; 
4 (2) The power to make decisions about where the adult subject to guardianship 
5 lives; 
6 (3) The power to make major medical decisions on behalf of the adult subject to 
7 guardianship; 
8 (4) Any power that requires court approval under section 5-315; or 
9 (5) Substantially all powers of the guardian. 
10 D. Notice that the gµardian will be unavailable to visit the adult subject to 
11 guardianship for more than 2 months or unable to perform the guardian's duties for 
12 more than one month; 
13 E. A copy of the guardian's report and plan; 
14 F. Access to court records pertaining to the guardianship; 
15 G. Notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the adult subject to 
16 guardianship; 
17 H. Notice that the court has limited or modified the powers of the guardian; and 
18 I. Notice of the guardian's removal. 
19 6. Entitled to notice; exceptions. A spouse, a domestic partner and the adult 
20 children of the adult subject to guardianship are entitled to notice under subsection 5 
21 unless the court determines notice would be contraty to the preferences or prior directions 
22 of the adult subject to guardianship or not in the best interest of the adult. 
23 §5-311. Notice of order of appointment; rights 
24 A guardian appointed under section 5-309 shall give to the adult subject to 
25 guardianship and to all other persons given notice under section 5-303 a copy of the order 
26 of appointment, together with a notice of the right to request termination or modification. 
27 The order and notice must be given not later than 14 days after the appointment. 
28 §5-312. Emergency guardian 
29 1. Basis for emergency guardianship. On petition by a person interested in an 
30 adult's welfare or on its own after a petition has been filed under section 5-302, the court 
31 may appoint an emergency guardian for the adult if the court finds: 
32 A. Appointment of an emergency guardian is likely to prevent substantial hatm to 
33 the adult's physical health, safety or welfare; 
34 B. No other person appears to have authority and willingness to act in the 
35 circumstances; and 
36 C. There is reason to believe that a basis for appointment of a guardian under section 
37 5-301 may exist. 
Page 42 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" p,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
,·, ,, 
1 2. Limited time and powers. The duration of authority of an emergency guardian 
2 for an adult may not exceed 60 days and the emergency guardian may exercise only the 
3 powers specified in the order. The emergency guardian's authority may be extended once 
4 for not more than 120 days if the court finds that the conditions for appointment of an 
5 emergency guardian in subsection 1 continue. 
6 3. Notice before petition. Prior to filing a petition under this section, notice must be 
7 provided as follows. 
8 A. The petitioner shall provide notice orally or in writing to the following: 
9 (1) The respondent and the respondent's spouse, parents, adult children and any 
10 domestic partner known to the court; 
11 (2) Any person who is serving as guardian or conservator or who has care and 
12 custody of the respondent; and 
13 (3) In case no other person is notified under subparagraph (1), at least one of the 
14 closest adult relatives of the respondent or, if there are none, an adult friend, if 
15 any can be found. 
16 B. Notice under paragraph A must include the following information: 
17 (1) The temporary authority that the petitioner is requesting; 
18 (2) The location and telephone number of the couit in which the petition is being 
19 filed; and 
20 (3) The name of the petitioner and the intended date of filing. 
21 C. The petitioner shall state in an affidavit the date, time, location and method of 
22 providing the required notice under paragraph A and to whom the notice was 
23 provided. The court shall make a determination as to the adequacy of the method of 
24 providing notice and whether the petitioner complied with the notice requirements of 
25 this subsection. The requirements of section 5-309 do not apply to this section. 
26 D. Notice is not required under this subsection in the following circumstances: 
27 (1) Giving notice would place the respondent at substantial risk of abuse, neglect 
28 or exploitation; 
29 (2) Notice, if provided, would not be effective; or 
30 (3) The court determines that there is good cause not to provide notice. 
31 E. If, prior to filing the petition, the petitioner does not provide notice as required 
32 under this subsection, the petitioner must state in the affidavit under paragraph C the 
33 reasons for not providing notice. If notice has not been provided, the court shall 
34 make a determination as to the sufficiency of the reason for not providing notice 
35 before issuing a temporary order. 
36 4. Appointment without notice and hearing. The court may appoint an emergency 
37 guardian for an adult without notice and a hearing only if the court finds from an affidavit 
3 8 or testimony that the respondent will be substantially harmed before a hearing on the 
39 appointment can be held. If the comt appoints an emergency guardian without notice and 
Page 43 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
• 1> a hearing, the court shall, not later than 48 hours after the appointment, notify the 
2 respondent, the respondent's attorney and any other person as the court determines of the 
3 appointment. If the respondent objects to the appointment, the court shall hold a hearing 
4 within 14 days of the appointment. 
5 5. Not a determination. Appointment of an emergency guardian under this section 
6 is not a determination that the conditions required for appointment of a guardian under 
7 section 5-301 have been satisfied. 
8 6. Removal; report; application. The court may remove an emergency guardian 
9 appointed under this section at any time. The emergency guardian shall make any report 
10 the court requires. In other respects, the provisions of this Act concerning guardians 
11 apply to an emergency guardian appointed under this section. 
12 §5-313. Duties of guardian for adult 
13 1. Fiduciary. A guardian for an adult is a fiduciary. Except as otherwise limited by 
14 the court, a guardian for an adult shall make decisions regarding the support, care, 
15 education, health and welfare of the adult subject to guardianship to the extent 
16 necessitated by the adult's limitations. 
17 2. Promote self-determination. A guardian for an adult shall promote the self-
18 determination of the adult subject to guardianship and, to the extent reasonably feasible, 
19 encourage the adult to participate in decisions, act on the adult's own behalf and develop 
20 or regain the capacity to manage the adult's personal affairs. In furtherance of this duty, 
21 the guardian shall: 
22 A. Become or remain personally acquainted with the adult subject to guardianship 
23 and maintain sufficient contact with the adult, including through regular visitation, to 
24 know of the adult's abilities, limitations, needs, opportunities and physical and mental 
25 health; 
26 B. To the extent reasonably feasible, identify the values and preferences of the adult 
27 subject to guardianship and involve the adult in decisions affecting the adult, 
28 including decisions about the adult's care, dwelling, activities and social interactions; 
29 and 
30 C. Make reasonable efforts to identify and facilitate supportive relationships and 
31 services for the adult subject to guardianship. 
32 3. Reasonable care, diligence and prudence. A guardian for an adult at all times 
33 shall exercise reasonable care, diligence and prudence when acting on behalf of or 
34 making decisions for the adult subject to guardianship. In fiutherance of this duty, the 
3 5 guardian shall: 
36 A. Take reasonable care of the personal effects, pets and service or supp01t animals 
37 of the adult subject to guardianship and bring a proceeding for a conservatorship or 
38 protective an-angement instead of conservatorship if necessary to protect the adult's 
39 property; 
40 B. Expend money of the adult subject to guardianship that has been received by the 
41 guardian for the adult's current needs for support, care, education, health and welfare; 
Page 44 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"~" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
:( )f C. Administer assets of the adult subject to guardianship having a value of $5,000 or 
2 less; 
3 D. Conserve any excess money of the adult subject to guardianship for the adult's 
4 future needs, but if a conservator has been appointed for the adult, the guardian shall 
5 pay the money to the conservator, at least quarterly, to be conserved for the adult's 
6 future needs; and 
7 E. Monitor the quality of services, including long-term care services, provided to the 
8 adult subject to guardianship. 
9 4. Decision of the adult. In maldng a decision for an adult subject to guardianship, 
10 the guardian shall malce the decision the guardian reasonably believes the adult would 
11 make if the adult were able unless doing so would unreasonably harm or endanger the 
12 welfare or personal or financial interests of the adult. To determine the decision the adult 
13 subject to guardianship would make if able, the guardian shall consider the adult's prior or 
14 cUl'rent directions, preferences, opinions, values and actions, to the extent actually known 
15 or reasonably ascertainable by the guardian. 
16 5. Decision in best interest of the adult. If a guardian for an adult cannot make a 
17 decision under subsection 4 because the guardian does not know and cannot reasonably 
18 determine the decision that the adult probably would make if able, or the guardian 
19 reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would unreasonably harm or 
20 endanger the welfare or personal or financial interests of the adult, the guardian shall act 
21 in accordance with the best interest of the adult. In determining the best interest of the 
22 adult, the guardian shall consider: 
23 A. Information received from professionals and persons that demonstrate sufficient 
24 interest in the welfare of the adult; 
25 B. Other information the guardian believes the adult would have considered if the 
26 adult were able to act; and 
27 C. Other factors that a reasonable person in the circumstances of the adult would 
28 consider, including consequences for others. 
29 6. Notice to court. A guardian for an adult immediately shall notify the court if the 
30 condition of the adult subject to guardianship has changed so that the adult is capable of 
31 exercising rights previously removed. 
32 §5-314. Powers of guardian for adult 
33 1. Powers. Except as otherwise limited by the court, a guardian for an adult may: 
34 A. Apply for or receive money or benefits for the support of the adult, unless a 
3 5 conservator has been appointed for the adult and the application or receipt is within 
36 the powers of the conservator; 
37 B. If otherwise consistent with an order by a coUl't with jurisdiction relating to the 
3 8 dwelling of the adult, establish the adult's place of dwelling; 
39 C. Consent to medical or other care, treatment or service for the adult; 
Page 45 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" p,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
i D. If a conservator for the adult has not been appointed, commence a proceeding, 
2 including an administrative proceeding, or take other appropriate action to compel 
3 another person to support the adult or pay funds for the adult's benefit; 
4 E. To the extent reasonable, delegate to the adult ce1tain responsibility for decisions 
5 affecting the adult's well-being; and 
6 F. Receive personally identifiable health care information concerning the adult. 
7 2. Adoption. The court may by specific order authorize a guardian for an adult to 
8 consent to the adoption of the adult. 
9 3. Specific order of court required. The court may by specific order authorize a 
10 guardian for an adult to: 
11 A. Consent or withhold consent to the marriage of the adult if the adult's right to 
12 maizy has been removed or made subject to conditions under section 5-310; 
13 B. Petition for divorce, dissolution or annulment of marriage of the adult or for a 
14 declaration of invalidity of the adult's marriage; or 
15 C. Support or oppose a petition for divorce, dissolution or annulment of marriage of 
16 the adult or for a declaration of invalidity of the adult's marriage. 
17 4. Court's consideration. In determining whether to authorize a power under 
18 subsection 2 or 3, the court shall consider whether the underlying act would be in 
19 accordance with the adult's preferences, values and prior directions and whether the 
20 underlying act would be in the best interest of the adult. 
21 5. Duties with respect to dwelling. In exercising the guardian's power under 
22 subsection 1, paragraph B to establish the dwelling of the adult subject to guardianship, a 
23 guardian shall: 
24 A. Select a residential setting the guardian believes the adult would select if the adult 
25 were able, in accordance with the decision-making standard in section 5-313, 
26 subsections 4 and 5. If the guardian does not know and cannot reasonably determine 
27 what setting the adult subject to guardianship probably would choose if able, or the 
28 guardian reasonably believes the decision the adult would make would unreasonably 
29 harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial interests of the adult, the 
30 guardian shall choose in accordance with section 5-313, subsection 5 a residential 
31 setting that is consistent with the best interest of the adult; 
32 B. In selecting among residential settings, give priority to a residential setting that is 
33 in a location that will allow the adult subject to guardianship to interact with persons 
34 important to the adult and meet the adult's needs in the least restrictive manner 
35 reasonably feasible unless doing so would be inconsistent with the decision-making 
36 standard in section 5-313, subsections 4 and 5; 
37 C. Not later than 30 days after a change in the dwelling of the adult subject to 
38 guardianship, give notice of the change to the court, the adult subject to guardianship 
39 and any person identified as entitled to the notice in the comi order appointing the 
40 guardian or a subsequent order. The notice must include the address and nature of 
41 the new dwelling and state whether the adult subject to guardianship received 
42 advance notice of the change and whether the adult objected to the change; 
Page 46 -128LR0452(02)-l 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT

'\L 
·· 1 D. Establish or move the permanent place of dwelling of an adult subject to 
2 guardianship to a nursing home, mental health facility or other facility that places 
3 restrictions on the individual's ability to leave or have visitors only if: 
4 (1) The establishment or move is set forth in the guardian's plan; 
5 (2) The court authorizes the establishment or move; or 
6 (3) Notice of the establishment or move is given at least 14 days before the 
7 establishment or move to the adult subject to guardianship and all persons 
8 entitled to the notice under section 5-310, subsection 5 or a subsequent order and 
9 no objection has been filed: 
10 E. Establish or move the place of dwelling of an adult subject to guardianship 
11 outside this State only if consistent with the guardian's plan and authorized by the 
12 court by specific order: and 
13 F. Take action that would result in the sale of or surrender the lease to the primary 
14 dwelling of the adult subject to guardianship only if: 
15 (1) The action is specifically set forth in the guardian's plan: 
16 (2) The court authorizes the action by specific order: or 
17 (3) Notice of the action is given at least 14 days before the action to the adult 
18 subject to guardianship and all persons entitled to the notice under section 5-310, 
19 subsection 5 or a subsequent order and no objection has been filed. 
20 6. Duties with respect to health care. In exercising the guardian's power under 
21 subsection 1, paragraph C to make health care decisions, a guardian shall: 
22 A. Involve the adult in decision making to the extent reasonably feasible, including, 
23 when practicable, by encouraging and supporting the adult in understanding the risks 
24 and benefits of health care options: 
25 B. Defer to a decision by an agent under a power of attorney for health care or an 
26 advance health care directive executed by the adult and cooperate to the extent 
27 feasible with the agent making the decision: and 
28 C. Take into account: 
29 (1) The risks and benefits of treatment options: and 
30 (2) The current and previous wishes and values of the adult, if known or 
31 reasonably ascertainable by the guardian. 
32 §5-315. Special limitations on guardian's power 
33 1. Limitations; health care; finances. Unless authorized by the court by specific 
34 order, a guardian for an adult does not have the power to revoke or amend a power of 
3 5 attorney for health care or an advance health care directive or power of attorney for 
3 6 finances executed by the adult. If a power of attorney for health care or an advance 
3 7 health care directive is in effect, unless there is a court order to the contraiy, a health care 
3 8 decision of an agent takes precedence over that of the guardian and the guardian shall 
Page 47 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 cooperate with the agent to the extent feasible. If a power of attorney for finances is in 
2 effect, unless there is a comt order to the contrary, a decision by the agent that the agent 
3 is authorized to make under the power of attorney for finances takes precedence over that 
4 of the guardian and the guardian shall cooperate with the agent to the extent feasible. 
5 2. Commitment to mental health facility. A guardian for an adult may not initiate 
6 the commitment of the adult to a mental health facility except in accordance with the 
7 State1s procedure for involuntary civil commitment under Title 34-B, chapter 3, 
8 subchapter 4, article 3. 
9 3. Restrictions on contact. A guardian for an adult may not restrict the ability of 
10 the adult to communicate, visit or interact with others, including receiving visitors or 
11 making or receiving telephone calls, personal mail or electronic communications, 
12 including through social media, or participating in social activities, unless: 
13 A. Authorized by the court by specific order; 
14 B. A protective order or a protective arrangement instead of guardianship is in effect 
15 that limits contact between the adult and a person; or 
16 C. The guardian has good cause to believe restriction is necessary because 
17 interaction with the person poses a risk of significant physical, psychological or 
18 financial haim to the adult and the restriction is: 
19 (1) For a period of not more than 7 business days if the person has a family or 
20 preexisting social relationship with the adult; or 
21 (2) For a period of not more than 60 days if the person does not have a family or 
22 preexisting social relationship with the adult. 
23 §5-316. Guardian's plan 
24 1. Plan; revision. The petitioner for appointment of a guardian for an adult shall file 
25 with the petition a plan for the care of the adult. When there is a subsequent change in 
26 circumstances, or the guardian seeks to deviate significantly from the plan previously 
27 filed, the guardian shall file with the court a revised plan for the care of the adult. The 
28 plan must be based on the needs of the adult and take into account the best interest of the 
29 adult as well as the adult's preferences, values and prior directions, to the extent known to 
30 or reasonably asce1tainable by the guardian. The plan must identify: 
31 A. The living arrangement, services and suppmts the guardian expects to arrange, 
32 facilitate or continue for the adult; 
33 B. Social and educational activities the guardian expects to facilitate on behalf of the 
34 adult; 
35 C. Any person with whom the adult has a relationship and any plan the guardian has 
36 for facilitating visits with the person; 
3 7 D. The anticipated nature and frequency of the guardian1s visits and communication 
3 8 with the adult; 
39 E. Goals for the adult including any goal related to the restoration of the adult's rights 
40 and how the guardian anticipates achieving the goals;

F. Whether the adult already has a plan in place and, if so, whether the guardian's

2. Notice of revised plan. A guardian shall give notice of the filing of a revised plan 
under subsection 1, along with a copy of the plan, to the adult subject to guardianship, all 
persons entitled to notice under section 5-310, subsection 5 or a subsequent order and 
other persons as the court determines. The notice must include a statement of the right to 
object to the revised plan and be given not later than 14 days after the filing. 
3. Objection to revised plan. An adult subject to guardianship and any person 
entitled under subsection 2 to receive notice and a copy of the guardian's plan may object 
to the revised plan. 
4. Court review of plan or revised plan; approval. The court shall review a 
guardian's plan or revised plan filed under subsection 1. In deciding whether to approve 
the plan or the revised plan the court shall consider an objection under subsection 3 and 
whether the plan or revised plan is consistent with the guardian's duties and powers under 
sections 5-313 and 5-314. The court may schedule a hearing on any revised plan 
submitted and may not approve any revised plan until 30 days after its filing. 
5. Copy of approved plan. After a guardian's plan under this section is approved by 
the court, the guardian shall provide a copy of the plan to the adult subject to 
guardianship, all persons entitled to notice under section 5-310, subsection 5 or a 
subsequent order and other persons as the court determines. 
§5-317. Guardian's report; monitoring of guardianship 
1. Report; contents. A guardian for an adult at least annually shall submit to the 
court a report in a record regarding the condition of the adult and accounting for money 
and other property in the guardian's possession or subject to the guardian's control. Each 
report must state or contain: 
A. The mental, physical and social condition of the adult; 
B. The living arrangements of the adult during the reporting period; 
C. A summary of the supported decision making, technological assistance, medical 
services, educational and vocational services and other supports and services 
provided to the adult and the guardian's opinion as to the adequacy of the adult's care; 
D. A summary of the guardian's visits with the adult, including the dates of the visits; 
E. Action taken on behalf of the adult; 
F. The extent to which the adult has participated in decision making; 
G. If the adult is living in a mental health facility or living in a facility that provides 
the adult with health care or other personal services, whether the guardian considers 
the facility's current plan for support, care, treatment or habilitation consistent with 
the adult's preferences, values, prior directions and best interest;

3 the guardian has received from an individual providing goods or services to the adult; 
4 I. If the guardian has delegated powers to an agent, the powers delegated and the 
5 reason for the delegation; 
6 J. Any business relation the guardian has with a person the guardian has paid or a 
7 person that has benefited from the property of the adult; 
8 K. A copy of the guardian's most recent plan and a statement whether the guardian 
9 has deviated from the plan and, if so, how the guardian has deviated and why;

11 M. A recommendation as to the need for continued guardianship and any 
12 recommended change in the scope of the guardianship; and 
13 N. Whether any coguardian or successor guardian appointed to serve when a 
14 designated future event occurs is alive and able to serve. 
15 2. Appointment of visitor. The court may appoint a visitor to review a report 
16 submitted under this section, interview the guardian or adult subject to guardianship or 
17 investigate any other matter involving the guardianship. 
18 3. Notice of filing of report; copy. Notice of the filing of a guardian's report under 
19 this section, together with a copy of the report, must be given to the adult subject to 
20 guardianship, all persons entitled to notice under section 5-310, subsection 5 or a 
21 subsequent order and any other person as the court determines. The notice and report 
22 must be given not later than 14 days after the filing of the report. 
23 4. System to monitor reports. The court shall establish a system for monitoring 
24 reports submitted under this section and review each report at least annually to determine 
25 whether: 
26 A. The report provides sufficient information to establish the guardian has complied 
27 with the guardian's duties; 
28 B. The guardianship should continue; and 
29 C. The guardian's requested fees, if any, should be approved. 
30 5. Noncompliance; modification or termination. If the court determines there is 
31 reason to believe a guardian for an adult has not complied with the guardian's duties or 
32 the guardianship should be modified or terminated, the court: 
33 A. Shall notify the adult, the guardian and all persons entitled to notice under section 
34 5-310, subsection 5 or a subsequent order; 
35 B. May require additional information from the guardian; 
36 C. May appoint a visitor to interview the adult or guardian or investigate any matter 
37 involving the guardianship; and

6. Fees not reasonable. If the court has reason to believe that fees requested by a 
guardian for an adult are not reasonable, the court shall hold a hearing to determine

7. Approval of report. A guardian for an adult may petition the court for approval 
of a report filed under this section. The court after review may approve the report. If, 
after notice and hearing, the court approves the report, there is a rebuttable presumption 
the report is accurate as to a matter adequately disclosed in the report. 
§5-318. Removal of guardian for adult; appointment of successor 
1. Removal; successor. The court may remove a guardian for an adult for failure to 
perform the guardian's duties or for other good cause and appoint a successor guardian to 
assume the duties of guardian. 
2. Hearing. The court shall conduct a hearing to determine whether to remove a 
guardian for an adult and appoint a successor on: 
A. Petition of the adult, the guardian or a person interested in the welfare of the adult 
that contains allegations that, if true, would support a reasonable belief that removal 
of the guardian and appointment of a successor may be appropriate, but the court may 
decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the same or substantially similar facts 
was filed within the preceding 6 months; 
B. Communication from the adult, the guardian or a person interested in the welfare 
of the adult that supports a reasonable belief that removal of the guardian and 
appointment of a successor may be appropriate; or 
C. Determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best interest of the 
adult. 
3. Notice. Notice of a petition under subsection 2, paragraph A must be given to the · 
adult subject to guardianship, the guardian and such other persons as the court 
determines. . · 
4. Attorney for the adult. An adult subject to guardianship who seeks to remove .. 
the guardian and have a successor appointed has a right to choose an attorney to represent 
the adult. If the adult subject to guardianship is not represented by an attorney, the court 
shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions as in section 5-305. The court shall 
award reasonable attorney's fees to the attorney for the adult as provided in section 5-119. 
5. Procedure to select successor. In selecting a successor guardian of an adult 
subject to guardianship, the court shall follow the procedures under section 5-309. 
6. Notice of appointment of successor. Not later than 30 days after appointing a 
successor guardian, the court shall give notice of the appointment to the adult subject to 
guardianship and all persons entitled to the notice under section 5-310, subsection 5 or a 
subsequent order.

1 §5-319. Termination or modification of guardianship for adult 
2 1. Petition for termination or modification. An adult subject to guardianship, the 
3 guardian for the adult or a person interested in the welfare of the adult may petition for: 
4 A. Termination of the guardianship on the ground that a basis for appointment under 
5 section 5-301 does not exist or termination would be in the best interest of the adult, 
6 or for other good cause; or 
7 B. Modification of the guardianship on the ground that the extent of protection or 
8 assistance granted is not appropriate, or for other good cause. 
9 2. Hearing. The court shall conduct a hearing to determine whether termination or 
10 modification of a guardianship of an adult is appropriate on: 
11 A. Petition under subsection 1 that contains allegations that, if true, would support a 
12 reasonable belief that termination or modification of the guardianship may be 
13 appropriate, but the comt may decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the 
14 same or substantially similar facts was filed within the preceding 6 months; 
15 B. Communication from the adult, the guardian or a person interested in the welfare 
16 of the adult that supports a reasonable belief that termination or modification of the 
17 guardianship may be appropriate, including because of a change in the functional 
18 needs of the adult or supports or services available to the adult; 
19 C. A report from a guardian or conservator that indicates that termination or 
20 modification may be appropriate because the functional needs of the adult or supports 
21 or services available to the adult have changed or a protective arrangement instead of 
22 guardianship or other less restrictive alternatives for meeting the adult's needs are 
23 available; or 
24 D. A determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best interest of the 
25 adult. 
26 3. Notice. Notice of a petition under subsection 2, paragraph A must be given to the 
27 adult subject to guardianship, the guardian and such other persons as the court 
28 determines. 
29 4. Termination. On presentation of prima facie evidence for termination of a 
30 guardianship for an adult, the court shall order termination unless it is proven that the 
31 basis for appointment of a guardian under section 5-301 is satisfied. 
32 5. Modification. The court shall modify the powers granted to a guardian for an 
33 adult if the powers arc excessive or inadequate due to a change in the abilities or 
34 limitations of the adult, the adult's supports or services or other circumstances. 
35 6. Procedure. Unless the comt otherwise orders for good cause, before terminating 
36 or modifying a guardianship for an adult, the comt shall follow the same procedures to 
37 safeguard the rights of the adult that apply to a petition for guardianship. 
38 7. Attorney for the adult. An adult subject to guardianship who seeks to terminate 
39 or modify the terms of the guardianship has a right to choose an attorney to represent the 
40 adult in this matter. If the adult is not represented by an attorney, the court shall appoint 
Page 52 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. (t,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
an attorney under the same conditions as in section 5-305. The court shall award 
reasonable attorney's fees to the attorney for the adult as provided in section 5-119.

4 CONSERVATORSHIP 
5 §5-401. Basis for appointment of conservator 
6 1. Conservator for minor; findings. On petition and after notice and hearing, the 
7 court may appoint a conservator for the property or financial affairs of a minor. if the 
8 court finds by a preponderance of evidence that: 
9 A. The minor owns money or property requiring management or protection that 
10 otherwise cannot be provided; or 
11 B. Appointment of a conservator is in the best interest of the minor and: 
12 (1) If the minor has a parent, the court gives weight to any recommendation of 
13 the minor's parent whether an appointment is in the best interest of the minor: and 
14 (2) Either: 
15 (a) The minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at 
16 unreasonable risk or hindered because of the minor's age: or 
17 (b) Appointment is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide money 
18 needed for the support, care. education, health or welfare of the minor. 
19 2. Conservator for adult; findings. On petition and after notice and hearing, the 
20 court may appoint a conservator for the property or financial affairs of an adult if the 
21 court determines by clear and convincing evidence that: 
22 A. The adult is unable to manage property or financial affairs because: 
23 (1) Of a limitation in the ability to receive and evaluate information or make or , 
24 communicate decisions even with the use of appropriate supportive services, : 
25 technological assistance and supported decision making: or 
26 (2) The adult is missing, detained or unable to return to the United States; 
27 B. Appointment is necessary to: 
28 (1) Avoid harm to the adult or significant dissipation of the property of the adult; 
29 or 
30 (2) Obtain or provide money needed for the support, care, education, health or 
31 welfare of the adult, or of an individual entitled to the adult's support, and 
32 protection is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide money for the purpose: 
33 and 
34 C. The respondent's identified needs cannot be met by less restrictive alternatives. 
35 3. Powers. The court shall grant a conservator only those powers necessitated by 
36 demonstrated limitations and needs of the respondent and enter orders that encourage the 
Page 53 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. p.,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
·. 1 l development of the respondent's maximum self-determination and independence. The 
2 court may not establish a full conservatorship if a limited conservatorship, protective 
3 arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternatives would meet 
4 the needs of the respondent. 
5 §5-402. Petition for appointment of conservator 
6 1. Petitioner. The following may petition for the appointment of a conservator: 
7 A. The individual for whom the order is sought; 
8 B. A person interested in the estate, financial affairs or welfare of the individual, 
9 including a person that would be adversely affected by lack of effective management 
10 of property and financial affairs of the individual; or 
11 C. The guardian of the individual. 
12 2. Contents. A petition under subsection 1 must set forth the petitioner's name, 
13 principal residence, current street address, if different, relationship to the respondent and 
14 interest in the appointment and state or contain the following to the extent known: 
15 A. The respondent's name, age, principal residence, cmTent street address, if 
16 different, and, if different, address of the dwelling in which it is proposed the 
17 respondent will reside if the petition is granted; 
18 B. The name and address of the respondent's: 
19 (1) Spouse or domestic partner or, if the respondent has none, any adult with 
20 whom the respondent has shared household responsibilities for more than 6 
21 months in the 12-month period before the filing of the petition; 
22 (2) Adult children or, if the respondent has none, each parent and adult sibling of 
23 the respondent or, if the respondent has none, at least one adult nearest in kinship 
24 to the respondent who can be found with reasonable diligence; and 
25 (3) Adult stepchildren whom the respondent actively parented during the 
26 stepchildren's minor years and with whom the respondent had an ongoing 
27 relationship within 2 years before filing of the petition; 
28 C. The name and cmTent address of each of the following, if applicable: 
29 (1) A person responsible for the care or custody of the respondent; 
30 (2) Any attomey cm1·ently representing the respondent; 
31 (3) The representative payee appointed by the United States Social Secmity 
32 Administration for the respondent; 
33 (4) A guardian or conservator acting for a respondent in this State or another 
34 jurisdiction; 
3 5 (5) A trnstee or custodian of a trust or custodianship of which the respondent is a 
36 beneficiary;

any person that had the primary care or custody of the minor for at least 730 
days during the 5 years preceding the filing of the petition; 
D. A general statement of the respondent's property with an estimate of its value, and 
the source and amount of other anticipated income or receipts; 
E. The reason conservatorship is necessary, including a brief description of: 
(1) The nature and extent of the respondent's alleged need; 
(2) If the petition alleges the respondent is missing, detained or unable to return 
to the United States, the relevant circumstances, including the time and nature of 
the disappearance or detention and any search or inquiry concerning the 
respondent's whereabouts; 
(3) Any protective arrangement instead of conservatorship 01· other less 
restrictive alternatives for meeting the respondent's alleged need which have been 
considered or implemented; 
(4) If no protective arrangement or other less restrictive alternatives have been 
considered or implemented, the reason they have not been considered or 
implemented; and 
(5) The reason a protective arrangement or other less restrictive alternatives are 
insufficient to meet the respondent's need; 
F. Whether the respondent needs an interpreter, translator or other form of support to 
communicate effectively with the court or understand court proceedings; 
G. Whether the petitioner seeks a limited conservatorship or a full conservatorship; 
H. If the petitioner seeks a full conservatorship, the reason a limited conservatorship 
or protective arrangement instead of conservatorship is not appropriate; 
Page 55 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" f}, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 · I. If the petition includes the name of a proposed conservator, the reason the 
2 proposed conservator should be appointed; and 
3 J. If the petition is for a limited conservatorship, a description of the property to be 
4 placed under the conservator's control and any other requested limitation on the 
5 authority of the conservator. 
6 3. Attorney for petitioner. A petition under subsection 1 must state the name, 
7 address, telephone number and bar registration number of an attorney representing the 
8 petitioner, if any. 
9 §5-403. Notice and hearing 
10 1. Date, time and place for hearing. On receipt of a petition for appointment of a 
11 conservator under section 5-402, the court shall set a date, time and place for hearing the 
12 petition. 
13 2. Notice to respondent. A copy of a petition under section 5-402 and notice of a 
14 hearing on the petition must be served personally on the respondent at least 14 days 
15 before the hearing. If the respondent's whereabouts are unknown or personal service 
16 cannot be made, service on the respondent must be made by substituted service or 
17 publication. The notice must inform the respondent of the respondent's rights at the 
18 hearing, including the right to an attorney and to attend the hearing. The notice must also 
19 include a description of the nature, purpose and consequences of granting the petition. 
20 Failure to serve the respondent with notice substantially complying with this subsection 
21 precludes the court from granting the petition. 
22 3. Notice to others. In a proceeding on a petition under section 5-402, notice of the 
23 hearing also must be given to the persons required to be listed in the petition under 
24 section 5-402, subsection 3, paragraphs A to C and any other person interested in the 
25 respondent's welfare as the court determines at least 14 days prior to the hearing. Failure 
26 to give notice under this subsection does not preclude the court from appointing a 
27 conservator. 
28 4. Notice of petition after order. Notice of a hearing on a petition that is filed after 
29 the appointment of a conservator and that seeks an order under this Part, together with a 
30 copy of the petition, must be given to the individual subject to conservatorship if the 
31 individual is 14 years of age or older and is not missing, detained or unable to return to 
32 the United States, the conservator and any other person as the court determines. 
33 §5-404. Petition for protective order 
34 1. Petition. The person to be protected, any person who is interested in the estate, 
35 affairs or welfare of the person to be protected, including the parent, guardian, custodian 
36 or domestic pa1tner of the person to be protected, or any person who would be adversely 
3 7 affected by lack of effective management of the propetiy and affairs of the person to be 
38 protected may petition for a protective order. 
39 2. Contents of petition. A petition under subsection 1 must contain such 
40 infonnation and be in such f01m as the Supreme Judicial Court by rule provides. 
41 3. Purpose; priority scheduling. A petition for a protective order made under oath 
42 may be used to initiate court consideration, accounting and remediation of the actions of

§5-405. Appointment and role of visitor 
1. Visitor for minor respondent. If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a 
conservator is a minor, the court may appoint a visitor to investigate a matter related to 
the petition or to inform the minor or a parent of the minor about the petition or a related 
matter. 
2. Visitor for adult respondent. If the respondent in a proceeding to appoint a . 
conservator is an adult, the court shall appoint a visitor unless the adult is represented by 
an attorney. The duties and reporting requirements of the visitor are limited to the relief 
requested in the petition. The visitor must be an individual having training or experience 
in the type of abilities, limitations and needs alleged in the petition. · 
3. Duties of visitor for adult respondent. A visitor appointed for an adult under 
subsection 2 shall interview the respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is 
best able to understand: 
A. Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature, purpose and 
effect of the proceeding, the respondent's rights at the hearing and the general powers 
and duties of a conservator: 
B. Determine the respondent's views about the appointment sought by the petitioner, 
including views about a proposed conservator, the conservator's proposed powers and 
duties and the scope and duration of the proposed conservatorship:

C. Inform the respondent of the respondent's right to employ and consult with an

attorney; and 
D. Inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the proceeding, including the 
respondent's attorney's fees, may be paid from the respondent's assets. 
4. Additional duties. In addition to the duties imposed by subsection 3, the visitor 
appointed for an adult under subsection 2 shall: 
A. Interview the petitioner and proposed conservator, if any; 
B. Review financial records of the respondent, if relevant to the visitor's 
recommendation under subsection 5, paragraph B; 
C. State whether the respondent's needs could be met by a less restrictive alternative, 
including a protective arrangement instead of conservatorship and, if so, identify the 
less restrictive alternative; and 
D. Investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter relating to the 
petition as the court directs. 
5. Report. A visitor appointed for an adult under subsection 2 shall file a report in a 
record with the court at least 10 days before any hearing on the petition. The repott must 
include: 
A. Whether or not the respondent wants to challenge any aspect of the proceeding or 
to seek any limitation on the conservator's powers; 
B. A recommendation whether an attorney should be appointed to represent the 
respondent; 
C. A recommendation: 
(1) Regarding the appropriateness of conservatorship, or whether a protective 
arrangement instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternatives for 
meeting the respondent's needs are available; 
(2) If a conservatorship is recommended, whether it should be full or limited; 
and 
(3) If a limited conservatorship is recommended, the powers to be granted to the 
conservator and the property that should be placed under the conservator's 
control; 
D. A statement of the qualifications of the proposed conservator and whether the 
respondent approves or disapproves of the proposed conservator; 
E. A recommendation whether a further professional evaluation under section 5-407 
is necessary; 
F. A statement whether the respondent is able to attend a hearing at the location court 
proceedings are typically conducted;
