5 §5-406. Appointment and role of attorney 
6 1. Attorney for respondent. The court shall appoint an attorney to represent a 
7 respondent in a proceeding on a petition under section 5-402 if: 
8 A. Requested by the respondent; 
9 B. Recommended by the visitor; 
10 C. The court determines that the respondent needs representation; or 
11 D. It comes to the court's attention that the respondent wishes to contest any aspect 
12 of the proceeding or to seek any limitation on the proposed conservator's powers. 
13 2. Duties of attorney. The attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding on a 
14 petition under section 5-402 shall: 
15 A. Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes: 
16 B. Advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably ascertainable: and 
17 C. If the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable, advocate for the result 
18 that is the least restrictive option in type, duration and scope, consistent with the 
19 respondent's interests. 
20 3. Attorney for parent of minor. The court may appoint an attorney to represent a 
21 parent of a minor who is the subject of a proceeding on a petition under section 5-402 if: 
22 A. The parent objects to appointment of a conservator; 
23 B. The court determines that counsel is needed to ensure that consent to appointment 
24 of a conservator is informed; or 
25 C. The court otherwise determines the parent needs representation. 
26 §5-407. Professional evaluation 
27 1. Evaluation; report. The respondent must be examined by a licensed physician or 
28 psychologist who is acceptable to the court, who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's 
29 alleged cognitive and functional abilities and limitations and who will not be advantaged 
30 or disadvantaged by a decision to grant the petition and does not otherwise have a conflict 
31 of interest. The individual conducting the evaluation shall file a report in a record with 
32 the court at least 10 days before any hearing on the petition. Unless otherwise directed by 
33 the court, the report must contain: 
34 A. A description of the nature, type and extent of the respondent's cognitive and 
35 functional abilities and limitations with regard to the management of the respondent's 
36 property and financial affairs; 
37 B. An evaluation of the respondent's mental and physical condition and, if 
38 appropriate, educational potential, adaptive behavior and social skills; 
Page 59 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT ,fa,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 C. A prognosis for improvement with regard to the ability to manage the 
2 respondent's property and financial affairs; and 
3 D. The date of the examination on which the report is based. 
4 2. Right to decline. The respondent has the right to decline to participate in an 
5 evaluation ordered under subsection 1. 
6 §5-408. Attendance and rights at hearing 
7 1. Attendance by respondent required. Except as otherwise provided in 
8 subsection 2, a hearing under section 5-403 may proceed only if the respondent attends 
9 the hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the 
10 location court proceedings typically are conducted, the court shall make reasonable 
11 efforts to hold the hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow 
12 the respondent to attend the hearing using real-time audiovisual technology. 
13 2. Hearing without respondent; findings. A hearing under section 5-403 may 
14 proceed without the respondent in attendance if the court finds by clear and convincing 
15 evidence that: 
16 A. The respondent consistently and repeatedly has refused to attend the hearing after 
17 having been fully infonned of the right to attend the hearing and the potential 
18 consequences of failing to do so; 
19 B. There is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and participate in the 
20 hearing even with appropriate supportive services and technological assistance; or 
21 C. The respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and attendance would 
22 be harmful to the minor. 
23 3. Assistance to respondent. The respondent may be assisted in a heating under 
24 section 5-403 by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing, assistive technology or 
25 an interpreter or translator, or a combination of these supports. If assistance would 
26 facilitate the respondent's participation in the hearing but is not otherwise available to the 
27 respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it. 
28 4. Attorney for respondent. The respondent has a right to choose an attorney to 
29 represent the respondent at a hearing under section 5-403. 
30 5. Rights of respondent at hearing. At a hearing under section 5-403, the 
31 respondent may: 
32 A. Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents; 
33 B. Examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and the visitor; and 
34 C. Otherwise participate in the hearing. 
35 6. Attendance by proposed conservator required. Unless excused by the court for 
36 good cause, the proposed conservator shall attend a hearing under section 5-403. 
37 7. Closed upon request; good cause. A hearing under section 5-403 must be closed 
3 8 on request of the respondent and a showing of good cause. 
Page 60 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" H· to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 8. Participation; best interest of respondent. Any person may request to 
2 participate in a hearing under section 5-403. The court may grant the request, with or 
3 without hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent will be served. 
4 The court may attach appropriate conditions to the person's participation. 
5 §5-409. Confidentiality of records 
6 1. Matter of public record; exceptions. The existence of a proceeding for or the 
7 existence of conservatorship is a matter of public record unless the court seals the record 
8 after: 
9 A. The respondent, the individual subject to conservatorship or the parent of a minor 
10 subject to conservatorship requests the record be sealed; and 
11 B. Either: 
12 (1) The petition for conservatorship is dismissed; or 
13 (2) The conservatorship is terminated. 
14 2. Access to records. An individual subject to a proceeding for a conservatorship, 
15 whether or not a conservator is appointed, an attorney designated by the individual and a 
16 person entitled to notice under section 5-411 or a subsequent order are entitled to access 
17 court records of the proceeding and resulting conservatorship, including the conservator's 
18 plan and report. In addition, a person for good cause may petition the coutt for access to 
19 court records of the conservatorship, including the conservator's plan and report. The 
20 court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the respondent or individual 
21 subject to conservatorship or furthers the public interest and does not endanger the 
22 welfare or financial interests of the respondent or individual. 
23 3. Reports; availability. A report under section 5-405 of a visitor or professional 
24 evaluation under section 5-407 is confidential and must be sealed on filing but is 
25 available to: 
26 A. The court; 
27 B. The individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation, without limitation as 
28 to use; 
29 C. The petitioner, visitor and petitioner's and respondent's attorneys, for purposes of 
30 the proceeding; 
31 D. An agent appointed under a power of attorney for finances in which the 
32 respondent is identified as the principal, unless the court orders otherwise; and 
33 E. Other persons when it is in the public interest or for a purpose the court orders for 
34 good cause. 
35 §5-410. Who may be conservator; priorities 
36 1. Priority for appointment. Except as otherwise provided in subsection 3, the 
3 7 court in appointing a conservator shall consider persons otherwise qualified in the 
38 following order of priority: 
Page 61 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. f1,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 A. A conservator, other than a temporary or emergency conservator, currently acting 
2 for the respondent in another jurisdiction; 
3 B. A person nominated as conservator by the respondent, including the respondent's 
4 most recent nomination made in a power of attorney for finances; 
5 C. An agent appointed by the respondent to manage the respondent's property under 
6 a power of attorney for finances; 
7 D. A spouse or domestic partner of the respondent: and 
8 E. A family member or other individual who has exhibited special care and concern 
9 for the respondent. 
10 2. Equal priority. With respect to persons having egual priority under subsection 1, 
11 the court shall select as conservator the person the court considers best qualified. In 
12 determining the best gualified person, the court shall consider the potential conservator's 
13 relationship with the respondent, the potential conservator's sldlls, the expressed wishes 
14 of the respondent, the extent to which the potential conservator and the respondent have 
15 similar values and preferences and the likelihood that the potential conservator will be 
16 able to satisfy the duties of a conservator successfully. 
17 3. Appointment based on best interest of respondent. The court, acting in the best 
18 interest of the respondent, may decline to appoint as conservator a person having priority 
19 under subsection 1 and appoint a person having a lower priority or no priority. 
20 4. Appointment prohibited; exceptions. A person that provides paid services to 
21 the respondent, or an individual who is employed by a person that provides paid services 
22 to the respondent or is the spouse, domestic patiner, parent or child of an individual who 
23 provides or is employed to provide paid services to the respondent, may not be appointed 
24 as conservator unless: 
25 A. The individual is related to the respondent by blood, man'iage or adoption; or 
26 B. The comi finds by clear and convincing evidence that the person is the best 
27 qualified person available for appointment and the appointment is in the best interest 
28 of the respondent. 
29 5. Long-term health care institution; exceptions. An owner, operator or employee 
30 of a long-term health care institution at which the respondent is receiving care may not be 
31 appointed as conservator unless the owner, operator or employee is related to the 
32 respondent by blood, marriage or adoption. 
33 §5-411. Order of appointment 
34 1. Conservator for minor; findings. A court order appointing a conservator for a 
35 minor must include findings to support appointment of a conservator and, if a full 
36 conservatorship is granted, the reason a limited conservatorship would not meet the 
37 identified needs of the minor. 
38 2. Conservator for adult; findings. A court order appointing a conservator for an 
39 adult must include a clear finding that: 
40 A. The identified needs of the respondent cannot be met by a protective arrangement 
41 instead of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternatives, including use of

B. Clear and convincing evidence established the respondent was given proper notice 
of the hearing on the petition. 
3. Basis for full conservatorship. A court order establishing a full conservatorship 
for an adult clearly must state the basis for granting a full conservatorship and include 
specific findings to support the conclusion that a limited conservatorship would not meet 
the functional needs of the adult. 
4. Limited conservatorship; powers granted to conservator. A court order 
establishing a limited conservatorship must state clearly the property placed under the 
control of the conservator and the powers granted to the conservator. 
5. Notice; access to reports and plans. The comt shall, as part of an order 
establishing a conservatorship, identify any person that subsequently is entitled to: 
A. Notice of the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship; 
B. Notice of a sale of or surrender of a lease to the primary dwelling of the individual 
subject to conservatorship; 
C. Notice that the conservator has delegated any power that requires court approval 
under section 5-414 or substantially all powers of the conservator; 
D. Notice that the conservator will be unavailable to perform the conservator's duties 
for more than one month; 
E. Copies of the conservator's plan and report; 
F. Access to comt records pertaining to the conservatorship; 
G. A transaction involving a substantial conflict between the conservator's fiduciary 
duties and personal interests; 
H. Notice of the death or significant change in the condition of the individual subject 
to conservatorship; 
I. Notice that the court has limited or modified the powers of the conservator; and 
J. Notice of the conservator's removal. 
6. Entitled to notice; exceptions. If an individual subject to conservatorship is an 
adult, the spouse, domestic partner and adult children of the adult subject to 
conservatorship are entitled under subsection 5 to notice unless the court determines 
notice would be contrary to the preferences or prior directions of the adult subject to 
conservatorship or not in the best interest of the adult subject to conservatorship. 
7. Notice when minor is subject to conservatorship. If an individual subject to 
conservatorship is a minor, each parent and adult sibling of the minor is entitled under 
subsection 5 to notice unless the court determines notice would not be in the best interest 
of the minor.

1 §5-412. Notice of order of appointment; rights 
2 1. Notice of appointment, order; rights. A conservator appointed under section 
3 5-401 shall give to the individual subject to conservatorship and to all other persons given 
4 notice under section 5-403 a copy of the order of appointment, together with a notice of 
5 the right to request termination or modification. The order and notice must be given not 
6 later than 14 days after the appointment. 
7 2. Notice if person missing. If a conservator is appointed under section 5-401, 
8 subsection 2, paragraph A, subparagraph (2) and the individual subject to conservatorship 
9 is missing, notice under subsection 1 to the individual is not required. 
10 §5-413. Emergency conservator 
11 1. Appointment; findings. On petition by a person interested in an individual's 
12 welfare or on its own after a petition has been filed under section 5-402, the comt may 
13 appoint an emergency conservator for the individual if the court finds: 
14 A. Appointment of an emergency conservator is likely to prevent substantial and 
15 irreparable harm to the respondent's property or financial interests; 
16 B. No other person appears to have authority and willingness to act in the 
17 circumstances; and 
18 C. There is reason to believe that a basis for appointment of a conservator under 
19 section 5-401 may exist. 
20 2. Duration of emergency conservatorship. The duration of authority of an 
21 emergency conservator may not exceed 60 days and the emergency conservator may 
22 exercise only the powers specified in the order. The emergency conservator's authority 
23 may be extended once for not more than 120 days if the court finds that the conditions for 
24 appointment of an emergency conservator in subsection 1 continue. 
25 3. Notice before petition. Prior to filing a petition under this section, notice must be 
26 provided as follows. 
27 A. The petitioner shall provide notice orally or in writing to the following: 
28 (1) The respondent and the respondent's spouse, parents, adult children and any 
29 domestic partner known to the court; 
30 (2) Any person who is serving as guardian or conservator or who has care and 
31 custody of the respondent; and 
32 (3) In case no other person is notified under subparagraph (1), at least one of the 
33 closest adult relatives of the respondent or, if there are none, an adult friend, if 
34 any can be found. 
35 B. Notice under paragraph A must include the following information: 
36 (1) The temporary authority that the petitioner is requesth1g; 
37 (2) The location and telephone number of the court in which the petition is being 
3 8 filed; and

(3) The name of the petitioner and the intended date of filing. 
C. The petitioner shall state in an affidavit the date, time, location and method of 
providing the required notice under paragraph A and to whom the notice was 
provided. The court shall make a determination as to the adequacy of the method of 
providing notice and whether the petitioner complied with the notice requirements of 
this subsection. The requirements of section 5-410 do not apply to this section. 
D. Notice is not required under this subsection in the following circumstances: 
(1) Giving notice would place the respondent at substantial risk of abuse, neglect 
or exploitation; 
(2) Notice, if provided, would not be effective; or 
(3) The court determines that there is good cause not to provide notice. 
E. If, prior to filing the petition, the petitioner does not provide notice as required 
under this subsection, the petitioner must state in the affidavit under paragraph C the 
reasons for not providing notice. If notice has not been provided, the court shall 
make a determination as to the sufficiency of the reason for not providing notice 
before issuing a temporary order. 
4. Appointment without notice and hearing. The court may appoint an emergency 
conservator without notice and a hearing only if the court finds from an affidavit or 
testimony that the respondent's property or financial interests will be substantially and 
irreparably harmed before a hearing on the appointment can be held. If the court appoints 
an emergency conservator without notice and a hearing, the court shall, not later than 48 
hours after the appointment, notify the respondent, the respondent's attorney and other 
persons as the court determines of the appointment. If a person objects to the 
appointment, the court shall hold a hearing within 14 days. 
5. Not a determination. Appointment of an emergency conservator under this 
section is not a determination that the conditions required for appointment of a 
conservator under section 5-401 have been satisfied. 
6. Removal; report; application. The court may remove an emergency conservator 
appointed under this section at any time. The emergency conservator shall make any 
report the court requires. In other respects, the provisions of this Part concerning 
conservators apply to an emergency conservator appointed under this section. 
§5-414. Powers of conservator requiring court approval 
1. Powers requiring specific authorization; notice. Except as otherwise ordered 
by the court, a conservator must give notice to persons entitled to notice under section 
5-403, subsection 4 and receive specific authorization by the court before the conservator 
may exercise with respect to the conservatorship the power to: 
A. Make gifts, except those of de minimis value; 
B. Sell, encumber an interest in or surrender a lease to the primary dwelling of the 
individual subject to conservatorship; 
Page 65 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" f), to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 C. Convey, release or disclaim contingent or expectant interests in propeey, 
2 including marital property and any right of survivorship incident to joint tenancy; 
3 D. Exercise or release a power of appointment; 
4 E. Create a revocable or irrevocable trust of property of the conservatorship estate, 
5 whether or not the trust extends beyond the duration of the conservatorship, or revoke 
6 or amend a trust revocable by the individual subject to conservatorship; 
7 F. Exercise a right to elect an option or change a beneficiary under an insurance 
8 policy or annuity or surrender the policy or annuity for its cash value; 
9 G. Exercise a right to an elective share in the estate of a deceased spouse or domestic 
10 partner of the individual subject to conservatorship or to renounce or disclaim a 
11 property interest; 
12 H. Grant a creditor a priority for payment over creditors of the same or higher class 
13 if the creditor is providing property or services used to meet the basic living and care 
14 needs of the individual subject to conservatorship and preferential treatment 
15 otherwise would be impermissible under section 5-428, subsection 5; and 
16 I. Make, modify, amend or revoke the will of the individual subject to 
17 conservatorship in compliance with the laws of the State governing executing wills. 
18 2. Approval based on decision of individual. In approving a conservator's exercise 
19 of the powers listed in subsection 1, the court shall consider primarily the decision the 
20 individual subject to conservatorship would make if able, to the extent the decision can be 
21 ascertained. 
22 3. To determine decision of individual. To determine under subsection 2 the 
23 decision the individual subject to conservatorship would make if able, the court shall 
24 consider the individual's prior or current directions, preferences, opinions, values and 
25 actions, to the extent actually known or reasonably ascertainable. The court also shall 
26 consider: 
27 A. The financial needs of the individual subject to conservatorship and individuals 
28 who are in fact dependent on the individual subject to conservatorship for support, 
29 and the interest of creditors; 
30 B. Possible reduction of income, estate, inheritance or other tax liabilities; 
31 C. Eligibility for governmental assistance; 
32 D. The previous pattern of giving or level of support provided by the individual 
33 subject to conservatorship; 
34 E. Any existing estate plan or lack of estate plan of the individual subject to 
35 conservatorship; 
36 F. The life expectancy of the individual subject to conservatorship and the 
37 probability that the conservatorship will terminate before the individual's death; and 
38 G. Any other relevant factors. 
39 4. Power of attorney for finances. A conservator may not revoke or amend a 
40 power of attorney for fmances executed by the individual subject to conservatorship. If a 
Page 66 -128LR0452(02)-1

1 power of attorney for finances is in effect, a decision of the agent takes precedence over 
2 that of the conservator, unless there is a court order to the contrary. 
3 §5-415. Petition for order subsequent to appointment 
4 An individual subject to conservatorship or a person interested in the welfare of the 
5 individual may file a petition in the court for an order: 
6 1. Bond or collateral. Requiring the conservator to furnish bond or collateral or 
7 additional bond or collateral or allowing a reduction in a bond or collateral previously 
8 furnished; 
9 
10 2. Accounting. 
conservatorship estate; Requiring an accounting for the administration of the 
11 3. Distribution. Directing distribution: 
12 4. Removal; temporary or successor. Removing the conservator and appointing a 
13 temporary or successor conservator; 
14 5. Modification. Modifying the type of appointment or powers granted to the 
15 conservator, if the extent of protection or management previously granted is currently 
16 excessive or insufficient to meet the individual's needs, including because the individual's 
17 abilities or supports have changed; 
18 6. Inventory, plan or report. Rejecting or modifying the conservator's inventory, 
19 plan or report; or 
20 7. Other relief. Granting other appropriate relief. 
21 §5-416. Bond or alternative asset-protection arrangement 
22 1. Bond or alternative asset-protection arrangement required. The court shall 
23 require a conservator to furnish a bond with a surety the court specifies, or require an 
24 alternative asset-protection arrangement, conditioned on faithful discharge of all duties of 
25 the conservator. The court may waive the requirement only if the court finds that a bond 
26 or other asset-protection arrangement is not necessary to protect the interests of the 
27 individual subject to conservatorship. The court may not waive the requirement if the 
28 conservator is in the business of serving as a conservator and is being paid for the 
29 conservator's service except as provided by subsection 3. 
30 2. Amount of bond; collateral. Unless the court directs otherwise, the bond 
31 required under this section must be in the amount of the aggregate capital value of the 
32 conservatorship estate, plus one year's estimated income, less the value of property 
33 deposited under arrangement requiring a court order for its removal and real property the 
34 conservator lacks power to sell or convey without specific court authorization. The court, 
35 in place of surety on a bond, may accept collateral for the performance of the bond, 
36 including a pledge of securities or a mortgage ofreal property. 
37 3. Bond not required. A regulated financial service institution qualified to do trust 
3 8 business in this State need not give a bond.

1 §5-417. Terms and reguirements of bond 
2 1. Bond requirements. The following rules apply to the bond required under 
3 section 5-416. 
4 A. Except as otherwise provided by the bond, the surety and the conservator are 
5 jointly and severally liable. 
6 B. By executing a bond provided by a conservator, a surety submits to the 
7 jurisdiction of the court that issued letters of office to the conservator in a proceeding 
8 pertaining to the duties of the conservator in which the surety is named as a party. 
9 Notice of the proceeding must be given to the surety at the address shown in the court 
10 records at the place where the bond is filed and any other address of the surety then 
11 known to the person required to provide the notice. 
12 C. On petition of a successor conservator or any person affected by a breach of the 
13 obligation of the bond, a proceeding may be brought against a surety for breach of the 
14 obligation of the bond. 
15 D. A proceeding against the bond may be brought until liability under the bond is 
16 exhausted. 
17 2. Proceeding against surety. A proceeding may not be brought against a surety of 
18 a bond under this section on a matter as to which a proceeding against the conservator is 
19 barred. 
20 3. Notice of nonrenewal. The surety or sureties of the bond must immediately serve 
21 notice to the court and to the individual under conservatorship if the bond is not renewed 
22 by the conservator. 
23 §5-418. Duties of conservator 
24 1. Duties as fiduciary. A conservator is a fiduciary and has a duty of prudence and 
25 duty ofloyalty to the individual subject to conservatorship. 
26 2. Promote self-determination. A conservator shall promote the self-determination 
27 of the individual subject to conservatorship and, to the extent feasible, encourage the 
28 individual to participate in decisions, act on the individual's own behalf and develop or 
29 regain the capacity to manage the individual's personal affairs. 
30 3. Decision of individual. In making a decision on behalf of the individual subject 
31 to conservatorship, the conservator shall make the decision the conservator reasonably 
32 believes the individual would make if able, unless doing so would fail to preserve the 
33 resources needed to maintain the individual's well-being and lifestyle or otherwise 
34 umeasonably harm or endanger the welfare or personal or financial interests of the 
35 individual. To determine the decision the individual would make if able, the conservator 
36 shall consider the individual's prior or current directions, preferences, opinions, values 
37 and actions to the extent actually known or reasonably ascetiainable by the conservator. 
38 4. Best interest of individual. If a conservator cannot make a decision under 
3 9 subsection 3 because the conservator does not know and cannot reasonably determine the 
40 decision that the individual subject to conservatorship probably would make if able, or 
41 the conservator reasonably believes the decision the conservator believes the individual 
Page 68 -128LR0452(02)-l 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
( 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "!1·,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 would make would fail to preserve resources needed to maintain the individual's well-
2 being and lifestyle or otherwise would unreasonably harm or endanger the welfare of the 
3 individual, the conservator shall act in accordance with the best interest of the individual. 
4 In determining the best interest of the individual, the conservator shall consider: 
5 A. Inf01mation received from professionals and persons that demonstrate sufficient 
6 interest in the welfare of the individual; 
7 B. Other information the conservator believes the individual would have considered 
8 if the individual were able to act; and 
9 C. Other factors a reasonable person in the circumstances of the individual would 
10 consider, including consequences for others. 
11 5. Prudent investor standard. Except when inconsistent with the conservator's 
12 duties under subsections 1 to 4, a conservator shall invest and manage the conservatorship 
13 estate as a prudent investor would, by considering: 
14 A. The circumstances of the individual subject to conservatorship and the 
15 conservatorship estate: 
16 B. General economic conditions; 
17 C. The possible effect of inflation or deflation; 
18 D. The expected tax consequences of an investment decision or strategy; 
19 E. The role of each investment or course of action in relation to the conservatorship 
20 estate as a whole; 
21 F. The expected total return from income and appreciation of capital; 
22 G. The need for liquidity, regularity of income and preservation or appreciation of 
23 capital; and 
24 H. The special relationship or value, if any, of specific property to the individual 
25 subject to conservatorship. 
26 6. Propriety of investment and management. The propriety of a conservator's 
27 investment and management of the conservatorship estate is determined in light of the 
28 facts and circumstances existing when the conservator decides or acts and not by 
29 hindsight. ·· 
30 7. Reasonable effort to verify facts. A conservator shall make a reasonable effort 
31 to verify facts relevant to the investment and management of the conservatorship estate. 
32 8. Special skills or expertise. A conservator that has special skills or expertise, or is 
33 named conservator in reliance on the conservator's representation of special skills or 
34 expertise, has a duty to use the special sldlls or expertise in carrying out the conservator's 
35 duties. 
36 9. Consistent with estate plan and other instrument. In investing, selecting 
3 7 specific property for distribution and invoking a power of revocation or withdrawal for 
38 the use or benefit of the individual subject to conservatorship, a conservator shall 
39 consider any estate plan of the individual known or reasonably ascertainable to the 
Page 69 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. p,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
'1 conservator and may examine the will or other donative, nominative or other appointive 
2 instrument of the individual. 
3 10. Insurance. A conservator shall maintain insurance on the insurable real and 
4 personal property of the individual subject to conservatorship, unless the conservatorship 
5 estate lacks sufficient funds to pay for insurance or a court issues an order finding: 
6 A. The property lacks sufficient equity; or 
7 B. Insuring the property would unreasonably dissipate the conservatorship estate or 
8 otherwise not be in the best interest of the individual subject to conservatorship. 
9 11. Cooperation, power of attorney for finances. If a power of attorney for 
10 finances is in effect, a conservator shall cooperate with the agent to the extent feasible. 
11 12. Digital assets. A conservator has access to and authority over a digital asset of 
12 the individual subject to conservatorship to the extent provided by the Revised Uniform 
13 Fiduciary Access to Digital Assets Act or by court order. 
14 13. Adult becomes capable. A conservator of an adult shall notify the court if the 
15 condition of the adult subject to conservatorship has changed so that the adult is capable 
16 of exercising rights previously removed immediately upon learning of the change. 
17 §5-419. Conservator's plan 
18 1. Plan; revision. The petitioner for appointment as conservator for an adult shall 
19 file with the petition a plan for protecting, managing, expending and distributing the 
20 assets of the conservatorship estate. When there is a change in circumstances or when the 
21 conservator seeks to deviate significantly from the conservator's plan previously filed, the 
22 conservator shall file with the court a revised plan for protecting, managing, expending 
23 and distributing the assets of the conservatorship estate. The plan must be based on the 
24 needs of the individual subject to conservatorship and take into account the best interest 
25 of the individual as well as the individual's preferences, values and prior directions, to the 
26 extent known to or reasonably asce1iainable by the conservator. The conservator shall 
27 include in the plan: 
28 A. A budget setting forth projected expenses and resources, including an estimate of 
29 the total amount of fees the conservator anticipates charging per year and a statement 
30 or list of the amount the conservator proposes to charge for each service the 
31 conservator anticipates providing to the individual subject to conservatorship; 
32 B. How the conservator will involve the individual subject to conservatorship in 
33 decisions about management of the conservatorship estate; 
34 C. Any step the conservator plans to take to develop or restore the ability of the 
35 individual subject to conservatorship to manage the conservatorship estate; and 
36 D. An estimate of the duration of the conservatorship. 
37 2. Notice of revised plan. A conservator shall give notice of the filing of a revised 
38 plan under subsection 1, along with a copy of the revised plan, to the individual subject to 
39 conservatorship, all persons entitled to notice under section 5-411, subsection 5 or a 
40 subsequent order and other persons as the court determines. The notice must be given not 
41 later than 14 days after the filing.

3. Objection to revised plan. An individual subject to conservatorship and any 
person entitled under subsection 2 to receive notice and a copy of the conservator's 
revised plan may object to the revised plan. 
4. Court review of plan or revised plan; approval. The court shall review a 
conservator's plan or revised plan filed under subsection 1. In deciding whether to 
approve the plan or revised plan, the court shall consider any objection under subsection 
3 and whether the plan or revised plan is consistent with the conservator's duties and 
powers. The court may not approve the plan or revised plan until 30 days after its filing. 
5. Copy of approved plan. After a conservator's plan or revised plan under this 
section is approved by the court, the conservator shall provide a copy of the plan or 
revised plan to the individual subject to conservatorship, all persons entitled to notice 
under section 5-411, subsection 5 or a subsequent order and other persons as the court 
determines. 
§5-420. Inventory; records 
1. Inventory. Not later than 60 days after appointment, a conservator shall prepare 
and file with the appointing court a detailed inventory of the conservatorship estate, 
together with an oath or affirmation that the inventory is believed to be complete and 
accurate as far as information permits. 
2. Notice of filing of inventory. A conservator shall give notice of the filing of an 
inventory to the individual subject to conservatorship, all persons entitled to notice under 
section 5-411, subsection 5 or a subsequent order and other persons as the court 
determines. The notice must be given not later than 14 days after the filing. 
3. Records. A conservator shall keep records of the administration of the 
conservatorship estate and make them available for examination on reasonable request of 
the individual subject to conservatorship, a guardian of the individual or any person as the 
conservator or the court determines. 
§5-421. Administrative powers of conservator not requiring court approval 
1. Powers unless limited; powers of trustee. Except as otherwise provided in 
section 5-414 or qualified or limited in the court's order of appointment and stated in the 
letters of office, a conservator has all powers granted in this section and any additional 
powers granted to a trustee by law of this State other than this Part. 
2. Powers of conservator. A conservator, acting reasonably and consistent with the 
fiduciaty duties of the conservator to accomplish the purpose of the appointment, without 
specific court authorization or confirmation, may: 
A. Collect. hold and retain property included in the conservatorship estate, including 
property in which the conservator has a personal interest and real property in another 
state, until the conservator determines disposition of the property should be made; 
B. Receive additions to the conservatorship estate; 
C. Continue or participate in the operation of a business or other enterprise; 
D. Acquire an undivided interest in property included in the conservatorship estate in 
which the conservator, in a fiduciary capacity, holds an undivided interest;

§5-422. Distribution from conservatorship estate 
Except as otherwise provided in section 5-414 or qualified or limited in the court's 
order of appointment and stated in the letters of office, and unless contrary to a 
conservator's plan filed under section 5-419, a conservator may expend or distribute 
income or principal of the conservatorship estate without specific court authorization or 
confirmation for the support, care, education, health or welfare of the individual subject 
to conservatorship or an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual subject to 
conservatorship, including the payment of child or spousal support, in accordance with 
the following rules. 
1. Appropriate standard. A conservator shall consider a recommendation relating 
to the appropriate standard of support, care, education, health or welfare for the individual 
subject to conservatorship, or an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual 
subject to conservatorship, made by a gµardian of the individual subject to 
conservatorship, if any, and, if the individual subject to conservatorship is a minor, a 
recommendation made by a gµardian or parent of the minor. 
Page 73 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"().,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 2. Liability for distribution. A conservator acting in compliance with the 
2 conservator's duties under section 5-418 is not liable for a distribution made based on a 
3 recommendation under subsection 1 unless the conservator knows the distribution is not 
4 in the best interest of the individual subject to conservatorship. 
5 3. Considerations for expenditure, distribution. In making an expenditure or 
6 distribution under this subsection, the conservator shall consider: 
7 A. The size of the conservatorship estate, the estimated duration of the 
8 conservatorship and the likelihood the individual subject to conservatorship, at some 
9 future time, may be fully self-sufficient and able to manage the individual's financial 
10 affairs and the conservatorship estate; 
11 B. The accustomed standard of living of the individual subject to conservatorship 
12 and an individual who is in fact dependent on the individual subject to 
13 conservatorship; 
14 C. Other money or source used for the support of the individual subject to 
15 conservatorship; and 
16 D. The preferences, values and prior directions of the individual subject to 
17 conservatorship. 
18 4. Compensation or reimbursement. Money expended or distributed under this 
19 subsection may be paid by the conservator to any person, including the individual subject 
20 to conservatorship, as reimbursement for expenditures the conservator might have made, 
21 or in advance for services to be rendered to the individual subject to conservatorship if it 
22 is reasonable to expect the services will be performed and advance payment is customary 
23 or reasonably necessary under the circumstances. 
24 §5-423. Conservator's report and accounting; monitoring 
25 1. Report. A conservator shall file a report in a record with the court regarding the 
26 administration of the conservatorship estate annually unless the court otherwise directs, 
27 on resignation or removal, on termination of the conservatorship and at any other time as 
28 the court directs. 
29 2. Contents. A report under subsection 1 must state or contain: 
30 A. An accounting that contains a list of property included in the conservatorship 
31 estate and of the receipts, disbursements, liabilities and distributions during the period 
32 for which the report is made; 
33 B. A list of the services provided to the individual subject to conservatorship; 
34 C. A copy of the conservator's most recently approved plan and a statement whether 
35 the conservator has deviated from the plan and, if so, how and why the conservator 
36 has deviated; 
37 D. Any recommended change in the conservatorship, including its scope and 
3 8 whether the conservatorship needs to continue; 
39 E. Annual credit report of the individual subject to conservatorship and to the extent 
40 feasible, a copy of the most recent reasonably available financial statements 
41 evidencing the status of bank accounts, investment accounts and mortgages or other

conservatorship or conservator and investigate any matter involving the conservatorship 
as the court directs. In connection with the report, the court may order the conservator to 
submit the conservatorship estate to appropriate examination in a manner the court 
directs. 
4. Notice of report; copy. Notice of the filing under this section of a conservator's 
report, together with a copy of the report, must be provided to the individual subject to 
conservatorship, all persons entitled to notice under section 5-411, subsection 5 or a 
subsequent order, and a person the court determines is entitled to the report. 
Notwithstanding section 5-409, the credit report provided pursuant to subsection 2, 
paragraph E is confidential and may not be provided with the rest of the conservator's 
report except to the individual subject to conservatorship. The notice and report must be 
given not later than 14 days after filing.

monitoring a conservator's plan and report and review the plan and report not less than 
annually to determine whether: 
A. The plan and report provide sufficient information to establish the conservator has 
complied with the conservator's duties; 
B. The conservatorship should continue; and 
C. The conservator's requested ~ees, if any, should be approved. 
6. Noncompliance. If the court determines there is reason to believe the conservator 
has not complied with the conservator's duties or the conservatorship should not continue, 
the court: 
A. Shall notify the conservator, the individual subject to conservatorship and all

B. · May require additional information from the conservator;

approve the report or accounting. An order, after notice and hearing, approving a final 
report or accounting discharges the conservator from all liabilities, claims and causes of 
action by a person given notice of the report or accounting and the hearing as to a matter 
adequately disclosed in the report or accounting. 
§5-424. Attempted transfer of property by individual subject to conservatorship 
1. Intetest not transferable or assignable; not subject to claims. The interest of 
an individual subject to conservatorship in property included in the conservatorship estate 
is not transferable or assignable by the individual and is not subject to levy, garnishment 
or similar process for claims against the individual unless allowed under section 5-428. 
2. Contract void against individual and property. If an individual subject to 
conservatorship enters into a contract after having the right to enter the contract removed 
by the court, the contract is void against the individual and the individual's property but is 
enforceable against the person that contracted with the individual. 
3. Protection of 3rd parties. A 3rd party that deals with an individual subject to 
conservatorship with respect to property included in the conservatorship estate is entitled 
to protection provided by law of this State other than this Act. 
§5-425. Ttansaction involving conflict of interest 
A transaction involving a conservatorship estate that is affected by a substantial 
conflict between the conservator's fiduciary duties and personal interests is voidable 
unless the transaction is authorized by the court by specific order after notice to all 
persons entitled to notice under section 5-411, subsection 5 or a subsequent order. A 
transaction affected by a substantial conflict between fiducia1y duties and personal 
interests includes a sale, encumbrance or other transaction involving the conservatorship 
estate entered into by the conservator, an individual with whom the conservator resides, 
the spouse, domestic partner, descendant, sibling, agent or attorney of the conservator, or 
a corporation or other enterprise in which the conservator has a substantial beneficial 
interest. 
§5-426. Protection of person dealing with conservator 
1. Protection of 3td party. A person that assists or deals with a conservator in good 
faith and for value in any transaction, other than one requiring a court order under section 
Page 76 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"(}. to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 5-414, is protected as though the conservator properly exercised the power in question. 
2 Knowledge by a person that the person is dealing with a conservator does not alone 
3 require the person to inquire into the existence of the authority of the conservator or the 
4 propriety of the conservator's exercise of authority, but restrictions on authority that are 
5 stated in letters of office, or as otherwise provided by law, are effective as to the person. 
6 A person that pays or delivers property to a conservator is not responsible for proper 
7 application of the property. 
8 2. Application of protection. Protection under subsection 1 extends to a procedural 
9 irregularity or jurisdictional defect in the proceeding leading to the issuance of letters of 
10 office and is not a substitute for protection provided to a person that assists or deals with 
11 a conservator by comparable provisions in law of this State other than this Act relating to 
12 commercial transactions or simplifying transfers of securities by fiduciaries. 
13 §5-427. Death of individual subject to conservatorship 
14 1. Delivery of will. If an individual subject to conservatorship dies, the conservator 
15 shall deliver to the court for safekeeping any will of the individual in the conservator's 
16 possession and inform the personal representative named in the will if feasible, or if not 
17 feasible a beneficiary named in the will, of the delivery. 
18 2. Powers and duties of personal representative; notice. If 40 days after the death 
19 of an individual subject to conservatorship no personal representative has been appointed 
20 and an application or petition for appointment is not before the court, the conservator may 
21 apply to exercise the powers and duties of a personal representative to administer and 
22 distribute the decedent's estate. The conservator shall give notice to a person nominated 
23 as personal representative by a will of the decedent of which the conservator is aware and 
24 to all of the decedent's heirs and all devisees of the will, if any. The court may grant the 
25 application if there is no objection and endorse the letters of office to note that the 
26 individual formerly subject to conservatorship is deceased and the conservator has 
27 acquired the powers and duties of a personal representative. 
28 3. Effect of appointment as personal representative. Issuance of an order under 
29 this section has the effect of an order of appointment of a personal representative under 
30 section 3-308 and Article 3, Parts 6 to 10. 
31 4. Distribution; discharge. On the death of an individual subject to 
32 conservatorship, the conservator shall conclude the administration of the conservatorship 
33 estate by distributing property subject to conservatorship to the individual's successors. 
34 Not later than 30 days after distribution, the conservator shall file a final report and 
3 5 petition for discharge. 
36 §5-428. Presentation and allowance of claim 
37 1. Claims against estate or protected person. A conservator may pay, or secure by 
38 encumbering . property included in the conservatorship estate, a claim against the 
39 conservatorship estate or the individual subject to conservatorship arising before or 
40 during the conservatorship on presentation and allowance in accordance with the 
41 priorities under subsection 4. A claimant may present a claim by: 
42 A. Sending or delivering to the conservator a statement in a record of the claim, 
43 indicating its basis, the name and address of the claimant and the amount claimed; or

B. Filing with the court a record of the claim, in a form acceptable to the court, and 
sending or delivering a copy of the statement to the conservator. 
2. Presented claim; allowance; disallowance. A claim under subsection 1 is 
presented on receipt by the conservator of the statement of claim by the conservator or 
the filing with the court of the claim, whichever first occurs. A presented claim is 
allowed if it is not disallowed by the conservator in a record sent or delivered to the 
claimant not later than 60 days after its presentation. Before payment the conservator 
may change an allowance of the claim to a disallowance in whole or in part, but not after 
allowance under a court order or order directing payment of the claim. Presentation of a 
claim tolls the running of a statute of limitations that has not expired relating to the claim 
until 30 days after its disallowance. 
3. Unpaid claim. A claimant whose claim under subsection 1 has not been paid may 
petition the court to determine the claim at any time before it is baned by a statute of 
limitations, and the court may order its allowance, payment or security by encumbering 
property included in the conservatorship estate. If a proceeding is pending against the 
individual subject to conservatorship at the time of appointment of the conservator or is 
initiated thereafter, the moving party shall give the conservator notice of the proceeding if 
it could result in creating a claim against the conservatorship estate. 
4. Distribution; order. If a conservatorship estate is likely to be exhausted before 
all existing claims are paid, the conservator shall distribute the estate in money or in kind 
in payment of claims in the following order: 
A. Costs and expenses of administration; 
B. A claim of the Federal Government or State Government having priority under 
law other than this Act; 
C. A claim incurred by the conservator for support, care, education, health or welfare 
previously provided to the individual subject to conservatorship or an individual who 
is in fact dependent on the individual subject to conservatorship; 
D. A claim arising before the conservatorship; and 
E. All other claims. 
5. Preference of claims. Preference may not be given in the payment of a claim 
under subsection 4 over another claim of the same class. A claim due and payable may 
not be prefened over a claim not due unless: 
A. Doing so would leave the conservatorship estate without sufficient funds to pay 
the basic living and health care expenses of the individual subject to conservatorship; 
and 
B. The court authorizes the preference under section 5-414, subsection 1, paragraph 
H. 
6. Security interest in conservatorship estate. If assets of a conservatorship estate­
are adequate to meet all existing claims, the comt, acting in the best interest of the 
individual subject to conservatorship, may order the conservator to grant a security 
interest in the conservatorship estate for payment of a claim at a future date.

§5-429. Personal liability of conservator 
1. Not personally liable. Except as otherwise agreed by a conservator, the 
conservator is not personally liable on a contract properly entered into in a fiduciary 
capacity in the course of administration of the conservatorship estate unless the 
conservator fails to reveal in the contract or before entering into the contract the 
conservator's representative capacity. 
2. Personally liable. A conservator is personally liable for an obligation arising 
from control of property of the conservatorship estate or an act or omission occurring in 
the course of administration of the conservatorship estate only if the conservator is 
personally at fault. 
3. Claims asserted against conservator. A claim based on a contract entered into 
by a conservator in a fiduciary capacity, an obligation arising from control of property 
included in the conservatorship estate or a claim based on a to1t committed in the course 
of administration of the conservatorship estate may be asserted against the 
conservatorship estate in a proceeding against the conservator in a fiduciary capacity, 
whether or not the conservator is personally liable for the claim. 
4. Determination of liability. A question of liability between a conservatorship 
estate and the conservator personally may be determined in a proceeding for accounting, 
surcharge or indemnification or another appropriate proceeding or action. 
§5-430. Removal of conservator; appointment of successor 
1. Removal by court. The court may remove a conservator for failure to perform 
the conservator's duties or other good cause and appoint a successor conservator to 
assume the duties of the conservator. 
2. Hearing upon petition, communication or determination. The court shall 
conduct a hearing to determine whether to remove a conservator and appoint a successor 
~ 
A. Petition of the individual subject to conservatorship, conservator or person 
interested in the welfare of the individual that contains allegations that, if true, would 
support a reasonable belief that removal of the conservator and appointment of a 
successor may be appropriate, but the court may decline to hold a hearing if a petition 
based on the same or substantially similar facts was filed within the preceding 6 
months; 
B. Communication from the individual subject to conservatorship, conservator or 
person interested in the welfare of the individual that supports a reasonable belief that 
removal of the conservator and appointment of a successor may be appropriate; or 
C. Determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best interest of the 
individual subject to conservatorship. 
3. Notice of petition. Notice of a petition under subsection 2, paragraph A must be 
given to the individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator and such other persons 
as the court determines.

1 4. Attorney for individual subject to conservatorship. If an individual subject to 
2 conservatorship who seeks to remove the conservator and have a successor appointed is 
3 not represented by an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same 
4 conditions as in section 5-406. The court shall award reasonable attorney1s fees to the 
5 attorney for the individual as provided in section 5-119. 
6 5. Selection of successor conservator. In selecting a successor conservator, the 
7 court shall follow the procedures under section 5-410. 
8 6. Notice of appointment of successor conservator. Not later than 30 days after 
9 appointing a successor conservator, the court shall give notice of the appointment to the 
10 individual subject to conservatorship and all persons entitled to the notice under section 
11 5-411, subsection 5 or a subsequent order. 
12 §5-431. Termination or modification of conservatorship 
13 1. Conservatorship for a minor. A conservatorship for a minor terminates on the 
14 earlier of: 
15 A. An order of the court; 
16 B. The minor becoming an adult or, if the minor consents or the court finds by clear 
17 and convincing evidence that substantial harm to the minor's interests is otherwise 
18 likely, attaining 21 years of age; 
19 C. Emancipation of the minor; and 
20 D. Death of the minor. 
21 2. Conservatorship for an adult. A conservatorship for an adult terminates on 
22 order of the court or when the adult dies. 
23 3. Petition for termination or modification. An individual subject to 
24 conservatorship, the conservator or a person interested in the welfare of the individual 
25 may petition for: 
26 A. Termination of the conservatorship on the ground that a basis for appoiniment 
27 under section 5-401 does not exist or termination would be in the best interest of the 
28 individual, or for other good cause; or 
29 B. Modification of the conservatorship on the ground that the extent of protection or 
30 assistance granted is not appropriate, or for other good cause. 
31 4. Hearing. The court shall conduct a hearing to determine whether tennination or 
32 modification of a conservatorship is appropriate on: 
33 A. Petition under subsection 3 that contains allegations that, if hue, would support a 
34 reasonable belief that teimination or modification of the conservatorship may be 
35 appropriate, but the court may decline to hold a hearing if a petition based on the 
36 same or substantially similar facts was filed within the preceding 6 months; 
37 B. A communication from the individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator 
3 8 or a person interested in the welfare of the individual that supports a reasonable belief 
39 that termination or modification of the conservatorship may be appropriate, including 
Page 80 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 because of a change in the functional needs of the individual or in the supports or 
2 services available to the individual; 
3 C. A report from a gµardian or conservator that indicates that termination or 
4 modification may be appropriate because the functional needs or supports or services 
5 available to the individual subject to conservatorship have changed or a protective 
6 arrangement of conservatorship or other less restrictive alternatives are available; or 
7 D. A determination by the court that a hearing would be in the best interest of the 
8 individual. 
9 5. Notice of petition. Notice of a petition under subsection 3 must be given to the 
10 individual subject to conservatorship, the conservator and such other persons as the court 
11 determines. 
12 6. Termination. On presentation of prima facie evidence for termination of a 
13 conservatorship, the court shall order termination unless a basis for appointment of a 
14 conservator under section 5-401 is satisfied. 
15 7. Modification. The court shall modify the powers granted to a conservator if the 
16 powers are excessive or inadequate due to a change in the abilities or limitations of the 
17 individual subject to conservatorship, the individual's supports or other circumstances. 
18 8. Safeguard rights of individual. Unless the court otherwise orders for good 
19 cause, before terminating a conservatorship, the court shall follow the same procedures to 
20 safeguard the rights of the individual subject to conservatorship that apply to a petition 
21 for conservatorship. 
22 9. Attorney for individual subject to conservatorship. If an individual subject to 
23 conservatorship who seeks to terminate or modify the terms of the conservatorship is not 
24 represented by an attorney, the court shall appoint an attorney under the same conditions 
25 in section 5-406. The court shall award reasonable attorney's fees to the individual's 
26 attorney as provided in section 5-119. 
27 10. Property; report; petition for discharge. On termination of a conservatorship 
28 and whether or not formally distributed by the conservator, property of the. 
29 conservatorship estate passes to the individual formerly subject to conservatorship or the 
30 individual's heirs, successors or assigns. The order of termination must provide for 
31 expenses of administration and direct the conservator to file a final report and petition for 
32 discharge on approval of the final report. 
33 11. Discharge. The court shall enter a final order of discharge on the approval of the 
34 final report and satisfaction by the conservator of any other condition placed by the court 
35 on the conservator's discharge. 
36 12. Distribution. On the death of an individual subject to conservatorship or other 
3 7 event terminating or partially terminating the conservatorship, the conservator shall 
3 8 proceed expeditiously to distribute the conservatorship estate to the individual or other 
39 persons entitled to it. The conservator may take reasonable measures necessary to 
40 preserve the conservatorship estate until distribution can be effected.

1 OTHER PROTECTIVE ARRANGEMENTS 
2 §5-501. Authority for protective arrangements 
3 1. Order protective arrangement. Under this Part, a court: 
4 A. Upon receiving a petition for a guardianship for an adult may order one or more 
5 protective arrangements instead of guardianship as a less restrictive alternative to 
6 guardianship; and 
7 B. Upon receiving a petition for a conservatorship for an individual may order one or 
8 more protective arrangements instead of conservatorship as a less restrictive 
9 alternative to conservatorship. 
10 2. Protective arrangement instead of guardianship. A person interested in an 
11 adult's welfare, including the adult or a conservator for the adult, may petition under this 
12 Part for one or more protective arrangements instead of guardianship. 
13 3. Protective arrangement instead of conservatorship. The following persons 
14 may petition under this Part for one or more protective arrangements instead of 
15 conservatorship: 
16 A. The individual for whom the protective arrangements are sought; 
17 B. A person interested in the property, financial affairs or welfare of the individual, 
18 including a person that would be adversely affected by lack of effective management 
19 of property or financial affairs of the individual; and 
20 C. The guardian of the individual. 
21 §5-502. Basis for protective arrangements instead of guardianship for adult 
22 1. Findings. After the hearing conducted on a petition for guardianship under 
23 section 5-302 or one or more protective airnngements instead of guardianship under 
24 section 5-501, subsection 1, the court may enter an order for one or more protective 
25 airnngements instead of guardianship under subsection 2 if the court finds by clear and 
26 convincing evidence that: 
27 A. The respondent lacks the ability to meet essential requirements for physical 
28 health, safety or self-care because the respondent is unable to receive and evaluate 
29 information or make or communicate decisions, even with appropriate supportive 
30 services, technological assistance or supported decision making; and 
31 B. The respondent's identified needs cannot be met by less restrictive alternatives. 
32 2. Orders other than guardianship. If the court makes the findings under 
33 subsection 1, the court, instead of appointing a guardian, may: 
34 A. Authorize or direct one or more transactions necessary to meet the respondent's 
35 need for health, safety or care, including but not limited to: 
36 (1) One or more paiiicular medical treatments or refusals of particular medical 
37 treatments; 
38 (2) A move to a specified place of dwelling; or

§5-503. Basis for protective arrangements instead of conservatorship for adult or 
minor 
1. Findings. After the hearing conducted on a petition for conservatorship for an 
adult under section 5-402 or one or more protective arrangements instead of 
conservatorship for an adult under section 5-501, subsection 3, the court may enter an 
order for one or more protective an-angements instead of conservatorship under 
subsection 3 for the respondent if the court finds: 
A. By clear and convincing evidence that the respondent is unable to manage 
property or financial affairs because of a limitation in the ability to receive and 
evaluate information or make or communicate decisions, even with appropriate 
supportive services, technological assistance or supported decision making, or the 
adult is missing, detained or unable to return to the United States; 
B. By a preponderance of the evidence that: 
(1) The respondent has property likely to be wasted or dissipated unless 
management is provided; or 
(2) The order under subsection 3 is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide 
money needed for the support, care, education. health or welfare of the adult or 
an individual who is entitled to the respondent's support and protection; and 
C. The respondent's identified needs cannot be met by less restrictive alternatives. 
2. Protective arrangements for minors. After the hearing conducted on a petition 
for conservatorship for a minor under section 5-402 or a protective an-angement instead 
of conservatorship for a minor under section 5-501, subsection 3, the comt may enter an 
order for a protective arrangement or protective arrangements instead of conservatorship 
under subsection 3 for the respondent if the court finds by a preponderance of the 
evidence that the minor owns money or property requiring management or protection that 
cannot be provided otherwise and: 
A. The minor has or may have financial affairs that may be put at unreasonable risk 
or hindered because of the minor's age; or 
B. The order under subsection 3 is necessary or desirable to obtain or provide money 
needed for the support, care, education, health or welfare of the minor. 
3. Orders other than conservatorship. If the court makes the findings under 
subsection 1 or 2, the court, instead of appointing a conservator, may:

19 by a person that the court finds by clear and convincing evidence:

22 respondent or the respondent's property; and 
23 B. Poses a serious risk of substantial financial harm to the respondent or the 
24 respondent's property.

26 shall consider the factors under section 5-418 a conservator must consider when making a 
27 decision on behalf of an individual subject to conservatorship. 
28 6. Minors; factors. In deciding whether to enter an order under subsection 3 or 4 
29 for a respondent who is a minor, the court also shall consider the best interest of the 
30 respondent, the preference of the parents of the respondent and the preference of the 
31 respondent if the minor is 14 years of age or older.

30 §5-505. Notice and hearing 
31 1. Date, time and place for hearing. On receipt of a petition under section 5-501, 
32 the court shall set a date, time and place for hearing on the petition. 
33 2. Notice to respondent. A copy of a petition under section 5-501 and notice of the 
34 hearing under subsection 1 must be served personally on the respondent. The notice must 
35 infmm the respondent of the respondent's rights at the hearing including the right to an 
36 attorney and to attend the hearing. The notice must also include a description of the 
37 nature, purpose and consequences of granting the petition. Failure to serve the 
38 respondent with notice substantially complying with this subsection precludes the court 
39 from granting the petition.

3. Notice to others. In a hearing under subsection 1, notice of the hearing also must 
be given to the persons listed in the petition and any other person interested in the 
respondent's welfare as the court determines. Failure to give notice under this subsection 
does not preclude the court from granting the petition. 
4. Notice of petition after order. Notice of a hearing on a petition filed under this 
Act after the court has ordered a protective arrangement or protective arrangements under 
this Part, together with a copy of the petition, must be given to the respondent and any 
other person as the court determines. 
§5-506. Appointment of visitor 
1. Petition for protective arrangement. On receipt of a petition for one or more 
protective arrangements instead of guardianship under section 5-501, the court shall 
appoint a visitor. A visitor appointed under this subsection must be an individual having 
training or experience in the type of abilities, limitations and needs alleged in the petition. 
2. Protective order for minor. On receipt of a petition for a protective order 
instead of conservatorship for a minor under section 5-501, the court may appoint a 
visitor to investigate a matter related to the petition 01· to inform the respondent or a 
parent of the respondent about the petition or a related matter. 
3. Protective order for adult. On receipt of a petition for a protective order instead 
of conservatorship for an adult under section 5-501, the court shall appoint a visitor 
unless the respondent is represented by an attorney. 
4. Visitor's duties. A visitor appointed under subsection 1 or 3 shall interview the 
respondent in person and, in a manner the respondent is best able to understand: 
A. Explain to the respondent the substance of the petition, the nature, purpose and 
effect of the proceeding, and the respondent's rights at the hearing: 
B. Determine the respondent's views with respect to the order sought: 
C. Inform the respondent of the respondent's right to employ and consult with an 
attorney at the respondent's expense and the right to request a court-appointed 
attomey; · 
D. Inform the respondent that all costs and expenses of the proceeding, including the 
respondent's attorney's fees, may be paid from the respondent's assets; 
E. If the petitioner seeks an order related to the dwelling of the respondent, visit the 
respondent's present dwelling and any dwelling in which it is reasonably believed the 
respondent will live if the order is granted; 
F. If one or more protective arrangements instead of guardianship are sought, obtain 
information from any physician or other person known to have treated, advised or 
assessed the respondent's relevant physical or mental condition; 
G. If one or more protective arrangements instead of conservatorship are sought, 
review financial records of the respondent ifrelevant to the visitor's recommendation 
under subsection 5, paragraph C: and 
H. Investigate the allegations in the petition and any other matter relating to the 
petition as the court directs.

1 5. Report. A visitor under this section promptly shall file a report in a record with 
2 the court, which must include: 
3 A. A recommendation whether an attorney should be appointed to represent the 
4 respondent; 
5 B. To the extent relevant to the order sought, a summary of self-care, independent 
6 living tasks and financial management tasks the respondent can manage without 
7 assistance or with existing supports, could manage with the assistance of a1mropriate 
8 supportive services, technological assistance or supported decision making and 
9 cannot manage; 
10 C. Recommendations regarding the appropriateness of the protective arrangement 
11 sought and whether less restrictive alternatives for meeting the respondent's needs are 
12 available; 
13 D. If the petition seeks to change the physical location of the dwelling of the 
14 respondent, a statement whether the proposed dwelling meets the respondent's needs 
15 and whether the respondent has expressed a preference as to the respondent's 
16 dwelling; 
17 E. A recommendation whether a professional evaluation under section 5-508 is 
18 necessary; 
19 F. A statement whether the respondent is able to attend a hearing at the location court 
20 proceedings typically are conducted; 
21 G. A statement whether the respondent is able to participate in a hearing and that 
22 identifies any technology or other form of supp01t that would enhance the 
23 respondent's ability to patticipate; and 
24 H. Any other matter as the court directs. 
25 §5-507. Appointment and role of attorney 
26 1. Appointment of attorney. The court shall appoint an attorney to represent the 
27 respondent in a proceeding under this Part if: 
28 A. Requested by the respondent; 
29 B. Recommended by the visitor; 
30 C. The court determines that the respondent needs representation; or 
31 D. It comes to the court's attention that the respondent wishes to contest any aspect 
32 of the proceeding or to seek any limitations on the protective arrangement. 
33 2. Attorney's duties. An attorney representing the respondent in a proceeding under 
34 this Part shall: 
35 A. Make reasonable efforts to ascertain the respondent's wishes; 
36 B. Advocate for the respondent's wishes to the extent reasonably ascertainable; and 
37 C. If the respondent's wishes are not reasonably ascertainable, advocate for the result 
3 8 that is the least restrictive option in type, duration and scope, consistent with the 
39 respondent's interests. 
Page 88 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .. p,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 3. Attorney for parent of minor. The court shall appoint an attorney to represent a 
2 parent of a minor who is the subject of a proceeding under this Part if: 
3 A. The parent objects to the entry of an order for a protective arrangement or 
4 protective arrangements instead of guardianship or conservatorship; 
5 B. The court determines that counsel is needed to ensure that consent to the entry of 
6 an order for one or more protective arrangements is informed; or 
7 C. The court othe1wise determines the parent needs representation. 
8 §5-508. Professional evaluation 
9 1. Order professional evaluation. At or before a hearing on a petition under this 
10 Part for a protective arrangement, the court shall order a professional evaluation of the 
11 respondent: 
12 A. If the respondent requests the evaluation: or 
13 B. Unless the court finds that it has sufficient information to determine the 
14 respondent's needs and abilities without the evaluation. 
15 2. Examination; report. If the court orders an evaluation under subsection 1, the 
16 respondent must be examined by a licensed physician or psychologist approved by the 
17 comt who is qualified to evaluate the respondent's alleged cognitive and functional 
18 abilities and limitations and will not he advantaged or disadvantaged by a decision to 
19 grant the petition or otherwise have a conflict of interest. The individual conducting the 
20 evaluation promptly shall file a report in a record with the court. Unless otherwise 
21 directed by the court, the report must contain: 
22 A. A description of the nature, type and extent of the respondent's cognitive and 
23 functional abilities and limitations: 
24 B. An evaluation of the respondent's mental and physical condition and, if 
25 appropriate, educational potential. adaptive behavior and social skills; 
26 C. A prognosis for improvement, including with regard to the ability to manage the 
27 respondent's property and financial affairs if a limitation in that ability is alleged, and 
28 recommendation for the appropriate treatment, support or habilitation plan: and 
29 D. The date of the examination on which the report is based. 
30 3. Right to decline. The respondent has the right to decline to participate in an 
31 evaluation ordered under subsection 1. 
32 §5-509. Attendance and rights at hearing 
33 1. Attendance by respondent required. Except as otherwise provided in 
34 subsection 2, a hearing under this Part may proceed only if the respondent attends the 
35 hearing. If it is not reasonably feasible for the respondent to attend a hearing at the 
36 location court proceedings typically are conducted, the comt shall make reasonable 
37 efforts to hold the hearing at an alternative location convenient to the respondent or allow 
38 the respondent to attend the hearing using real-time audiovisual technology. 
Page 89 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT .p,, to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 2. Hearing without respondent; findings. A hearing under this Part may proceed 
2 without the respondent in attendance if the court fmds by clear and convincing evidence 
3 that: 
4 A. The respondent consistently and repeatedly has refused to attend the hearing after 
5 having been fully informed of the right to attend the hearing and the potential 
6 consequences of failing to do so; 
7 B. There is no practicable way for the respondent to attend and participate in the 
8 hearing even with appropriate supportive services and technological assistance; 
9 C. The respondent is represented by an attorney and the attorney represents that the 
10 respondent does not want to attend the hearing; 
11 D. The visitor has confirmed with the respondent that the respondent has no 
12 objection to the protective arrangements and that the respondent does not wish to 
13 attend the hearing; or 
14 E. The respondent is a minor who has received proper notice and attendance would 
15 be harmful to the minor. 
16 3. Assistance to respondent. The respondent may be assisted in a hearing under 
17 this Part by a person or persons of the respondent's choosing, assistive technology or an 
18 interpreter or translator, or a combination of these supports. If assistance would facilitate 
19 the respondent's participation in the hearing but is not otherwise available to the 
20 respondent, the court shall make reasonable efforts to provide it. 
21 4. Attorney for respondent. The respondent has a right to choose an attorney to 
22 represent the respondent at a hearing under this Part. 
23 5. Rights of respondent at hearing. At a hearing under this Part, the respondent 
24 may: 
25 A. Present evidence and subpoena witnesses and documents; 
26 B. Examine witnesses, including any court-appointed evaluator and the visitor; and 
27 C. Otherwise participate in the hearing. 
28 6. Closed upon request; good cause. A hearing under this Part must be closed on 
29 request of the respondent and a showing of good cause. 
30 7. Participation; best interest of respondent. Anv person may request to 
31 participate in a hearing under this Part. The court may grant the request, with or without 
32 hearing, on determining that the best interest of the respondent will be served. The comt 
33 may attach appropriate conditions to the person's participation. 
34 §5-510. Notice of order 
35 The court shall give notice of an order under this Part to the individual who is the 
36 subject of the protective arrangements instead of guardianship or conservatorship, a 
37 person whose access to the respondent is restricted by the order and any other person as 
3 8 the court determines.
