§5-511. Confidentiality of records 
1. Matter of public record; exceptions. The existence of a proceeding for or the 
existence of one or more protective arrangements instead of a guardianship or 
conservatorship is a matter of public record unless the court seals the record after: 
A. The respondent, the individual subject to the protective arrangements or the 
parent of a minor subject to the protective arrangements reguests the record be sealed: 
and 
B. Either: 
(1) The proceeding is dismissed: 
(2) The protective arrangement is no longer in effect: or 
(3) Any act authorized by the order granting the protective arrangement has been 
completed. 
2. Access to records. A respondent, an individual subject to a proceeding for one or 
more protective arrangements instead of guardianship or conservatorship, an attorney 
designated by the respondent or individual, a parent of a minor subject to one or more 
protective arrangements and any other person the court determines are entitled to access 
court records of the proceeding and resulting protective arrangement. A person not 
otherwise entitled to access to court records under this subsection may petition the court 
for access. The court shall grant access if access is in the best interest of the respondent 
or individual subject to the protective arrangements or furthers the public interest and 
does not endanger the welfare or financial interests of the respondent or individual. 
3. Reports sealed; availability. A report of a visitor or professional evaluation 
generated in the course of a proceeding under this Part must be sealed on filing but is 
available to: 
A. The comt: 
B. The individual who is the subject of the report or evaluation, without limitation as 
to use; 
C. The petitioner, visitor and petitioner's and respondent's attorneys, for purposes of 
the proceeding: 
D. Unless the comt directs otherwise. an agent appointed under a power of attorney 
for finances in which the respondent is identified as the principal: 
E. If the order is for one or more protective arrangements instead of guardianship 
and unless the court directs otherwise. an agent appointed under a power of attorney 
for health care in which the respondent is identified as the principal: and 
F. Other persons when it is in the public interest or for a pm:pose the court orders for 
good cause.

1 SUBPART! 
2 GENERAL PROVISIONS 
3 §5-601. Short title 
4 This Part may be known and cited as "the Uniform Adult Guardianship and 
5 Protective Proceedings Jurisdiction Act.11 
6 §5-602. Definitions 
7 As used in this Part, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following terms have 
8 the following meanings. 
9 1. Adult. 11Adult11 means an individual who has attained 18 years of age. 
10 2. Conservator. 11Conservator11 means a person appointed by the court to administer 
11 the property of an adult, including a person appointed under Part 4. 
12 3. Guardian. "Guardian" means a person appointed by the court to make decisions 
13 regarding the person of an adult, including a person appointed under Part 3. 
14 4. Guardianship proceeding. "Guardianship proceeding" means a judicial 
15 proceeding in which an order for the appointment of a guardian is sought or has been 
16 issued. 
17 5. Individual subject to guardianship. "Individual subject to guardianship" means 
18 an adult for whom a guardian has been appointed. 
19 6. Party. 11Party11 means an interested person within the meaning of section 1-201, 
20 subsection 26, including the respondent, petitioner, guardian, conservator or any other 
21 person allowed by the court to participate in a guardianship or protective proceeding. 
22 7. Person. 11Person,11 except in the term "protected person," means an individual; 
23 corporation; business trust; estate; trust; partnership; limited liability company; 
24 association; joint venture; public corporation; government or governmental subdivision, 
25 agency or instrumentality; or any other legal or commercial entity. 
26 8. Protected person. "Protected person" means an adult for whom a protective 
27 order has been issued. 
28 9. Protective order. 11Protective order11 means an order appointing a conservator or 
29 other order related to management or disposition of an adult1s property. 
30 10. Protective proceeding. "Protective proceeding" means a judicial proceeding in 
31 which a protective order is sought or has been issued. 
32 11. Respondent. 11Respondent11 means an adult for whom a protective order or the 
33 appointment of a guardian is sought. 
34 §5-603. International application of Part 
35 A court of this State may treat a foreign country as if it were a state for the pm:pose of 
36 applying this Part. 
Page 92 -128LR0452(02)-1

1 §5-604. Communication between courts 
2 1. Communication between courts; participation; record. A court of this State 
3 may communicate with a comt in another state concerning a proceeding arising under this 
4 Part. The court may allow the parties to participate in the communication. Except as 
5 otherwise provided in subsection 2, the court shall make a record of the communication. 
6 The record may be limited to the fact that the communication occurred. 
7 2. No record required. Courts may communicate concerning schedules, calendars, 
8 court records and other administrative matters without making a record. 
9 §5-605. Cooperation between courts 
1 O 1. Request of court of another state. In a guardianship proceeding or protective 
11 proceeding in this State, a court of this State may request the appropriate court of another 
12 state to do any of the following: 
13 A. Hold an evidentiary hearing; 
14 B. Order a person in that state to produce evidence or give testimony pursuant to 
15 procedures of that state; 
16 C. Order that an evaluation or assessment be made of the respondent; 
17 D. Order any appropriate investigation of a person involved in a proceeding; 
18 E. Forward to the court a certified copy of the transcript or other record of a hearing 
19 under paragraph A or any other proceeding, any evidence otherwise produced under 
20 paragraph B and any evaluation or assessment prepared in compliance with an order 
21 under paragraph C or D; 
22 F. Issue any order necessary to ensure the appearance in the proceeding of a person 
23 whose presence is necessary for the court to make a determination, including the 
24 respondent or the individual subject to guardianship or protected person; and 
25 G. Issue an order authorizing the release of medical, financial, criminal or other 
26 relevant information in that state, including protected health information as defined in 
27 45 Code of Federal Regulations, Section 160.103, as amended. 
28 2. Jurisdiction to comply with request. If a court of another state in which a 
29 guardianship proceeding or protective proceeding is pending requests assistance of the 
30 kind provided in subsection 1, a court of this State has jurisdiction for the limited purpose 
31 of granting the request or making reasonable efforts to comply with the request. 
32 §5-606. Taking testimony in another state 
33 1. Testimony of witness in another state. In a guardianship proceeding or 
34 protective proceeding, in addition to other procedures that may be available, testimony of 
35 a witness who is located in another state may be offered by deposition or other means 
36 allowable in this State for testimony taken in another state. The court on its own motion 
37 may order that the testimony of a witness be taken in another state and may prescribe the 
38 manner in which and the terms upon which the testimony is to be taken. 
39 2. Deposition or testimony by electronic means. In a guardianship proceeding or 
40 protective proceeding, a court in this State may permit a witness located in another state

1 to be deposed or to testify by telephone or audiovisual or other electronic means. A court

3 location for the deposition or testimony. 
4 3. Documentary evidence transmitted, no original writing. Documentarv

8 SUBPART2 
9 JURISDICTION 
10 §5-621. Definitions; significant-connection factors 
11 1. Definitions. As used in this subpart, unless the context othe1wise indicates, the 
12 following terms have the following meanings. 
13 A. "Emergency" means a circumstance that likely will result in substantial harm to a 
14 respondent1s health, safety or welfare and for which the appointment of a guardian is 
15 necessary. 
16 B. "Home state" means the state in which the respondent was physically present, 
17 including any period of temporary absence, for at least 6 consecutive months 
18 immediately before the filing of a petition for a protective order or the appointment of 
19 a guardian or, if the respondent was not physically present in a single state for the 6 
20 months immediately preceding the filing of the petition, the state in which the 
21 respondent was physically present, including any period of temporary absence, for at 
22 least 6 consecutive months ending within the 6 months prior to the filing of the 
23 petition. 
24 C. "Significant-connection state" means a state, other than the home state, with 
25 which a respondent has a significant connection other than mere physical presence 
26 and in which substantial evidence concerning the respondent is available. 
27 2. Significant-connection factm·s. In determining under section 5-623 and section 
28 5-631, subsection 5 whether a respondent has a significant connection with a particular 
29 state, the court shall consider: 
30 A. The location of the respondent's family and other persons required to be notified 
31 of the guardianship proceeding or protective proceeding; 
32 B. The length of time the respondent at any time was physically present in the state 
33 and the duration of any absence; 
34 C. The location of the respondent's property; and 
35 D. The extent to which the respondent has ties to the state such as voting registration, 
36 state or local tax return filing, vehicle registration, driver's license, social relationship 
37 and receipt of services. 
Page 94 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
' ' COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "H" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 §5-622. Exclusive basis 
2 This subpart provides the exclusive jurisdictional basis for a court of this State to 
3 appoint a guardian or issue a protective order for an adult. 
4 §5-623. Jurisdiction 
5 A court of this State has jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order 
6 for a respondent if: 
7 1. Respondent's home state. This State is the respondent's home state: or 
8 2. Significant-connection state and other factors. On the date the petition is filed, 
9 this State is a significant-connection state and: 
10 A. The respondent does not have a home state or a court of the respondent's home 
11 state has declined to exercise jurisdiction because this State is a more appropriate 
12 forum: 
13 B. The respondent has a home state, a petition for an appointment or order is not 
14 pending in a court of that state or another significant-connection state and, before the 
15 court makes the appointment or issues the order: 
16 (1) A petition for an appointment or order is not filed in the respondent's home 
17 state: 
18 (2) An objection to the court's jurisdiction is not filed by a person required to be 
19 notified of the proceeding: and 
20 (3) The court in this State concludes that it is an appropriate fornm under the 
21 factors set forth in section 5-626; 
22 C. This State does not have jurisdiction under either paragraph A or B, the 
23 respondent's home state and all significant-connection states have declined to 
24 exercise jurisdiction because this State is the more appropriate forum and jurisdiction 
25 in this State is consistent with the Constitution of Maine and the United States 
26 Constitution: or 
27 D. The requirements for special jurisdiction under section 5-624 are met. 
28 §5-624. Special jurisdiction 
29 1. Special jurisdiction. If this State is not the respondent's home state and not a 
30 significant-connection state, a court of this State has special jurisdiction to do any of the 
31 following: 
32 A. Appoint a guardian in an emergency for a term not exceeding 6 months for a 
33 respondent who is physically present in this State: 
34 B. Issue a protective order with respect to real or tangible personal property located 
3 5 in this State: or 
36 C. Appoint a guardian or conservator for an individual subject to guardianship or 
37 protected person for whom a provisional order to transfer the proceeding from 
38 another state has been issued under procedures similar to those in section 5-631. 
Page 95 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT·~" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
· 1 2. Emergency appointment. If a petition for the appointment of a guardian in an 
2 emergency is brought in this State and this State was not the respondent's home state on 
3 the date the petition was filed, the court shall dismiss the proceeding at the request of the 
4 court of the home state, if any, whether dismissal is requested before or after the 
5 emergency appointment. 
6 §5-625. Exclusive and continuing jurisdiction 
7 Except as otherwise provided in section 5-624, a comt that has appointed a guardian 
8 or issued a protective order consistent with this Part has exclusive and continuing 
9 jurisdiction over the proceeding until it is terminated by the court or the appointment or 
10 order expires by its own terms. 
11 §5-626. Appropriate forum 
12 1. Decline jurisdiction. A court of this State having jurisdiction under section 5-623 
13 to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order may decline to exercise its jurisdiction if 
14 it determines at any time that a court of another state is a more appropriate forum. 
15 2. Actions by court that declines jurisdiction. If a court of this State declines to 
16 exercise its jurisdiction under subsection 1, it shall either: 
17 A. Dismiss or stay the proceeding; or 
18 B. Impose any condition the comt considers just and proper, including the condition 
19 that a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective order be 
20 filed promptly in another state. 
21 3. Appropriate forum factors. In determining whether it is an appropriate forum, 
22 the court shall consider all relevant factors, which may include: 
23 A. Any expressed preference of the respondent; 
24 B. Whether abuse, neglect or exploitation of the respondent has occurred or is likely 
25 to occm and which state could best protect the respondent from the abuse, neglect or 
26 exploitation; 
27 C. The length of time the respondent was physically present in or was a legal 
28 resident of this State or another state; 
29 D. The distance of the respondent from the court in each state; 
30 E. The financial circumstances of the respondent's estate; 
31 F. The nature and location of the evidence; 
32 G. The ability of the court in each state to decide the issue expeditiously and the 
33 procedures necessary to present evidence; 
34 H. The familiarity of the court of each state with the facts and issues in the 
35 proceeding; and 
36 I. If an appointment were made, the court's ability to monitor the conduct of the 
37 guardian or conservator.

., , '. r' §5-627. Jurisdiction declined by reason of conduct 
2 1. Jurisdiction because of unjustifiable conduct. If at any time a court of this 
3 State determines that it acquired jurisdiction to appoint a gµardian or issue a protective 
4 order because of unjustifiable conduct, the court may: 
5 A. Decline to exercise jurisdiction; 
6 B. Exercise jurisdiction for the limited purpose of fashioning an appropriate remedy 
7 to ensure the health, safety and welfare of the respondent or the protection of the 
8 respondent's property or prevent a repetition of the unjustifiable conduct, including 
9 staying the proceeding until a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance 
10 of a protective order is filed in a court of another state having jurisdiction; or 
11 C. Continue to exercise jurisdiction after considering: 
12 (1) The extent to which the respondent and all persons required to be notified of 
13 the proceedings have acquiesced in the exercise of the court's jurisdiction: 
14 (2) Whether it is a more appropriate forum than the court of any other state under 
15 the factors set forth in section 5-626, subsection 3; and 
16 (3) Whether the court of any other state would have jurisdiction under factual 
17 circumstances in substantial conformity with the jurisdictional standards of 
18 section 5-623. 
19 2. Assessment of expenses. If a court of this State determines that it acquired 
20 jurisdiction to appoint a guardian or issue a protective order because a party seeking to 
21 invoke its jurisdiction engaged in unjustifiable conduct, it may assess against that party 
22 necessary and reasonable expenses, including attorney's fees, investigative fees, court 
23 costs, communication exQenses, witness fees and expenses and travel expenses. The 
24 court may not assess fees, costs or expenses of any kind against this State or a 
25 governmental subdivision, agency or instrumentality of this State unless authorized by 
26 law other than this Part. 
27 §5-628. Notice of proceeding 
28 If a petition for the appointment of a guardian or issuance of a protective order is 
29 brought in this State and this State was not the respondent's home state on the date the 
30 petition was filed, in addition to complying with the notice requirements of this State, 
31 notice of the petition must be given to those persons who would be entitled to notice of 
32 the petition if a proceeding were brought in the respondent's home state. The notice must 
33 be given in the same manner as notice is required to be given in this State. 
34 §5-629. Proceedings in more than one state

3 8 of a protective order is filed in this State and in another state and neither petition has been

11 SUBPART 3 
12 TRANSFER OF GUARDIANSHIP OR CONSERVATORSHIP 
13 §5-631. Transfer of guardianship or conservatorship to another state 
14 1. Petition. A guardian or conservator appointed in this State may petition the court 
15 to transfer the guardianship or conservatorship to another state. 
16 2. Notice. Notice of a petition under subsection 1 must be given to the persons that 
17 would be entitled to notice of a petition in this State for the appointment of a guardian or 
18 conservator. 
19 3. Hearing or opportunity for hearing. On the court's own motion or on request of 
20 the guardian or conservator, the individual subject to guardianship or protected person or 
21 other person required to be notified of the petition, the court shall hold a hearing or 
22 provide an opp01iunity for a hearing to be held on a petition filed pursuant to subsection 
23 .L 
24 4. Provisional order; guardianship. The court shall issue an order provisionally 
25 granting a petition to transfer a guardianship and shall direct the guardian to petition for 
26 guardianship in the other state if the court is satisfied that the guardianship will be 
27 accepted by the comi in the other state and the court finds that: 
28 A. The individual subject to guardianship is physically present in or is reasonably 
29 expected to move peimanently to the other state; 
30 B. An objection to the transfer has not been made or, if an objection has been made, 
31 the objector has not established by a preponderance of the evidence that the transfer 
32 would be contrary to the best interest of the individual subject to guardianship; and 
33 C. Plans for care and services for the individual subject to guardianship in the other 
34 state are reasonable and sufficient. 
35 5. Provisional order; conservatorship. The court shall issue a provisional order 
36 granting a petition to transfer a conservatorship and shall direct the conservator to petition 
3 7 for conservatorship in the other state if the comi is satisfied that the conservatorship will 
38 be accepted by the court of the other state and the court finds that:

A. A provisional order accepting the proceeding from the court to which the

B. The documents required to terminate a guardianship or conservatorship in this 
State. 
§5-632. Accepting guardianship or conservatorship transferred from another state 
1. Petition. To confirm transfer of a guardianship or conservatorship transferred to 
this State under provisions similar to section 5-631, the guardian or conservator must 
petition the court in this State to accept the guardianship or conservatorship. The petition 
must include a ce1iified copy of the other state's provisional order of transfer. 
2. Notice. Notice of a petition under subsection 1 must be given to those persons 
who would be entitled to notice if the petition were a petition for the appointment of a 
guardian or issuance of a protective order in both the transferring state and this State. 
The notice must be given in the same manner as notice is required to be given in this 
State. 
3. Hearing. On the comi's own motion or on request of the guardian or conservator, 
the individual subject to guardianship or protected person or other person required to be 
notified of the proceeding, the court shall hold a hearing on a petition filed pursuant to 
subsection 1. 
4. Provisional order. The court shall issue an order provisionally granting a petition 
filed under subsection 1 unless: 
A. An objection is made and the objector establishes by a preponderance of the 
evidence that transfer of the proceeding would be contrary to the best interest of the 
individual subject to guardianship or protected person: or 
B. The guardian or conservator is ineligible for appointment in this State. 
5. Final order. The court shall issue a final order accepting the proceeding and 
appointing the guardian or conservator as guardian or conservator in this State upon its 
receipt from the court from which the proceeding is being transferred of a final order 
issued under provisions similar to section 5-631 transferring the proceeding to this State. 
6. Recognition of order from other state. In granting a petition under this section, 
the court shall recognize a guardianship or conservatorship order from the other state,

9 SUBPART4 
10 MISCELLANEOUS PROVISIONS 
11 §5-641. Uniformity of application and construction 
12 In applying and construing this Part, consideration must be given to the need to 
13 promote uniformity of the law with respect to its subject matter among states that enact it. 
14 §5-642. Relation to Electronic Signatures in Global and National Commerce Act 
15 This Part modifies, limits and supersedes the federal Electronic Signatures in Global 
16 and National Commerce Act, 15 United States Code, Section 7001 et seq., but does not 
17 modify, limit or supersede 15 United States Code, Section 7001(c) or authorize electronic 
18 delivery of any of the notices described in 15 United States Code, Section 7003(b). 
19 §5-643. Transitional provisions 
20 1. Proceedings on or after July 1, 2019. This Part applies to guardianship and 
21 protective proceedings begun on or after July 1, 2019. 
22 2. Proceedings before July 1, 2019. Subparts 1 and 3 and sections 5-641 and 5-642 
23 apply to proceedings begun before July 1, 2019, regardless of whether a guardianship or 
24 protective order has been issued. 
25 PART 7 
26 PUBLIC GUARDIAN AND CONSERVATOR 
27 §5-701. Public guardians and conservators; general 
28 1. Appointment of public guardian or conservator. In any case in which a 
29 guardian or conservator may be appointed by the court under this Article, the court may 
30 appoint a public guardian or conservator as provided in this Patt for persons who are in 
31 need of protective services. 
32 2. Department of Health and Human Services. The Department of Health and 
33 Human Services shall act as the public guardian or conservator for persons in need of 
34 protective services. 
35 3. Article applies to public guardians and conservators. Except as otherwise 
36 provided in this Part, the appointment, termination, rights and duties and other provisions 
37 for guardians and conservators in this Article apply to public guardians and conservators. 
Page 100 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A "to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 §5-702. Priority of private guardian or conservator 
2 A public guardian or conservator may not be appointed if the court determines that a 
3 suitable private guardian or conservator is available and willing to assume the 
4 responsibilities of a guardian or conservator. 
5 §5-703. Exclusiveness of public guardian or conservator 
6 When the court has appointed a public guardian or conservator under this Part, no 
7 coguardian or coconservator may be appointed for the same individual subject to 
8 guardianship or protected person during the continuation of the public guardianship or 
9 public conservatorship. 
10 §5-704. Nomination of public guardian or conservator 
11 1. Nomination of public {Wardian. Anv oerson who is eligible to petition for 
12 appointment of a guardian under section 5-302, subsection 1, including the commissioner 
13 of any state department, the head of any state institution, the overseers of the poor and the 
14 welfare director or health officer of any municipality, may nominate the public guardian. 
15 2. Nomination of public conservator. Any person who is eligible to petition for 
16 appointment of a conservator under section 5-402, subsection 1, including the 
17 commissioner of any state department, the head of any state institution, the overseer of 
18 the poor and the welfare director or health officer of any municipality, may nominate the 
19 public conservator. 
20 3. Article applies to proceedings for determining appointment. Except as 
21 supplemented by section 5-705, the proceedings for determining the appointment of a 
22 public guardian or conservator are governed by the provisions of this Article for the 
23 appointment of guardians and conservators generally. 
24 §5-705. Acceptance by public guardian or conservator; plan 
25 Prior to the appointment of a public guardian or conservator, the appropriate agency 
26 nominated shall accept or reject the nomination in writing within 30 days of its receipt of 
27 notification that it has been nominated and if the nomination is accepted shall file a 
28 detailed plan that, as relevant, must include but is not limited to the type of proposed 
29 living an-angement for the individual subject to guardianship, how the individual's 
30 financial needs will be met, how the individual's medical and other remedial needs will be 
31 met, how the individual's social needs will be met and a plan for the individual's 
32 continuing contact with relatives and friends, as well as a plan for the management of the 
33 individual's or protected person's estate in the case of a public conservatorship. 
34 §5-706. Officials authorized to act as public guardian or conservator 
35 1. Commissioner of Health and Human Services. When the Department of Health 
36 and Human Services is appointed public guardian or conservator of a person, the 
3 7 authority of the public guardian or conservator must be exercised by the Commissioner of 
3 8 Health and Human Services and by any persons duly delegated by the commissioner to 
39 exercise such authority.

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT

1 2. Delegation of authority. Persons duly delegated by the officials authorized to act 
2 under subsection 1 may include a staff of competent social workers or competent social 
3 workers assigned to the public guardian or conservator by the Department of Health and 
4 Human Services. In the event that the delegation is to an individual, such individual must 
5 be qualified by reason of education or experience, or both, in administering to the needs 
6 of the individual or individuals over whom the individual is to exercise administrative or 
7 supervisory authority under the public guardian. 
8 §5-707. Duties and powers of a public guardian or conservator 
9 A public guardian or conservator has the same powers, rights and duties respecting 
10 the individual subject to guardianship or the protected person as provided for guardians 
11 and conservators by the other Parts of this Article except as otherwise Sl?ecifically 
12 provided in this Part, including the following particular provisions. 
13 1. Placement in licensed facility; removal. A public guardian may place an 
14 individual subject to guardianship in a facility described in Title 22, section 1811 only if 
15 the facility is duly licensed. In the event that the license of any such facility is suspended 
16 or revoked, the public guardian having any individual subject to guardianship placed in 
17 that facility shall remove the individual and effect an appropriate placement of the 
18 individual as soon as practicable after knowledge of the suspension or revocation of the 
19 license. 
20 2. Examination and evaluation; report to court. A public guardian or conservator 
21 at least annually, and at any time when ordered by the court, shall review the case of 
22 every person for whom the public guardian or conservator is acting under this Part. A 
23 report of each review must be filed with the court. Each review must contain an 
24 examination and evaluation of the plan created under section 5-705 for the individual 
25 subject to guardianship or protected person and recommendations for a modification of 
26 the plan, as appropriate or necessary. 
27 3. Records. A public guardian or conservator shall keep books of account or other 
28 records showing separately the principal amount received, increments thereto and 
29 disbursements therefrom for the benefit of the individual subject to guardianship or 
30 protected person, and such other records as are appropriate for the particular situation, 
31 !Qgether with the name of the individual subject to guardianship or protected person, the 
32 source from which the money was received and the purpose for which the money was 
33 expended. 
34 4. In absence of ldn, autopsy and burial. A public guardian, in the absence of 
35 available next of kin, may authorize the performance of an autopsy upon the body of a 
36 deceased individual subject to guardianship. The public guardian, in the absence of 
37 available next of kin, or in the event that next of kin refuses to assume responsibility for 
38 the deceased individual subject to guardianship, shall cause any deceased individual 
39 subject to guardianship to be suitably buried and has authority to expend funds of the 
40 individual for that purpose, and in the event the individual is without funds at the time of 
41 death, the public guardian shall cause the individual to be suitably buried at public 
4 2 expense, as in the case of the burial of any other deceased indigent person.

(, 11 · §5-708. No change in rights to services 
2 The appointment of a public guardian or conservator in no way enlarges or 
3 diminishes the individual subject to guardianship1s or protected person1s right to services 
4 made available to all persons in need of service or protection in the State except for the 
5 provision of guardianship or conservatorship services as provided under this Article. 
6 §5-709. No change in powers and duties of agency heads and trustees 
7 Nothing in this Article abrogates any other powers or duties vested by law in the head 
8 of any public institution, or vested by the settlor of a trust in the trustee thereof, for the 
9 benefit of any individual subject to guardianship or protected person for whom the public 
10 guardian or conservator is appointed. 
11 §5-710. Bond 
12 The public guardian or conservator is not required to file bonds in individual 
13 guardianships or conservatorships, but shall give a surety bond for the joint benefit of the 
14 individuals subject to guardianship or protected persons placed under the responsibility of 
15 the public guardian or conservator and the State, with a surety company or companies 
16 authorized to do business within the State, in an amount not less than the total value of all 
17 assets held by the public guardian or conservator, which amount must be computed at the 
18 end of each state fiscal year and approved by the Probate Court for Kennebec County. At 
19 no time may the bond of each of the public guardians or conservators be less than $500 
20 respectively. 
21 §5-711. Compensation 
22 1. Reasonable expenses; account for costs. The public guardian or conservator 
23 may receive such reasonable amounts for its expenses as guardian or conservator as the 
24 Probate Court may allow. The amounts so allowed must be allocated to an account from 
25 which may be drawn expenses for filing fees, bond premiums, court costs and other 
26 exnenses required in the administration of the functions of the public guardian or 
27 conservator. No amounts thus received may inure to the benefit of any employee of the 
28 public guardian or conservator. Any balance in the account at the end of a fiscal year 
29 does not lapse but is can'ied forward from year to year and used for the purposes provided 
3 0 for in this subsection. 
31 2. Reimbursement of personal expenditures. Any personal expenditures made on 
32 the individual subject to guardianship1s or protected person1s behalf by the public 
33 guardian or conservator must, when properly evidenced, be reimbursed out of the 
34 individual subject to guardianship1s or protected person1s estate. Claims for services 
35 rendered by state agencies must be submitted to the Probate Court for approval before 
36 payment. 
37 §5-712. Individuals subject to guardianship; guardian ad litem costs 
38 1. Guardian ad litem, other special costs. The costs of the guardian ad litem or 
39 any other special costs may be paid by the Department of Health and Human Services, 
40 within the limits of the department1s budget, when: 
41 A. A person is in need of protective services and:

15 PART 8 
16 UNIFORM HEALTH CARE DECISIONS ACT 
17 §5-801. Short title 
18 This Part may be known and cited as "the Uniform Health Care Decisions Act." 
19 §5-802. Definitions 
20 As used in this Part, unless the context otherwise indicates, the following te1ms have 
21 the following meanings. 
22 1. Advance health care directive. "Advance health care directive" means an 
23 individual instruction from, or a power of attorney for health care by, an individual with 
24 capacity. 
25 2. Agent. "Agent" means an individual with capacity designated in a power of 
26 attorney for health care to make a health care decision for the individual granting the 
27 power. 
28 3. Capacity. "Capacity" means the ability to have a basic understanding of the 
29 diagnosed condition and to understand the significant benefits, risks and alternatives to 
30 the proposed health care and the consequences of forgoing the proposed treatment, the 
31 ability to make and communicate a health care decision and the ability to understand the 
32 consequences of designating an agent or surrogate to make health care decisions. 
33 4. Guardian. "Guardian" means a judicially appointed guardian or conservator 
34 having authority to make a health care decision for an individual. 
35 5. Health care. "Health care" means any care, treatment, service or procedure to 
36 maintain, diagnose or otherwise affect an individual's physical or mental condition. 
Page 104 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
,,-, 
.,, COMMITTEEAMENDMENT'~ "toH.P,91,L.D.123 
1 6. Health care decision. "Health care decision" means a decision made by an 
2 individual with capacity or by the individual's agent, guardian or surrogate regarding the 
3 individual's health care, including: 
4 A. Selection and discharge of health care providers and institutions: 
5 B. Approval or disapproval of diagnostic tests, surgical procedures. programs of 
6 medication and orders not to resuscitate: and 
7 C. Directions to provide, withhold or withdraw artificial nutrition and hydration and 
8 all other forms of health care, including life-sustaining treatment. 
9 7. Health care institution. "Health care institution" means an institution, facility or 
10 agency licensed. certified or otherwise authorized or permitted by law to provide health 
11 care in the ordinary course of business. 
12 8. Health care provider. "Health care provider" means an individual licensed, 
13 certified or otherwise authorized or permitted by law to provide health care in the 
14 ordinary course of business or practice of a profession. 
15 9. Individual instruction. "Individual instruction" means a direction from an 
16 individual with capacity concerning a health care decision for the individual. 
17 10. Life-sustaining treatment. "Life-sustaining treatment" means any medical 
18 procedure or intervention that, when administered to a person without capacity and in 
19 either a terminal condition or a persistent vegetative state, will serve only to prolong the 
20 process of dying. "Life-sustaining treatment" may include artificially administered 
21 nutrition and hydration, which is the provision of nutrients and liquids through the use of 
22 tubes. intravenous procedures or similar medical interventions. 
23 11. Persistent vegetative state. "Persistent vegetative state" means a state that 
24 occurs after coma in which the patient totally lacks higher cortical and cognitive function, 
25 but maintains vegetative brain stem processes, with no realistic possibility of recovery, as 
26 diagnosed in accordance with acceptable medical standards. 
27 12. Person. "Person" means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust, 
28 partnership, association, joint venture, government, governmental subdivision, agency or 
29 instrumentality or any other legal or commercial entity. 
30 13. Physician. "Physician" means an individual authorized to practice medicine 
31 under Title 32. 
32 14. Power of attorney for health care. "Power of attorney for health care" means 
33 the desigpation of an agent with capacity to make health care decisions for the individual 
34 granting the power. 
35 15. Primary physician. "Primary physician" means a physician designated by an 
36 individual with capacity or by the individual's agent, guardian or surrogate to have 
37 primary responsibility for the individual's health care or, in the absence of a designation 
3 8 or if the designated physician is not reasonably available, a physician who undertakes the 
39 responsibility. 
Page 105 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"~ "to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 16. Reasonably available. "Reasonably available" means readily able to be 
2 contacted without undue effort and willing and able to act in a timely manner considering 
3 the urgency of the patient's health care needs. 
4 17. Supervising health care provider. "Supervising health care provider" means 
5 the primary physician or, if there is no primary physician or the primary physician is not 
6 reasonably available, the health care provider who has undertaken primary responsibility 
7 for a patient's health care. 
8 18. Surrogate. "Surrogate" means an individual with capacity, other than a patient's 
9 agent or guardian, authorized under this Part to make health care decisions as provided in 
10 section 5-806. 
11 19. Terminal condition. "Terminal condition" means an incurable and irreversible 
12 condition that, without the administration of life-sustaining treatment, in the opinion of 
13 the primary physician, will result in death within a relatively short time. 
14 §5-803. Advance health care directives 
15 1. Individual instruction. An adult or emancipated minor with capacity may give 
16 an individual instruction. The instruction may be oral or written. The instruction may be 
17 limited to take effect only if a specified condition arises. An oral instruction is valid only 
18 if made to a health care provider or to an individual who may serve as a surrogate under 
19 section 5-806, subsection 2. 
20 2. Power of attorney for health care. An adult or emancipated minor with capacity 
21 may execute a power of attorney for health care, which may authorize the agent to make 
22 any health care decision the principal could have made while having capacity. The power 
23 must be in writing and signed by the principal and 2 witnesses. Notwithstanding any law 
24 validating electronic or digital signatures, signatures of the principal and witnesses must 
25 be made in person and not by electronic means. The power remains in effect 
26 notwithstanding the principal's later incapacity and may include individual instluctions. 
27 Unless related to the principal by blood, marriage or adoption, an agent may not be an 
28 owner, operator or employee of a residential long-term health care institution at which the 
29 principal is receiving care. 
30 3. Effective upon determination that principal lacks capacity. Unless otherwise 
31 specified in a power of attorney for health care, the authority of an agent becomes 
32 effective only upon a determination that the principal lacks capacity and ceases to be 
33 effective upon a detennination that the principal has recovered capacity. 
34 4. Determination. Unless otherwise specified in a written advance health care 
35 directive, a determination that an individual lacks or has recovered capacity or that 
36 another condition exists that affects an individual instruction, the authority of an agent or 
37 the validity of an advance health care directive must be made by the primary physician, 
38 by a court of competent jurisdiction or, for an individual who has included a directive 
39 authorizing mental health treatment in an advance health care directive, by a person 
40 qualified to conduct an examination pursuant to Title 34-B, section 3863. 
41 5. Decision in accordance with instructions, wishes, best interest. An agent shall 
42 make a health care decision in accordance with the principal's individual instructions, if 
43 any, and other wishes to the extent known to the agent. Otherwise, the agent shall make

the decision in accordance with the agent's determination of the principal's best interest. 
In determining the principal's best interest, the agent shall consider the principal's 
personal values to the extent known to the agent. 
6. Effective without judicial approval. A health care decision made by an agent 
for a principal is effective without judicial approval. 
7. Nomination of guardian. A written advance health care directive may include 
the individlial's nomination.of a guardian of the person. 
8. Validity of advance health care directive. An advance health care directive is 
valid for purposes of this Part if it complies with this Part, regardless of when or where 
executed or communicated, or if it is valid under the laws of the state in which it was 
executed. An advance health care directive that is valid where executed or communicated 
is valid for the purposes of this Part. 
9. Directing mental health treatment. An advance health care directive is valid for 
purposes of directing mental health treatment. The terms of the directive must be 
construed in accordance with this Part and Title 34-B, sections 3831 and 3862. 
10. Personal representative for purposes of federal law. A sun·ogate or an agent 
named in an advance health care directive has the power and authority to serve as the 
personal representative of the patient who executed the health care directive for all 
purposes of the federal Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996, 42 
United States Code, Section 1320d et seg. and its regulations, 45 Code of Federal 
Regulations, Parts 160-164. The surrogate or agent has all the rights of the patient with 
respect to the use and disclosure of the individually identifiable health info1mation and 
other medical records of the patient. 
§5-804. Revocation of advance health care directive 
1. Revocation of designation of agent. An individual with capacity may revoke the 
designation of an agent only by a signed writing or by personally informing the 
supervising health care provider. 
2. Revocation of advance health care directive. An individual with capacity may 
revoke all or part of an advance health care directive, other than the designation of an 
agent, at any time and in any manner that communicates an intent to revoke. 
3. Communication of revocation. A health care provider, agent,· guardian or 
surrogate who is informed of a revocation by an individual with capacity shall promptly 
communicate the fact of the revocation to the supervising health care provider and to any 
health care institution at which the patient is receiving care. 
4. Revocation of spouse as agent. A decree of annulment, divorce, dissolution of 
marriage or legal separation revokes a previous designation of a spouse as agent unless 
otherwise specified in the decree or in a power of attorney for health care. 
5. Revocation of earlier advance health care directive in conflict. An advance 
health care directive that conflicts with an earlier advance health care directive revokes 
the earlier directive to the extent of the conflict.

COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A "to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
r §5-805. Optional form 
2 The following form may, but need not, be used to create an advance health care 
3 directive. The other sections of this Part govern the effect of this or any other writing 
4 used to create an advance health care directive. An individual with capacity may 
5 complete or modify all or any part of the following form. 
6 ADVANCE HEALTH CARE DIRECTIVE 
7 Explanation 
8 You have the right to give instructions about your own health care. You also have 
9 the right to name someone else to make health care decisions for you. This form lets you 
10 do either or both of these things. It also lets you express your wishes regarding donation 
11 of organs and the designation of your primary physician. If you use this form, you may 
12 complete or modify all or any part of it. You are free to use a different form. 
13 Part 1 of this form is a power of attorney for health care. Part 1 lets you name 
14 another individual as agent to make health care decisions for you if you become incapable 
15 of making your own decisions or if you want someone else to make those decisions for 
16 you now even though you are still capable. You may also name an alternate agent to act 
17 for you if your first choice is not willing, able or reasonably available to make decisions 
18 for you. Unless related to you, your agent may not be an owner, operato1· or employee of 
19 a residential long-term health care institution at which you are receiving care. 
20 Unless the form you sign limits the authority of your agent, your agent may make all 
21 health care decisions for you. This form has a place for you to limit the authority of your 
22 agent. You need not limit the authority of your agent if you wish to rely on your agent 
23 for all health care decisions that may have to be made. If you choose not to limit the 
24 authority of your agent, your agent will have the right to: 
25 (1) Consent or refuse consent to any care, treatment, service or procedure to 
26 maintain, diagnose or otherwise affect a physical or mental condition; 
27 (2) Select or discharge health care providers and institutions; 
28 (3) Approve or disapprove diagnostic tests, surgical procedures, programs of 
29 medication and orders not to resuscitate; and 
30 (4) Direct the provision, withholding or withdrawal of aiiificial nutrition and 
31 hydration and all other forms of health care, including life-sustaining treatment. 
32 Part 2 of this form lets you give specific instructions about any aspect of your health 
33 care. Choices are provided for you to express your wishes regarding the provision, 
34 withholding or withdrawal of treatment to keep you alive, including the provision of 
35 artificial nutrition and hydration, as well as the provision of pain relief. Space is also 
3 6 provided for you to add to the choices you have made or for you to write out any 
37 additional wishes. 
38 Part 3 of this form lets you express an intention to donate your bodily organs and 
39 tissues following your death.

After completing this form, sign and date the form at the end. You must have 2 other 
individuals sign as witnesses. Give a copy of the signed and completed form to your 
physician, to any other health care providers you may have, to any health care institution 
at which you are receiving care and to any health care agents you have named. You 
should talk to the person you have named as agent to make sure that he or she 
understands your wishes and is willing to take the responsibility. 
You have the right to revoke this advance health care directive or replace this form at 
any time.

14 §5-806. Decisions by surrogate 
15 1. Decisions by surrogate. A surrogate may make a decision to withhold or 
16 withdraw life-sustaining treatment for a patient who is an adult or emancipated minor if 
17 the patient has been determined by the primary physician to lack capacity, no agent or 
18 guardian has been appointed or the agent or guardian is not reasonably available and the 
19 patient is in a terminal condition or a persistent vegetative state as determined by the 
20 primary physician. 
21 A surrogate also is authorized to make any other health care decision for a'patient who is 
22 an adult or emancipated minor if the patient has been determined by the primary 
23 physician to lack capacity and no agent or guardian exists. except that a surrogate may 
24 not deny surgery, procedures or other interventions that are lifesaving and medically 
25 necessary. 
26 A medically necessary procedure is one providing the most patient-appropriate 
27 intervention or procedure that can be safely and effectively given. 
28 2. Priority of who may act as surrogate. Any member of the following classes of 
29 the patient's family who is reasonably available, in descending order of priority, may act 
30 as surrogate: 
31 A. The spouse, unless legally separated; 
32 B. An adult who shares an emotional, physical and financial relationship with the 
33 patient similar to that of a spouse; 
34 C. An adult child; 
Page 113 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
CO:MMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 D. A parent; 
2 E. An adult brother or sister; 
3 F. An adult grandchild; 
4 G. An adult niece or nephew. related by blood or adoption; 
5 H. An adult aunt or uncle, related by blood or adoption; or 
6 I. Any adult relative of the patient. related by blood or adoption, who is familiar with 
7 the patient's personal values and is reasonably available for consultation. 
8 3. Adult who has exhibited special concern. If none of the individuals eligible to 
9 act as surrogate under subsection 2 is reasonably available, an adult who has exhibited 
1 O special concern for the patient. who is familiar with the patient's personal values and who 
11 is reasonably available may act as surrogate. 
12 4. Communication of assumption of authority. A surrogate shall communicate the 
13 surrogate's assumption of authority as promptly as practicable to the members of the 
14 patient's family specified in subsection 2 who can be readily contacted. 
15 5. Conflict among potential surrogates; neutral 3rd party or court. If more than 
16 one member of a class assumes authority to act as surrogate and they, or members of 
17 different classes who are reasonably available, do not agree on a health care decision and 
18 the supervising health care provider is so informed, the supervising health care provider 
19 may comply with the decision of the class having priority or a majority of the members of 
20 that class who have communicated their views to the provider. The health care provider 
21 may refer the members of the class or classes to a neutral 3rd party for assistance in 
22 resolving the dispute or to a court of competent jurisdiction. If the class is evenly divided 
23 concerning the health care decision and the supervising health care provider is so 
24 info1med, that class and all individuals having lower priority are disqualified from 
25 making the decision. 
26 6. Decision in accordance with instructions, wishes, best interest. A surrogate 
27 shall make a health care decision in accordance with the patient's individual instiuctions, 
28 if any, and other wishes to the extent known to the surrogate. Otherwise, the surrogate 
29 shall make the decision in accordance with the surrogate's dete1mination of the patient's 
30 best interest and in good faith. In determining the patient's best interest, the surrogate 
31 shall consider the patient's personal values to the extent known to the surrogate. A 
3 2 consent is not valid if it conflicts with the intention of the patient previously expressed to 
33 the surrogate. 
34 7. Effective without judicial approval. A health care decision made by a surrogate 
35 for a patient lacldng capacity is effective without judicial approval. 
36 8. Disqualification. An individual with capacity at any time may disqualify another, 
37 including a member of the individual's family. from acting as the individual's surrogate 
38 by a sigped writing or by personally informing the supervising health care provider of the 
39 disqualification. 
40 9. Conflict of interest. A surrogate may not be an owner, operator or employee of a 
41 residential long-term health care institution at which the patient is receiving care unless 
42 the surrogate is one of the following:

A. The spouse of the patient; 
B. An adult child gfthe patient; 
C. A parent of the patient; or 
D. A relative of the patient with whom the patient has resided for more than 6 
months prior to the decision. 
10. Written declaration supporting authority. A supervising health care provider 
may require an individual claiming the right to act as surrogate for a patient to provide a 
written declaration under penalty of perjury stating facts and circumstances reasonably 
sufficient to establish the claimed authority. 
10 §5-807. Decisions by guardian 
11 1. Compliance with expressed wishes; cannot revoke advance health care 
12 directive. Except as authorized by a court of competent jurisdiction, a gµardian shall 
13 comply with the individual subject to guardianship's individual instructions and other 
14 wishes, if any, expressed while the individual subject to guardianship had capacity and to 
15 the extent !mown to the guardian and may not revoke the individual subject to 
16 guardianship's advance health care directive unless the appointing court expressly so 
17 authorizes. 
18 2. Agent's decision takes precedence. Absent a court order to the contrary, a health 
19 care decision of an agent takes precedence over that of a guardian. 
20 3. Effective without judicial approval; exceptions. A health care decision made 
21 by a guardian for the individual subject to guardianship is effective without judicial 
22 approval, except under the following circumstances: 
23 A. The guardian's decision is contrary to the individual subject to guardianship's 
24 individual instructions and other wishes, expressed while the individual subject to 
25 guardianship had capacity; or 
26 B. The guardian seeks to withhold or withdraw life-sustaining treatment from the 
27 individual subject to guardianship, against the advice of the individual subject to 
28 guardianship's primary physician and in the absence of instmctions from the 
29 individual subject to guardianship, made while the individual subject to gµardianship 
30 had capacity. 
31 §5-808. Obligations of health care provider 
32 1. Communicate to patient. Before implementing a health care decision made for a 
33 patient, a supervising health care provider, if possible, shall promptly communicate to the 
34 patient the decision made and the identity of the person making the decision. 
35 2. Include in record advance health care directive, surrogate, revocation, 
36 disqualification. A supervising health care provider who lmows of the existence of an 
3 7 advance health care directive, a revocation of an advance health care directive or a 
3 8 designation or disqualification of a surrogate shall promptly record its existence in the 
39 patient's health care record and, if it is in writing, shall request a copy and if one is 
40 furnished shall an·ange for its maintenance in the health care record. 
Page 115 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT "A "to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
l 3. Include in record determinations on capacity; communicate. A primary 
2 physician who makes or is informed of a determination that a patient lacks or has 
3 recovered capacity or that another condition exists that affects an individual instruction or 
4 the authority of an agent, guardian or surrogate or the validity of an advance health care 
5 directive shall promptly record the determination in the patient's health care record and 
6 communicate the determination to the patient, if possible, and to any person then 
7 authorized to make health care decisions for the patient. 
8 4. CompUance. Except as provided in subsections 5 and 6, a health care provider or 
9 health care institution providing care to a patient shall: 
10 A. Comply with an individual instruction of the patient and with a reasonable 
11 interpretation of that instruction made by a person then authorized to make health 
12 care decisions for the patient; and 
13 B. Comply with a health care decision for the patient made by a person then 
14 authorized to make health care decisions for the patient to the same extent as if the 
15 decision had been made by the patient while having capacity. 
16 5. Decline to comply; not in compliance; reasons of conscience; contrary to 
17 policy. A health care provider may decline to comply with an individual instruction or 
18 health care decision if the instruction or decision appears not to be in compliance with 
19 this Part or for reasons of conscience. A health care institution may decline to comply 
20 with an individual instruction or health care decision if the instruction or decision appears 
21 not to be in compliance with this Part or if the instruction or decision is contr·ary to a 
22 policy of the institution that is expressly based on reasons of conscience and the policy 
23 was timely communicated to the patient or to a person then authorized to make health 
24 care decisions for the patient. 
25 6. Decline to comply; ineffective health care; contrary to generally accepted 
26 standards. A health care provider or health care institution may decline to comply with 
27 an individual instruction or health care decision that requires medically ineffective health 
28 care or health care contrary to generally accepted health care standards applicable to the 
29 health care provider or institution. 
30 7. Duties if decline to comply. A health care provider or health care institution that 
31 declines to comply with an individual instruction or health care decision shall: 
32 A. Promptly so inform the patient, if possible, and any person then authorized to 
33 make health care decisions for the patient; 
34 B. Provide continuing care to the patient until a transfer can be effected or a comi of 
3 5 competent jurisdiction issues a final order regarding the decision; and 
36 C. Unless the patient or person then authorized to make health care decisions for the 
3 7 patient refuses assistance, immediately make all reasonable effmis to assist in the 
38 transfer of the patient to another health care provider or institution that is willing to 
39 comply with the instruction or decision. 
40 8. Not as a condition for providing health care. A health care provider or health 
41 care institution may not require or prohibit the execution or revocation of an advance 
42 health care directive as a condition for providing health care.

1 §5-809. Health care information 
2 Unless otherwise specified in an advance health care directive, a person then 
3 authorized to make health care decisions for a patient has the same rights as the patient to 
4 request, receive, examine, copy and consent to the disclosure of medical or any other 
5 health care information. 
6 §5-810. Immunities 
7 1. Health care provider or institution. A health care provider or health care 
8 institution acting in good faith and in accordance with generally accepted health care 
9 standards applicable to the health care provider or health care institution is not subject to 
10 civil or criminal liability or to discipline for unprofessional conduct for: 
11 A. Complying with a health care decision of a person apparently having authority 
12 and capacity to make a health care decision for a patient, including a decision to 
13 withhold or withdraw health care; 
14 B. Declining to comply with a health care decision of a person based on a belief that 
15 the person then lacked authority or capacity or that the decision otherwise does not 
16 comply with this Part; 
17 C. Complying with an advance health care directive and assuming that the directive 
18 was valid when made and has not been revoked or terminated; or 
19 D. Seeking judicial relief from a court of competent jurisdiction. 
20 2. Agent, guardian or surrogate. An individual acting as agent, guardian or 
21 surrogate under this Part is not subject to civil or criminal liability or to discipline for 
22 unprofessional conduct for health care decisions made in good faith. 
23 §5-811. Statutory damages 
24 1. Health care provider or institution; intentional violation. A health care 
25 provider or health care institution that intentionally violates this Part is subject to liability 
26 to the aggrieved individual for damages of $500 or actual damages resulting from the 
27 violation, whichever is greater, plus reasonable attorney's fees. 
28 2. Interference with autonomy to make health care decisions. A person who 
29 intentionally falsifies, forges, conceals, defaces or obliterates an individual's advance 
30 health care directive or a revocation of an advance health care directive without the 
31 individual's consent, or who coerces or fraudulently induces an individual to give, revoke 
32 or not to give an advance health care directive, is subject to liability to that individual for 
33 damages of $2,500 or actual damages resulting from the action, whichever is greater, plus 
34 reasonable attorney's fees. 
35 §5-812. Capacity 
36 1. Right to make health care decisions while having capacity. This Part does not 
3 7 affect the right of an individual to make health care decisions while having capacity to do 
38 so. 
39 2. Presumed to have capacity; rebuttal. An individual is presumed to have 
40 capacity to make a health care decision, to give or revoke an advance health care directive 
Page 117 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT" A" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 and to designate or disqualify a surrogate. This presumption may be rebutted by a 
2 determination by the individual's primary physician or by a court of competent 
3 jurisdiction. 
4 §5-813. Effect of copy 
5 A copy of a written advance health care directive, revocation of an advance health 
6 care directive or designation or disqualification of a surrogate has the same effect as the 
7 original. 
8 §5-814. Effect of Part 
9 1. No presumption concerning intention if no advance health care directive or if 
10 revoked. This Part does not create a presumption concerning the intention of an 
11 individual who has not made or who has revoked an advance health care directive. 
12 2. Death resulting from withholding or withdrawing health care. Death resulting 
13 from the withholding or withdrawal of health care in accordance with this Part does not 
14 for any pm-pose constitute a suicide or homicide or legally impair or invalidate a policy of 
15 insurance or an annuity providing a death benefit, notwithstanding any term of the policy 
16 or annuity to the contrary. 
17 3. Prohibited by other statutes. This Pait does not authorize mercy killing, assisted 
18 suicide, euthanasia or the provision, withholding or withdrawal of health care to the 
19 extent prohibited by other statutes of this State. 
20 4. Health care contrary to generally accepted health care standards. This Part 
21 does not authorize or require a health care provider or health care institution to provide 
22 health care contra1y to generally accepted health care standards applicable to the health 
23 care provider or health care institution. 
24 5. Admission to a mental health institution. This Part does not authorize an agent 
25 or surrogate to consent to the admission of an individual to a mental health institution 
26 unless the individual's written advance health care directive expressly so provides. 
27 6. Other statutes governing treatment for mental illness. This Part does not 
28 affect other statutes of this State governing treatment for mental illness of an individual 
29 involuntarily committed to a mental health institution. 
30 §5-815. Judicial relief 
31 On petition of a patient, the patient's agent, guardian or surrogate, a health care or 
32 social services provider or health care institution involved with the patient's care, a state 
33 agency mandated to provide adult protective services pursuant to Title 22, chapter 958-A, 
34 or an adult relative or adult friend of the patient, the court may enjoin or direct a health 
35 care decision or other equitable relief. 
36 §5-816. Uniformity of application and construction 
37 This Part must be applied and construed to effectuate its general purpose to make 
38 unif01m the law with respect to the subject matter of this Part among states enacting it.

§5-817. Military advanced medical directives 
A military advanced medical directive executed in accordance with 10 United States 
Code, Section 1044c is valid in this State. 
PART9 
MAINE UNIFORM POWER OF ATTORNEY ACT 
SUBPART1 
GENERAL PROVISIONS AND DEFINITIONS 
§5-901. Short title 
This Part may be known and cited as "the Maine Uniform Power of Attorney Act." 
§5-902. Definitions 
As used in this Part. unless the context otherwise indicates, the following terms have 
the following meanings. 
1. Agent. "Agent" means a person granted authority to act for a principal under a 
power of attorney, whether denominated an agent, attorney-in-fact or otherwise. "Agent" 
includes an original agent, coagent, successor agent and a person to whom an agent's 
authority is delegated. 
2. Durable. "Durable," with respect to a power of attorney, means not terminated by 
the principal's incapacity. 
3. Electronic. "Electronic" means relating to technology having electrical, digital, 
magnetic. wireless, optical, electromagnetic or similar capabilities. 
4. Good faith. "Good faith" means honesty in fact. 
5. Incapacity. "Incapacity" means inability of an individual to effectively manage 
property or business affairs because the individual: 
A. Is impaired by reason of mental illness, mental deficiency, physical illness or 
disability, chronic use of chugs, chronic intoxication or other cause to the extent that 
the individual lacks sufficient understanding, capacity or ability to receive and 
evaluate info1mation or make or communicate decisions regarding the individual's 
property or business affairs; or 
B. Is: 
(1) Missing: 
(2) Detained, including incarcerated in a penal system; or 
(3) Outside the United States and unable to return. 
6. Person. · "Person" means an individual, corporation, business trust, estate, trust, 
partnership, limited liability company,. association, joint venture, public corporation, 
government or governmental subdivision, agency or instrumentality or any other legal or 
commercial entity. 
Page 119 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT"~" to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 7. Power of attorney. "Power of attorney" means a writing or other record that 
2 grants authority to an agent to act in the place of the principal, whether or not the term 
3 "power of attorney" is used. 
4 8. Presently exercisable general power of appointment. "Presently exercisable 
5 general power of appointment," with respect to property or a property interest subject to a 
6 power of appointment, means power exercisable at the time in question to vest absolute 
7 ownership in the principal individually, the principal1s estate, the ptincipal1s creditors or 
8 the creditors of the principal's estate. "Presently exercisable general power of 
9 appointment" includes a power of appointment not exercisable until the occurrence of a 
10 specified event, the satisfaction of an ascertainable standard or the passage of a specified 
11 period only after the occurrence of the specified event, the satisfaction of the 
12 ascertainable standard or the passage of the specified period. "Presently exercisable 
13 general power of appointment" does not include a power exercisable in a fiduciary 
14 capacity or only by will. 
15 9. Principal. "Principal" means an individual who grants authority to an agent in a 
16 power of attorney. 
17 10. Property. "Property" means anything that may be the subject of ownership, 
18 whether real or personal or legal or equitable, or any interest or right therein. 
19 11. Sign. 11Sign11 means, with present intent to authenticate or adopt a record: 
20 A. To execute or adopt a tangible symbol; or 
21 B. To attach to or logically associate with the record an electronic sound, symbol or 
22 process. 
23 12. Stocks and bonds. "Stocks and bonds" means stocks, bonds, mutual funds and 
24 all other types of securities and financial instmments, whether held directly, indirectly or 
25 in any other manner. "Stocks and bonds" does not include commodity futures contracts 
26 and call or put options on stocks or stock indexes. 
27 §5-903. Applicability 
28 This Part applies to all powers of attorney except: 
29 1. Coupled with an interest in the subject of the power. A power to the extent it 
30 is coupled with an interest in the subject of the power, including a power given to or for 
31 the benefit of a creditor in connection with a credit transaction; 
32 2. Health care decisions. A power to make health care decisions; 
33 3. Proxy or other delegation to exercise rights. A proxy or other delegation to 
34 exercise voting rights or management rights with respect to an entity; and 
35 4. Governmental purpose. A power created on a form prescribed by a government 
36 or governmental subdivision, agency or instmmentality for a governmental purpose. 
37 §5-904. Power of attorney is durable 
38 A power of attorney created tmder this Part is durable lilllcss it expressly provides 
39 that it is terminated by the incapacity of the principal. 
Page 120 -128LR0452(02)-1 
COMMITTEE AMENDMENT 
COMMITTEEAMENDMENT"A "to H.P. 91, L.D. 123 
1 ,, §5-905. Execution of power of attorney; notices 
) · 2 1. Signed by principal; acknowledged. A power of attorney must be signed by the 
3 principal or in the principal's conscious presence by another individual directed by the 
4 principal to sign the principal's name on the power of attorney. A signature on a power of 
5 attorney is presumed to be genuine if the principal acknowledges the signature before a 
6 notary public or other individual authorized by law to take acknowledgments. A power 
7 of attorney under this Part is not valid unless it is acknowledged before a notary public or 
8 other individual authorized by law to take acknowledgments. 
9 2. Notices for durable power of attorney. A durable power of attorney under this 
10 Part is not valid unless it contains the following notices substantially in the following 
11 form: 
12 "Notice to the Principal: As the "Principal" you are using this power of attorney to grant 
13 power to another person (called the Agent) to make decisions about your property and to 
14 use your property on your behalf. Under this power of attorney you give your Agent 
15 broad and sweeping powers to sell or otherwise dispose of your property without notice 
16 to you. Under this document your Agent will continue to have these powers after you 
17 become incapacitated. The powers that you give your Agent are explained more fully in 
18 the Maine Uniform Power of Attorney Act. Maine Revised Statutes, Title 18-C, Article 5, 
19 Part 9. You have the right to revoke this power of attorney at any time as long as you are 
20 not incapacitated. If there is anything about this power of attorney that you do not 
21 understand, you should ask an attorney to explain it to you. 
22 Notice to the Agent: As the "Agent" you are given power under this power of attorney to 
23 make decisions about the property belonging to the Principal and to dispose of the 
24 Principal's property on the Principal's behalf in accordance with the terms of this power 
25 of attorney. This power of attorney is valid only if the Principal is of sound mind when 
26 the Principal signs it. When you accept the authority granted under this power of 
27 attorney. a special legal relationship is created between you and the Principal. This 
28 relationship imposes upon you legal duties that continue until you resign or the power of 
29 attorney is terminated or revoked. The duties are more fully explained in the Maine 
30 Uniform Power of Attorney Act. Maine Revised Statutes, Title 18-C. Article 5. Part 9 and 
31 Title 18-B, sections 802 to 807 and Title 18-B, chapter 9. As the Agent, you are 
32 generally not entitled to use the Principal's property for your own benefit or to make gifts 
33 to yourself or others unless the power of attorney gives you such authority. If you violate 
34 your duty under this power of attorney, you may be liable for damages and may be 
35 subject to criminal prosecution. You must stop acting on behalf of the Principal if you 
36 learn of any event that terminates this power of attorney or your authority under this 
37 power of attorney. Events of termination are more fully explained in the Maine Uniform 
38 Power of Attorney Act and include, but are not limited to, revocation of your authority or 
39 of the power of attorney by the Principal, the death of the Principal or the commencement 
40 of divorce proceedings between you and the Principal. If there is anything about this 
41 power of attorney or your duties under it that you do not understand, you should ask an 
4 2 attorney to explain it to you."

1 §5-906. Validity of power of attorney 
2 1. Executed on or after July 1, 2019. A power of attorney executed in this State on 
3 or after July 1, 2019 is valid if its execution complies with section 5-905. 
4 2. Executed on or after July 1, 2010 but before July 1, 2019. A power of attorney 
5 executed on or after July 1, 2010 but before July 1, 2019 is valid if its execution complied 
6 with former Title 18-A, section 5-906. 
7 3. Executed before July 1, 2010. A power of attorney executed in this State before 
8 July 1, 2010 is valid if its execution complied with the law of this State as it existed at the 
9 time of execution. 
10 4. Executed other than in this State. A power of attorney executed other than in 
11 this State is valid in this State if, when the power of attorney was executed, the execution 
12 complied with: 
13 A. The law of the jurisdiction that determines the meaning and effect of the power of 
14 attorney pursuant to section 5-907; or 
15 B. The requirements for a military power of attorney pursuant to 10 United States 
16 Code, Section 1044b, as amended. 
17 5. Defective notice. A power of attorney executed in this State is valid and 
18 enforceable 2 years after execution if the notice required by section 5-905, subsection 2 is 
19 included but is incomplete or defective in any respect. 
20 6. Copy. Except as otherwise provided by statute other than this Part, a photocopy 
21 or electronically transmitted copy of an original power of attorney has the same effect as 
22 the original. 
23 §5-907. Meaning and effect of power of attomey 
24 The meaning and effect of a power of attorney are determined by the law of the 
25 jurisdiction indicated in the power of attorney and, in the absence of an indication of 
26 jurisdiction, by the law of the jurisdiction in which the power of attorney was executed. 
27 §5-908. Nomination of conservator or guardian; relation of agent to court-
28 appointed fiduciary 
29 1. Nomination of conservator or guardian. In a power of attorney, a principal may 
30 nominate a conservator of the principal's estate or guardian of the principal's person for 
31 consideration by the court if protective proceedings for the principal1s estate or person are 
32 begun after the principal executes the power of attorney. Except for good cause shown or 
33 disqualification, the comt shall make its appointment in accordance with the principal's 
34 most recent nomination. 
35 2. Relation of agent to court-appointed fiduciary. If, after a principal executes a 
36 power of attorney, a cou1t appoints a conservator of the principal's estate or other 
37 fiduciary charged with the management of some or all of the principal's property, the 
3 8 agent is accountable to the fiduciaty as well as to the principal. The power of attorney is 
39 not terminated and the agent's authority continues unless limited, suspended or terminated 
40 by the coutt.
